The Effect of Riba on Testimony: Notoriety and Legal Proof
Commentary on ruling that eating riba makes testimony rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rejecting testimony of one who eats riba and explain the condition of notoriety (shuhra) and its rationale.

Core Idea
Eating riba disqualifies testimony, but the Hanafi school requires notoriety — mere suspicion does not suffice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key condition in witness disqualification. While riba is a major sin, the school distinguishes between proven fisq and mere accusation. The commentator explains why notoriety is needed and how it differs from consuming orphan's property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Eating riba is prohibited and classified as a major sin (kabira), which constitutes fisq (immorality) and thus disqualifies a witness.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 2:275 is cited: 'Those who eat riba'. The commentator explains that 'eating' metaphorically means 'taking' the excess.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding the specific ruling on testimony.
3
Identify the condition in Zahir al-Riwayah
Imam Muhammad in al-Asl restricted the ruling: testimony is rejected only if the person is well-known (mashhuran bihi) for eating riba.
The author of al-Kanz did not mention this condition, but the commentator corrects it.
4
Analyze the rationale for notoriety
Al-Hidayah explains that most people engage in some form of invalid contracts, so without notoriety, it is likely just an accusation. Notoriety separates persistent sin from a rare slip.
This aligns with the restriction for wine drinking, where addiction is required.
5
Compare with orphan's property
Eating orphan's property requires no notoriety; testimony is rejected immediately. The commentator argues that both ultimately require proof to the judge, so the difference is only in the method of proof.
Al-Zayla'i distinguished by ownership: orphan's property never enters ownership, while riba does temporarily, but the commentator finds this unhelpful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو يأكل الربا لأنه من الكبائر أي يأخذ القدر الزائد فالمراد بالأكل الأخذ وإنما ذكره تبعاً للآية {الذين يأكلون الربا} [البقرة: 275] وإنما ذكره في الآية لأنه معظم منافع المال ولأن الربا شائع في المطعومات، والمراد بالربا بالقدر الزائد لا الزيادة وهي المرادة في قوله تعالى {وحرم الربا} [البقرة: 275] كما بيناه في بابه. وأطلقه المؤلف تبعاً لكثير، وقيده في الأصل بأن يكون مشهوراً به، وعلله في الهداية بأن الإنسان قل ما ينجو عن مباشرات العقود الفاسدة وكل ذلك ربا ا هـ . وهو أولى مما قيل لأن الربا ليس بحرام محض لأنه يفيد الملك بالقبض كسائر البياعات الفاسدة وإن كان غاصباً مع ذلك فكان ناقصاً في
كونه كبيرة بخلاف أكل مال اليتيم ترد شهادته بمرة والأوجه ما قيل لأنه إن لم يشتهر به كان الواقع ليس إلا تهمة أكل الربا ولا تسقط العدالة به كما قدمناه في وجه تقييد شرب الخمر بالإدمان ولا يصح قوله إنه ليس بحرام محض بعد الاتفاق على أنه كبيرة والملك بالقبض شيء آخر، وأما أكل مال اليتيم فلم يقيده أحد وأنت تعلم أنه لا بد من الظهور للقاضي فلا فرق بين الربا ومال اليتيم. والحاصل أن الفسق نفسه مانع شرعاً من قبولها غير أن القاضي لا يرتكب ذلك إلا بعد ظهوره له فالكل سواء وفرق الزيلعي بينهما بأن أكل مال اليتيم لم يدخل تحت ملكه ومال الربا دخل فلا يفيد شيئاً كما لا يخفى
His saying: (Or eats riba) because it is among the major sins. That is, he takes the excess amount. The meaning of 'eating' is 'taking'. He mentioned it following the verse: 'Those who eat riba' (2:275). He mentioned it in the verse because it is the main benefit of wealth and because riba is common in foodstuffs. The intended meaning of riba is the excess amount, not the increase which is meant in His saying 'and Allah has forbidden riba' (2:275) as we explained in its chapter. The author (al-Kanz) released it unrestrictedly following many, but it was restricted in the original (of the school) that he must be well-known for it. The Hidayah explained it by saying that a person rarely escapes from engaging in invalid contracts, all of which are riba. That is more appropriate than what was said that riba is not purely haram because it gives ownership by taking possession like other invalid sales, and even if he is a usurper along with that, it is deficient in... Being a major sin unlike eating the property of an orphan: his testimony is rejected once. The most correct view is what was said: if he is not well-known for it, then what actually happened is only an accusation of eating riba, and it does not nullify integrity as we have presented in the restriction of drinking wine by addiction. And his statement that it is not purely haram is incorrect after the consensus that it is a major sin, and ownership by possession is something else. As for eating the property of an orphan, no one restricted it. And you know that it must become apparent to the judge, so there is no difference between riba and orphan's property. The conclusion is that fisq (immorality) itself is a legal impediment to accepting testimony, but the judge does not act upon it except after it becomes apparent to him, so all are equal. Al-Zayla'i distinguished between them: eating orphan's property does not enter into his ownership, while riba property does, so it does not benefit anything, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase 'or eats riba'. The author clarifies that 'eating' here metaphorically means 'taking' the excess amount. He cites the Quranic verse to show that it is a major sin. The author of al-Kanz left the ruling unrestricted, but Imam Muhammad in the original text (al-Asl) restricted it: testimony is only rejected if the person is well-known for committing riba. The Hidayah explains that most people engage in some form of invalid contracts, so without notoriety, it is likely just a suspicion. Then the text addresses an objection: some argued riba is not purely haram because ownership transfers by possession (qabd) in invalid sales, but the response is that it is still a major sin by consensus. A comparison is made with consuming orphan's property: for that, there is no requirement of notoriety; the testimony is rejected immediately. The best view is that since the judge can only act on what is apparent, both require evidence. Al-Zayla'i made a technical distinction: orphan's property never entered the taker's ownership (so it is pure usurpation), while riba property temporarily comes into ownership, but that does not affect the sin. The key rule: fisq itself is the impediment, but the judge needs proof.

Key Terms
الربا (al-riba): Usury or interest; specifically the excess (fadl) in a loan or exchange of certain commodities.
مشهوراً به (mashhuran bihi): Well-known for committing the act, i.e., notorious for it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, how does the condition of notoriety for riba compare to the rule for orphan's property?
A) The condition is unique to riba and does not apply to orphan's property.
B) Both require that the judge have knowledge of the fisq; notoriety is just one means of proof.
C) Orphan's property requires notoriety as well, but the texts differ.
D) The commentator says there is an irreconcilable difference.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires notoriety (shuhra) for rejecting testimony due to riba, because mere suspicion is insufficient; the judge must have concrete evidence of habitual sin, parallel to the rule for wine drinking.

Backgammon vs Chess: Conditions for Nullifying Witness Integrity
Commentary on gambling and its effect on witness integrity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when backgammon and chess nullify a witness's integrity, and list the five conditions that make chess fisq.

Core Idea
Backgammon always nullifies integrity; chess does so only if any of five conditions is met.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh: while backgammon automatically disqualifies a witness due to consensus on its prohibition, chess receives a nuanced treatment. The author explains that chess only nullifies integrity when accompanied by one of five specific conditions, reflecting the school's balanced approach between permissibility and safeguarding religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the two games
Identify the ruling for backgammon and chess as presented in the text. Backgammon is absolutely prohibited and nullifies integrity by consensus. Chess is not automatically fisq; it only nullifies integrity if one of five conditions is present.
This distinction is based on ijtihad and consensus (ijma) for backgammon.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Recognize that Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i (and a narration from Abu Yusuf) hold chess to be absolutely permissible (mubah) without any effect on integrity.
Their basis is that chess is a game of skill, not inherently linked to gambling or neglect.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing view
The Hanafi school accepts that chess is not inherently prohibited but argues that it can become a cause of sin (fisq) if it leads to five specific vices. This is why integrity is only lost conditionally.
The five conditions are derived from Fath al-Qadir and Siraj al-Wahhaj.
4
Enumerate the five conditions for chess
List the conditions from the text: 1) gambling (qimar), 2) missing prayer due to it, 3) frequent swearing/oaths about it, 4) playing on the road, 5) using abusive language related to it. If none are present, chess does not affect testimony.
These conditions are specified in Fath al-Qadir and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
5
Apply the ruling to a testimony scenario
Given a witness who plays chess, check for the five conditions. If any is found, the witness's testimony is rejected; otherwise it is accepted as if he never played. For backgammon, testimony is always rejected.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference between the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو يقامر بالنرد والشطرنج أو تفوته الصلاة بسببهما لأن كل ذلك من الكبائر وظاهر تقييده بما ذكر استواء النرد والشطرنج وليس كذلك فإن اللعب بالنرد مبطل للعدالة مطلقاً كما في العناية وغيرها للإجماع على حرمته بخلاف الشطرنج لأن للاجتهاد فيه مساغاً لقول مالك والشافعي بإباحته وهو مروي عن أبي يوسف كما في المجتبى من الحظر والإباحة، واختارها ابن الشحنة إذا كان لإحضار الذهن، واختار أبو زيد الحكيم حله؛ ذكره شمس الأئمة السرخسي كذا في المحيط البرهاني. وفي النوازل سئل أبو القاسم عمن ينظر إلى لاعبيه من غير لعب أيجوز؟ فقال : أخاف أن يصير فاسقاً ا هـ . وفيه إذا قامر به سقطت عدالته إجماعاً، وفي الميسر اسم لكل قمار والحاصل أن العدالة إنما تسقط بالشطرنج إذا وجد فيه واحد من خمس : القمار، وفوت الصلاة بسببه ، وإكثار الحلف عليه، واللعب به على الطريق كما في فتح القدير أو يذكر عليه فسقاً كما في السراج الوهاج وإلا فلا بخلاف النرد فإنه مسقط لها مطلقاً. والنرد كما في المصباح لعبة معروفة وهو معرب ا هـ. القاموس : إنه وضعه أردشير بن بابك ولهذا يقال النردشير ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير : ولعب الطاب في بلادنا مثله لأنه يرمى ويطرح بلا حساب وإعمال فكر وكلما كان كذلك مما أحدثه وعمله أهل الغفلة فهو حرام مطلقاً ا وأما الشطرنج فسنتكلم عليه وعلى واضعه في من الحظر والإباحة، وأما القمار فقدمنا أنه الميسر. وفي القاموس : قامره مقامرة وقماراً فقمره كنصره وتقمره راهنه فغلبه وهو التقامر ا هـ . وذكر النووي أنه مأخوذ من القمر لأن ماله تارة يزداد إذا غلب وينتقص إذا غلب كالقمر يزيد وينقص ا.هـ. وعلى هذا فلا بد في القمار من الرهان من الجانبين لتسقط العدالة كالسباق بالخيل والإقدام والدرس، وذكر في يتيمة الدهر من الحدود أن اللعب بالشطرنج من القمار وفي القاموس : الشطرنج ولا يفتح أوله لعبه والسين لغة فيه ا هـ
His saying: (Or gambles with backgammon and chess, or prayer passes him by because of them) because all of that is among the major sins. The apparent restriction of his mention indicates equality of backgammon and chess, but it is not so. Playing with backgammon nullifies integrity absolutely, as in al-‘Inayah and others, due to consensus on its prohibition. Unlike chess, because there is room for ijtihad about it, due to the statement of Malik and al-Shafi’i permitting it, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf in al-Mujtaba from the chapter of prohibition and permissibility. Ibn al-Shihnah chose it if it is for sharpening the mind, and Abu Zaid al-Hakim chose its permissibility; Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsi mentioned it in al-Muhit al-Burhani. In al-Nawazil, Abu al-Qasim was asked about one who watches the players without playing: is it permissible? He said: I fear he may become a sinner. And in it: if he gambles with it, his integrity is lost by consensus. Al-Maysir is a name for every form of gambling. The conclusion is that integrity is only lost by chess if one of five things is present: gambling, missing prayer because of it, frequent swearing by it, playing with it on the road as in Fath al-Qadir, or if abuse is mentioned about it as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj; otherwise no. Unlike backgammon, for it nullifies integrity absolutely. Backgammon, as in al-Misbah, is a well-known game, and it is an arabicized word. Al-Qamus: it was invented by Ardashir ibn Babak, hence it is called nardshir. In Fath al-Qadir: the game of tab in our lands is similar to it because it is thrown and cast without calculation and mental effort, and anything like that which is innovated and practiced by heedless people is absolutely haram. As for chess, we will speak about it and its inventor in the chapter of prohibition and permissibility. As for gambling, we have already mentioned that it is al-maysir. In al-Qamus: qamarahu muqamaratan and qimaran faqamarahu like nasarahu and taqamara: he wagered with him and defeated him, and that is al-taqamur. Al-Nawawi mentioned that it is derived from al-qamar (moon) because his wealth sometimes increases when he wins and decreases when he loses, like the moon increases and decreases. Based on this, gambling requires staking from both sides to nullify integrity, like horse racing, competitions, and lessons. In Yatimah al-Dahr from the chapters of Hudud, it is mentioned that playing chess is a form of gambling. In al-Qamus: al-shatranj, the first letter is not fathah; its game, and the sin is a language variant.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase regarding gambling with backgammon (نرد) and chess (شطرنج) and missing prayer due to them. The author first notes that the matn seems to treat both equally, but clarifies that they are different. Backgammon absolutely nullifies a witness's integrity due to consensus on its prohibition. Chess, however, is subject to ijtihad: Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i permit it, and a narration from Abu Yusuf also permits it. Some Hanafi scholars like Ibn al-Shihnah allow it for mental sharpening. Nevertheless, chess can still nullify integrity if one of five conditions is present: (1) gambling (staking money), (2) it causes missing prayer, (3) frequent swearing/oaths related to it, (4) playing it on the road (public immodesty), or (5) if it is associated with abusive language. Without these, chess does not automatically disqualify a witness. The text then defines backgammon, its origin, and equates games like الطاب (a dice game) to it. Gambling (قمار) essentially requires a stake from both sides to nullify testimony. The discussion ends with a note that some consider chess itself as gambling. The key distinction: backgammon always harms integrity; chess does so only conditionally, reflecting the Hanafi school's nuanced approach.

Key Terms
النرد (al-nard): Backgammon; a game played with dice and pieces.
الشطرنج (al-shatranj): Chess; a game of strategy.
الميسر (al-maysir): Gambling; any game that involves staking money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following does NOT automatically nullify a witness's integrity?
A) Playing backgammon (نرد).
B) Missing prayer due to playing chess.
C) Playing chess on the road.
D) Playing chess without any of the five conditions.

Key Takeaway
Backgammon always nullifies witness integrity by consensus; chess does so only if accompanied by any of five conditions: gambling, missing prayer, frequent oaths, playing on road, or abusive language.

Public Indecency and Witness Credibility
Commentary on matn ruling about public acts and testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that urinating or eating on the road in public view disqualifies a witness and explain the rationale based on the concept of muru'a.

Core Idea
Public shamelessness negates witness credibility.

In this lesson, we explore a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of public indecency on a person's eligibility to testify. The source passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, stating that urinating or eating on the road in public view is considered a violation of muru'a (manly dignity). Because such behavior indicates a lack of shame, the person is suspected of being willing to lie, and thus his testimony is rejected. We will analyze the conditions and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its consequence
The act is urinating or eating on the road. The consequence is rejection of the person's testimony. Determine that the ruling depends on the act being done in public view.
2
Understand the legal criterion: muru'a
Muru'a (manly dignity and modesty) is a prerequisite for 'adalah (upright character) in a witness. Publicly performing normally private acts shows a lack of shame, which undermines credibility.
The text explicitly says 'tārik li-l-murū'a' (abandoning manliness).
3
Recognize the rationale (ta'līl)
The reason given: if a person is not ashamed of such acts, he will not refrain from lying. This creates suspicion (tuhmah) about his truthfulness, leading to rejection of his testimony.
The argument is based on practical reasoning (ta'līl) rather than a direct textual proof.
4
Apply the condition of public visibility
The ruling only applies when the act occurs 'bi-marā min al-nās' (within sight of people). Private acts do not affect testimony. Also, the same applies to uncovering private parts for istinjā' in public.
The passage also analogizes playing chess on the road (discussed earlier) as similarly violating muru'a.
5
Distinguish between the act's inherent ruling and its impact on testimony
The act itself (urinating or eating) is not haram but rather makruh tanzīhī when done publicly. However, the impact on testimony is a separate matter: it disqualifies the witness due to tark al-murū'a.
The Hanafi position is that such behavior reduces the witness's moral standing, making him unreliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو يبول أو يأكل على الطريق لأنه تارك للمروءة وإذا كان لا يستحي عن مثل ذلك لا يمتنع عن الكذب فيتهم وقدمنا أن اللعب بالشطرنج على الطريق كذلك. والمراد بالأكل على الطريق والبول بأن يكون بمرأى من الناس ومثله الذي يكشف عورته ليستنجي
His saying: (Or urinates or eats on the road) because he is one who abandons manliness. And if he is not ashamed of such things, he will not refrain from lying, so he is suspected. And we have already mentioned that playing chess on the road is likewise. The intended meaning of eating and urinating on the road is that it be within sight of people, and similarly one who uncovers his private parts to cleanse himself.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase about urinating or eating on the road. The reason given is that such behavior shows a lack of muru'a (manly dignity and modesty). A person who does not feel shame about doing such acts in public is likely to lie, so his testimony becomes suspect. The commentator also analogizes playing chess on the road, which was discussed earlier, as also destroying muru'a. The key point is that the act must be done in public view ('bi-mara min al-nas'). Similarly, uncovering one's private parts for cleaning (istinja) in public is also considered a violation of muru'a. Thus, the ruling is not about the act itself (urination or eating) but about performing it publicly without shame, which undermines the witness's credibility.

Key Terms
المروءة (al-muru'a): Manly dignity, modesty, and social propriety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it shows lack of shame and leads to suspicion of lying.
C) Because it is impure.
D) Because it disturbs passersby.

Key Takeaway
Public shamelessness negates witness credibility in Hanafi law, as it indicates a character prone to lying.

Mura'a as a Condition for Testimony Acceptance
Defines mura'a and lists disqualifying acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions that violate mura'a and explain why they prevent testimony acceptance in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Lack of mura'a disqualifies a witness even if the act is not sinful.

Testimony requires 'adala (uprightness), which includes avoiding not only sins but also actions that undermine social decorum. This lesson explores the Hanafi concept of mura'a and its impact on the validity of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Define mura'a
Identify the definitions given: 'not doing what requires apology,' 'good bearing,' 'guarding the tongue,' and the definition of Muhammad: 'religion and righteousness.'
Note that definitions vary but all emphasize honorable conduct.
2
List actions that violate mura'a
From the text, compile examples: urinating/eating on the road, walking in only a sarawil, stretching legs before people, uncovering head improperly, wrestling elders in mosque, etc.
These are illustrative, not exhaustive.
3
Understand the legal effect
Even if the act is permissible (mubah), doing it forfeits 'adala and thus testimony is rejected. The doer is neither 'adil nor fasiq.
This nuance distinguishes mura'a from sin.
4
Distinguish from lowly professions
The text clarifies that lowly professions (e.g., canal-cleaner, weaver) do not automatically disqualify; the criterion is 'adala, not occupation.
Quote: 'Indeed the most noble of you is the most righteous.'
5
Note the role of persistence
Unlike minor sins where persistence is required, for mura'a-violating acts, a single occurrence can disqualify according to the author's speculation.
The author suggests persistence is not stipulated for mura'a.

المستحقرة مثل البول والأكل على الطريق، والمروءة أن لا يأتي الإنسان بما يعتذر منه مما يبخسه عن مرتبته عند أهل الفضل وقيل السمت الحسن وحفظ اللسان وتجنب السخف والمجون والارتفاع عن كل خلق دنيء والسخف رقة للعبد، وإن كان كاذباً فكذلك فعذره الخليفة زاد في فتح القدير بعده والذي عندي أن رد أبي يوسف شهادته ليس للكذبة لأن قول الحر للغير أنا عبدك إنما هو مجاز باعتبار معنى القيام بخدمتك وكوني تحت أمرك ممتثلاً له على إهانة نفسي في ذلك إلى آخره. وليس منها الصناعة الدنية كالقنواتي والزبال والحائك فإن الصحيح القبول إذا كان عدلاً، ومثله النخاسون والدلالون والعامة على قبول شهادة الأعرابي والقروي إذا كان عدلاً ا هـ. وقد ذكرنا في شرح المنار أن منها سرقة لقمة والإفراط في المزح المفضي إلى الاستخفاف وصحبة الأراذل والاستخفاف بالناس ولبس الفقيه قباء ولعب الحمام ا ثم اعلم أنهم شرطوا في الصغيرة الإدمان وما شرطوه في فعل ما يخل بالمروءة فيما رأيت، وينبغي اشتراطه بالأولى وإذا فعل ما يخل بها فقد سقطت عدالته وإن لم يكن فاسقاً به حيث كان مباحاً ففاعل المخل بها ليس بعدل ولا فاسق فالعدل من اجتنب الثلاثة والفاسق من فعل كبيرة أو أصر على صغيرة ولم أر من نبه عليه. وفي العتابية : لا تقبل شهادة من يعتاد الصياح في الأسواق . سب هـ. قوله : (وليس منها الصناعة الدنية الخ) قال الرملي : فتحرر أن العبرة للعدالة لا للحرفة وهذا الذي يجب أن يعول عليه ويفتى به فإنا نرى بعض أصحاب الحرف الدنية عنده من الدين والتقوى ما ليس عند كثير من أرباب الوجاهة وأصحاب المناصب وذوي المراتب وإن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم) [الحجرات: ١٣].
Book of Testimonies, Chapter: On whose testimony is accepted and whose not. From the side of blessing and the people present, and it has become frequent in our time; thus in Fath al-Qadir. The author indicated by what he mentioned that what violates manliness prevents acceptance even if not forbidden. Hence he said in al-Hidayah: The testimony of one who does contemptible acts such as urinating and eating on the road is not accepted. Manliness is that a person does not do something for which he would apologize, which lowers his rank among people of virtue. It is also said: good bearing, guarding the tongue, avoiding foolishness and frivolity, and rising above every base trait. Foolishness is weakness of intellect, from their saying 'thin cloth' if it is of little thread; thus in Fath al-Qadir and al-Mi'raj and in Ghayat al-Bayan from the chapter on Ta'zir. Muhammad said: In my view, manliness is religion and righteousness. Our teachers have mentioned things that violate manliness; we mention them: among them are the four mentioned things; among them are what is in Fath al-Qadir taken from al-Mi'raj: walking in only a sarawil, stretching one's leg before people, uncovering one's head in a place where it is considered light behavior, bad manners, lack of manliness and modesty; wrestling of an elder with youths in the mosque. Among that is the story that al-Fadl ibn al-Rabi' testified before Abu Yusuf, and he rejected his testimony. He complained to the caliph, and the caliph said: My minister is a religious man who does not bear false witness; why did you reject his testimony? He said: Because I heard him one day say to the caliph, 'I am your slave.' If he was truthful, then a slave's testimony is not accepted; if he was lying, then likewise. So the caliph accepted his excuse. Added in Fath al-Qadir after it: In my view, Abu Yusuf's rejection of his testimony was not due to the lie, because a free man's saying 'I am your slave' is merely a metaphor based on the meaning of serving you and being under your command, humiliating myself in that, etc. Not from that category are lowly professions like the canal-cleaner, the garbage collector, and the weaver, for the correct view is acceptance if they are upright. Likewise the horse-traders and brokers; the general principle is acceptance of testimony of the Bedouin and the villager if they are upright. We have mentioned in Sharh al-Manar that among them are stealing a morsel, excessive joking that leads to disrespect, keeping company with the lowly, showing disrespect to people, a faqih wearing a cloak, and playing with pigeons. Then know that they have stipulated persistence in minor sins, but regarding acts that violate manliness, I have not seen them stipulating that; it is more appropriate to stipulate it. If one does an act that violates manliness, his uprightness is forfeited even if he is not sinful, when the act is permissible. So the doer of that which violates manliness is neither upright nor sinful. The upright person is one who avoids the three (major sins, persistence in minor, and violating manliness?), and the sinful is one who commits a major sin or persists in a minor sin. I have not seen anyone draw attention to this. In al-Utabiyyah: The testimony of one who habitually shouts in the markets is not accepted. His statement: (And not from that are lowly professions...) al-Ramli said: It is established that the criterion is uprightness, not the profession, and this is what must be relied upon and given as fatwa. For indeed we see some practitioners of lowly professions having more religion and piety than many of those with status, positions, and ranks, and 'Indeed the most noble of you in the sight of Allah is the most righteous' [49:13].
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the concept of mura'a (manliness/decorum) as a condition for the acceptance of testimony. The author explains that actions which violate mura'a, even if not sinful, can prevent testimony from being accepted. Examples include urinating or eating on the road, walking in only a sarawil, stretching one's legs before people, uncovering one's head where it is considered improper, and wrestling with youths in the mosque. The story of al-Fadl ibn al-Rabi' illustrates that Abu Yusuf rejected his testimony because he had said to the caliph 'I am your slave,' which could be interpreted as a lie or as a metaphor indicating servitude. The commentary clarifies that the rejection was not due to the lie but because such a statement implies self-humiliation for worldly gain. Importantly, the passage emphasizes that lowly professions (e.g., canal-cleaner, garbage collector) do not automatically disqualify a witness; uprightness ('adala) is the criterion. The commentary from al-Ramli reinforces that the verse 'the most noble of you is the most righteous' supports this principle. The passage also notes that habitual shouting in markets violates mura'a. The author distinguishes between major sins, persistence in minor sins, and acts that violate mura'a, stating that committing the latter forfeits 'adala even if the act is not sinful, but the doer is not considered a fasiq. This is a nuanced Hanafi position.

Key Terms
المروءة (al-murū'a): A quality of manliness and decorum that avoids contemptible actions; defined as good bearing, guarding the tongue, avoiding foolishness, and rising above base traits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the testimony of a person who walks in public wearing only a sarawil (trousers)?
A) His testimony is accepted because it is not a sin.
B) His testimony is rejected because it violates mura'a.
C) His testimony is accepted only if he repents.
D) His testimony is rejected only if he does it repeatedly.

Key Takeaway
Lack of mura'a is an independent ground for rejecting testimony, distinct from sinfulness.

Open Reviling of the Salaf and Its Effect on Testimony
Explains ruling on testimony of one who openly reviles the salaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of one who openly reviles the salaf and distinguish between open and concealed reviling in terms of 'adala.

Core Idea
Open reviling of the salaf forfeits 'adala and rejects testimony; concealed reviling does not.

This lesson examines a key condition for uprightness ('adala) in witnesses. The Hanafi school holds that openly reviling the righteous predecessors (salaf) – including the Companions, Followers, and leading imams – shows apparent fisq (sinfulness), which invalidates testimony. However, if the reviling is concealed, the testimony is accepted because the fisq is not apparent. This ruling reflects the principle that testimony requires apparent uprightness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is open reviling of the salaf. The ruling: the witness's testimony is rejected due to loss of 'adala.
The act must be open (zahir); private reviling does not affect testimony.
2
Locate the condition
The condition is openness. The text explicitly restricts the ruling to 'openly' (yuzhir). If concealed, testimony is accepted as in al-Hidayah.
This shows the Hanafi emphasis on apparent condition over hidden sin.
3
Define the salaf
Salaf includes the Companions (Sahaba), the Followers (Tabi'un), and according to this text, also Abu Hanifa and other scholars. Some later sources include all early pious scholars.
There is an intra-Hanafi discussion on whether Abu Hanifa is a tabi'i.
4
Distinguish between fisq and kufr
Reviling the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar) is considered kufr, making the reviler an apostate and testimony definitely rejected. Reviling other Muslims (including non-salaf) is fisq, which also forfeits 'adala.
The text notes that the rule is general: reviling any Muslim, even if not from salaf, forfeits 'adala.
5
Note the practical consequence
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that testimony is rejected from anyone who openly reviles the salaf, whether the reviling is fisq or kufr.
The ruling is based on zahir al-riwayah and relied upon in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

منهم
المؤلف كغيره أو يظهر سب مسلم لكان أولى لأن العدالة تسقط بسبب مسلم وإن لم يكن من السلف كما في النهاية وغيرها وقولهم هنا بعدم القبول شامل لما إذا كان السب فسقاً أو كفراً فيشمل سب الشيخين رضي الله تعالى عنهما فإنه لا تقبل شهادة من سبهما لكونه كافراً كما في الخلاصة والبزازية وقدمناه في باب الردة والفرق بين السلف والخلف أن السلف الصالح الصدر الأول من التابعين والخلف بفتح اللام من بعدهم في الخير والسكون في الشر؛ كذا في مختصر النهاية وعطف أبي حنيفة على التابعين إما عطف خاص على عام بناء على أنه كما في مناقب الكردري وصرح به في العناية أو ليس منهم بناء على ما صرح به شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر فإنه جعله من الطبقة السادسة ممن عاصر صغار التابعين ولكن لم يثبت له لقاء أحد من الصحابة ؛ ذكره في تقريب التهذيب
His statement: (or openly reviles the salaf) due to the apparent fisq. It is restricted by 'openly' because if he conceals it, his testimony is accepted; thus in al-Hidayah. Even if he disassociates from the Companions, it is accepted as in al-Inayah. Reviling is insult as we have mentioned earlier. Salaf, as in al-Nihayah, are the Companions, the Followers, and Abu Hanifa. Added in Fath al-Qadir: and likewise the scholars. If he said... His statement: (Addition in Fath al-Qadir...) al-Ramli said: The complete text of Fath al-Qadir is: 'And speaking metaphorically based on an analogy, for the similarity is not a forbidden lie, hence metaphor is used in the Quran, but he rejected it because it implies self-humiliation and obedience for worldly gain, so this statement may be harmful if said to the caliph. Specifically... Page 156: Book of Testimonies, Chapter: On whose testimony is accepted and whose not. And his parents by breastfeeding, and the mother of his wife and her daughter, and the husband of his daughter, and the wife of his father and his son, and the people of whims except the Khattabiyyah. Among them: The author, like others, or he openly reviles a Muslim would be more appropriate, because 'adala is forfeited due to a Muslim even if he is not from the salaf, as in al-Nihayah and others. Their statement here about non-acceptance includes when the reviling is fisq or kufr; thus it includes reviling the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar), may Allah be pleased with them, for the testimony of one who reviles them is not accepted because he is a disbeliever, as in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, and we have mentioned it in the chapter on apostasy. The difference between salaf and khalaf is that the righteous salaf are the first generation of the Followers, and khalaf (with fatha on the lam) are those after them in goodness and rest in evil; thus in Mukhtasar al-Nihayah. The inclusion of Abu Hanifa among the Followers is either a specific inclusion under a general category based on what is in Manaqib al-Kardari and stated explicitly in al-Inayah, or he is not from them based on what Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar stated, for he placed him in the sixth layer among those who met the younger Followers but not proven to have met any Companion; mentioned in Taqrib al-Tahdhib.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on the testimony of one who openly reviles the salaf (the predecessors). The text states that if someone openly shows reviling of the salaf, his testimony is not accepted due to apparent fisq (sinfulness). The key point is that it must be open (zahir); if he conceals it, his testimony is accepted because the fisq is not apparent. The salaf include the Sahaba (Companions), the Tabi'un (Followers), and according to this text, Imam Abu Hanifa is also included among them, though there is a difference of opinion on whether he met any Companions. The reviling can be fisq (if it is of other Muslims) or kufr (if it includes reviling the two shaykhs, Abu Bakr and Umar, which is considered apostasy). The passage also clarifies that reviling a Muslim, even if not from the salaf, forfeits 'adala. The difference between salaf and khalaf is explained: salaf refers to the early pious generation, while khalaf refers to those after them, often with less virtue. The inclusion of Abu Hanifa among the salaf is discussed, with some considering him a Follower (tabi'i) and others not.

Key Terms
السلف (al-salaf): The righteous predecessors: the Companions, the Followers, and according to this text, also Abu Hanifa and other scholars.
العدالة (al-'adala): Uprightness or moral probity required in a witness; forfeited by open sin.
الفسق (al-fisq): Sinfulness; open fisq invalidates testimony.
الكفر (al-kufr): Disbelief; reviling the two shaykhs is considered kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) His testimony is not accepted because reviling the salaf is fisq.
B) His testimony is accepted because the fisq is not apparent.
C) His testimony is accepted only if he repents.
D) His testimony is not accepted because it shows bad character.

Key Takeaway
Open reviling of the salaf forfeits 'adala and makes testimony rejected; concealed reviling does not affect testimony.

Testimony for Relatives and from Ahl al-Ahwa'
Ruling on testimony for relatives and from ahl al-ahwa' with expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the relatives for whom testimony is accepted, apply the principle of tuhma to determine acceptance, and state the Hanafi position on testimony of ahl al-ahwa'.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted unless bias (tuhma) exists; separate property removes tuhma, and belief-based fisq does not disqualify.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two areas of testimony law: testifying for close relatives and testifying by people of heretical beliefs (ahl al-ahwa'). The Hanafi school uses the principle of tuhma (accusation of bias) as the benchmark. The passage lists specific relatives—brother, uncle, parents by breastfeeding, etc.—and explains that because their properties and benefits are separate from the testifier's, there is no tuhma. It then addresses a nuance: if the father is alive, testifying for a brother might seem problematic, but the answer confirms acceptance because the brother's property is entirely separate. A second caution: if the witness has been actively litigating alongside the plaintiff for years, he becomes like an opponent and his testimony is rejected. Finally, the text rules that testimony from ahl al-ahwa' (except the extreme Khattabiyyah sect) is accepted because their fisq is in belief, not action, so they remain 'udul in outward conduct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed relatives
Read the list: brother, uncle, parents by breastfeeding, mother of wife, daughter of wife, husband of daughter, wife of father, son. These are all relatives but note they are not ones where property is shared (e.g., son's property is separate from father).
The list excludes direct ascendants/descendants where property may be connected.
2
Understand the rationale: absence of tuhma
The principle: testimony is rejected if there is tuhma (accusation of bias). For these relatives, properties and their benefits are separate, so no tuhma exists. This is the key distinction from cases like father-son where property is connected.
Tuhma arises from financial or personal interest.
3
Analyze the objection from al-Muhit al-Burhani
If the father is alive, testifying for a brother might seem like indirect testimony for the father (since brother may benefit father). The commentator answers: testimony for brother is not for oneself at all because brother's property is entirely separate from the testifier's. The connection between father and son does not make the brother's testimony a testimony for the father.
This answer holds even if brother and father live together.
4
Note the litigant exception from al-Qunyah
If a person has repeatedly accompanied the plaintiff in litigation for years, he becomes like an opponent of the defendant and his testimony is rejected. This is a different form of tuhma based on partisanship.
The exception applies to relatives and non-relatives alike.
5
Apply the ruling on ahl al-ahwa'
People of whims (heretical beliefs) are accepted as witnesses except for the Khattabiyyah sect. The reason: their fisq is in belief (i'tiqad), not in action. They are still considered upright in their dealings, so testimony is accepted as long as they do not call others to their beliefs or commit open fisq.
Khattabiyyah are excluded for their extreme views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتقبل لأخيه وعمه وأبويه رضاعاً وأم امرأته وبنتها وزوج بنته وامرأة أبيه وابنه لانعدام التهمة لأن الأملاك ومنافعها متباينة ولا بسوطة لبعضهم في مال بعض. وفي المحيط البرهاني وهذا الجواب لا يشكل فيما إذا شهد لأخيه والأب ميت وإنما يشكل فيما إذا شهد لأخيه والأب حي، وينبغي أن لا تقبل شهادته لأن منافع الأملاك بین أخيه وأبيه متصلة فكأنه شهد لأبيه . والجواب أن شهادة الإنسان لأبيه إنما لا تقبل لأن منافع الأملاك بين الأب وابنه متصلة فكانت الشهادة للأب شهاد لنفسه من وجه فلم تقبل وأما شهادته لأخيه فليست لنفسه أصلاً لتباين الأملاك ا هـ . وفي القنية : امتدت الخصومة سنين ومع المدعي أخ وابن عم يخاصمان له مع المدعى عليه ثم شهدا له في هذه الخصومة بعد هذ الخصومات لا تقبل شهادتهما ا هـ . وذكر ابن وهبان : وقياس ذلك أن يطرد ذلك في كل قرابة وصاحب تردد مع قرابته أو صاحبه إلى المدعي في الخصومة سنين ويخاصم له ومعه على المدعي ثم يشهد بعد ذلك فإنه ينبغي أن لا تقبل، والفقة فيه أنه لما طال التردد مع المخاصم والمخاصمة له مع المدعى عليه صار بمنزلة الخصم للمدعى عليه ا هـ . وفي خزانة الفتاوى : إذا تخاصم الشهود والمدعى عليه تقبل إن كانوا ينبغي . حمله على ما إذا لم يساعدوا في الخصومة أو لم يكثر ذلك منهم توفيقاً. قوله : (وأهل الأهواء إلا الخطابية أي تقبل شهادتهم لأن فسقهم من حيث الاعتقاد عدولاً ا هـ. له فعدل إلى الاعتذار بأمر يقرب من خاطره
His statement: (And accepted for his brother, uncle, and his parents by breastfeeding, and the mother of his wife and her daughter, and the husband of his daughter, and the wife of his father, and his son) due to the absence of accusation, because properties and their benefits are separate, and one does not have control over the property of another. In al-Muhit al-Burhani: This answer is not problematic when he testifies for his brother and the father is dead; it is problematic when he testifies for his brother and the father is alive, and it is appropriate that his testimony should not be accepted because the benefits of property between his brother and father are connected, so it is as if he testified for his father. The answer is that a person's testimony for his father is not accepted because benefits of property between father and son are connected, so testimony for the father is testimony for himself in some respect, therefore not accepted. As for his testimony for his brother, it is not for himself at all, because properties are separate. In al-Qunyah: The litigation continued for years, and with the plaintiff were a brother and cousin who were litigating for him against the defendant; then they testified for him in this litigation after these litigations; their testimony is not accepted. Ibn Wahban mentioned: By analogy, this applies to every relative or companion who repeatedly comes with his relative or companion to the plaintiff in litigation for years and litigates for him against the plaintiff, then testifies afterwards; it is appropriate that it should not be accepted. The fiqh is that because the frequent coming with the litigant and litigating for him against the defendant, he becomes like an opponent of the defendant. In Khizanat al-Fatawa: If the witnesses and the defendant have litigated [with each other], it is accepted if they are upright. It should be interpreted as when they did not assist in the litigation or did not do so frequently, as a compromise. His statement: (And the people of whims except the Khattabiyyah) i.e., their testimony is accepted because their fisq is in belief; they are upright. So he turned to an excuse by something close to his mind.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First, testimony for close relatives such as brother, uncle, parents by breastfeeding, etc., is accepted because there is no accusation of bias (tuhma) since their properties and benefits are separate. The text addresses a potential objection: if the father is alive, testifying for a brother might be like testifying for the father indirectly because of shared interests? The answer is that the connection is not as strong; testimony for a brother does not benefit the testifier himself. However, if the testifier has been actively litigating for the plaintiff for years, he may be considered an opponent, and his testimony is rejected. Second, regarding ahl al-ahwa' (people of whims, i.e., those with heretical beliefs), their testimony is accepted except for the Khattabiyyah sect. Their fisq is in belief (i'tiqad), not in action, so they are considered 'udul (upright) in terms of testimony if they otherwise satisfy conditions. The Khattabiyyah are excluded because of their extreme views.

Key Terms
أهل الأهواء (ahl al-ahwā'): People of whims; those who hold heretical beliefs (e.g., innovators) but whose fisq is only in belief, not in action.
الخطابية (al-Khattābiyyah): A sect (followers of Abu al-Khattab) with extreme beliefs that are considered beyond the pale; their testimony is rejected entirely.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Accusation; the legal presumption of bias that disqualifies a witness when there is a strong personal interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following witnesses is most likely to have their testimony rejected due to tuhma?
A) A man testifying for his brother-in-law.
B) A woman testifying for her father (who is alive).
C) A cousin who has regularly accompanied the plaintiff in court for years.
D) A Muslim known to hold Mu'tazili beliefs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony for close relatives when there is no tuhma (bias) due to separate property, and accepts testimony from ahl al-ahwa' because their fisq is in belief, not action, except for the extreme Khattabiyyah sect.

Testimony for Relatives: The Principle of Suspicion
Expands matn ruling on relatives' testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi list of relatives whose testimony is accepted, explain the reasoning, and apply the qiyas to the case of testifying for a brother when the father is alive.

Core Idea
Testimony for relatives is accepted when benefits are separate, except direct self-interest.

The Hanafi school accepts testimony for specific relatives (brother, uncle, foster parents, in-laws) due to absence of suspicion (tuhma). However, a complication arises when testifying for a brother while the father is alive: does the indirect benefit connection disqualify? This lesson unpacks the ruling and the qiyas used to resolve it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the relatives listed
From the matn and commentary, list the relatives whose testimony is accepted according to Hanafi law: brother, uncle, two foster parents, mother of wife, daughter of wife, husband of daughter, father's wife, son. Note the reasoning: properties and benefits are separate.
The list is from the matn (كنز الدقائق) and commentary confirms.
2
Understand the principle of tuhma
The acceptance is based on lack of suspicion (tuhma). The general rule: testimony for someone with whom you share a direct benefit connection is rejected. For these relatives, the connection is indirect or nonexistent.
This is explained in al-Muhit al-Burhani and the commentary.
3
Analyze the problematic case: brother when father is alive
Some scholars analogized from father to brother: if father is alive, testifying for brother might indirectly benefit father (whose estate brother may inherit). But the Hanafi answer distinguishes: testimony for brother is not for oneself; benefits are completely separate.
The qiyas is a form of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) and is rejected in this case.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario where a man testifies for his brother while their father is alive, state the ruling and reasoning. The testimony is accepted because no tuhma exists.
Contrast with testimony for father (rejected).

كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل وأبويه رضاعاً وأم امرأته وبنتها وزوج بنته وامرأة أبيه وابنه وأهل الأهواء إلا الخطابية منهم المؤلف كغيره أو يظهر سب مسلم لكان أولى لأن العدالة تسقط بسبب إلى المدعي في الخصومة سنين ويخاصم له ومعه على المدعي ثم يشهد بعد ذلك فإنه ينبغي أن لا تقبل، والفقة فيه أنه لما طال التردد مع المخاصم والمخاصمة له مع المدعى عليه صار بمنزلة الخصم للمدعى عليه ا هـ . وفي خزانة الفتاوى : إذا تخاصم الشهود والمدعى عليه تقبل إن كانوا وينبغي . حمله على ما إذا لم يساعدوا في الخصومة أو لم يكثر ذلك منهم توفيقاً. قوله : (وأهل الأهواء إلا الخطابية أي تقبل شهادتهم لأن فسقهم من حيث الاعتقاد عدولاً ا هـ . له فعدل إلى الاعتذار بأمر يقرب من خاطره قوله : (وليس منها الصناعة الدنية الخ) قال الرملي : فتحرر أن العبرة للعدالة لا للحرفة وهذا الذي يجب أن يعول عليه ويفتى به فإنا نرى بعض أصحاب الحرف الدنية عنده من الدين والتقوى ما ليس عند كثير من أرباب الوجاهة وأصحاب المناصب وذوي المراتب وإن أكرمكم . عند الله أتقاكم) [الحجرات: ١٣]. قوله : (وفي خزانة الفتاوى إذا تخاصم الشهود والمدعى عليه تقبل الخ) قال الرملي : مفهومه أنهم إذا كانوا مستورين لا تقبل وإن لم تمتد الخصومة للتهمة بالمخاصمة، وإذا كانوا عدولاً تقبل وإن امتدت لارتفاع التهمة مع العدالة فيحمل ما في القنية على ما إذا لم يكونوا عدولاً لأنه مطلق، وما في الخزانة مقيد فيحمل المطلق على المقيد توفيقاً، وما قلناه أشبه لأن المعتمد في باب الشهادة العدالة تأمل قوله : (وليس هذا القيد في ظاهر الرواية إن كان المراد المقيد الذي ذكره في الذخيرة فلا معنى لرده لأنه سينقل تصحيحه وأن ما في الأصل محمول عليه فكان في حكم المذكور في ظاهر الرواية، وإن كان مراده ما زاده في السراج فكذلك لأن العدالة شرط في أهل السنة والجماعة ما ظنك في غيرهم. وفي فتح القدير قال محمد بقبول شهادة الخوارج إذا اعتقدوا ولم يقاتلوا فإنا قاتلوا ردت شهادتهم
The book of testimonies, chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. And his two foster parents, and the mother of his wife and her daughter, and the husband of his daughter, and his father's wife and his son, and the people of innovation except the Khattabiyya among them. The author and others: if he appears cursing a Muslim, it would be better because justice falls due to a Muslim even if not from the predecessors as in al-Nihaya and others. Their statement here of non-acceptance includes whether the cursing is sin or disbelief, so it includes cursing the two shaykhs, may Allah be pleased with them; the testimony of one who curses them is not accepted because he is a disbeliever as in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, and we have presented it in the chapter of apostasy. The difference between predecessor (salaf) and successor (khalaf): the righteous predecessors are the first generation of the Successors, and the successors (with fatha on the lam) are those after them in good and with sukun in evil; thus in Mukhtasar al-Nihaya. And the inclusion of Abu Hanifa among the Successors is either a specific inclusion in a general category based on what is in Manaqib al-Kardari and stated in al-Inaya, or he is not among them based on what Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar stated, for he made him of the sixth class of those who met the younger Successors but he did not establish meeting any Companion; mentioned in Taqrib al-Tahdhib. His statement: (And it is accepted for his brother, his uncle, his two foster parents, the mother of his wife and her daughter, the husband of his daughter, his father's wife and his son due to lack of suspicion because properties and their benefits are separate and none has authority over the property of another. And in al-Muhit al-Burhani: This answer is not problematic when he testifies for his brother and the father is dead; it is only problematic when he testifies for his brother and the father is alive, and it should not be accepted because the benefits of properties between his brother and father are connected, as if he testified for his father. The answer: testimony of a person for his father is not accepted because the benefits of properties between father and son are connected, so testifying for the father is testifying for himself in a sense, therefore not accepted. As for his testimony for his brother, it is not for himself at all due to separation of properties. End quote. And in al-Qunyah: If the dispute extended for years and the plaintiff has a brother and paternal cousin who plead for him against the defendant, then they testify for him in this dispute after these pleadings, their testimony is not accepted. End quote. And Ibn Wahban mentioned: By analogy, this applies to every relative or companion who frequently accompanies his relative or companion to the plaintiff in the dispute for years and pleads for him with him against the plaintiff, then testifies after that; it should not be accepted. The fiqh of it is that when the frequent accompanying of the one being pleaded against and the one pleaded for with the defendant becomes like being a litigant against the defendant. End quote. And in Khizanat al-Fatawa: If the witnesses and the defendant have disputed, it is accepted if they are [just], and it should be. It is interpreted as when they did not assist in the dispute or did not do so frequently, harmonizing. His statement: (And people of innovation except the Khattabiyya) means their testimony is accepted because their sin is in terms of belief. End quote. He then turned to excusing with something close to his mind. His statement: (And it is not among them lowly professions) al-Ramli said: It is established that the criterion is justice not occupation, and this is what should be relied upon and given fatwa, for we see some people of lowly professions have of religion and piety what many people of prestige, office holders, and rank owners do not have, and 'Indeed the most noble of you to Allah is the most righteous' (49:13). His statement: (And in Khizanat al-Fatawa: If the witnesses and the defendant have disputed...) al-Ramli said: Its implication is that if they are concealed (masturin) it is not accepted even if the dispute did not extend due to suspicion of the dispute, and if they are just it is accepted even if it extended due to the removal of suspicion with justice. So what is in al-Qunyah is interpreted as when they are not just, because it is absolute, and what is in Khizanat is restricted, so the absolute is carried on the restricted for harmonization. What we said is more appropriate because the relied upon in the chapter of testimony is justice. Consider his statement: (And this condition is not in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah)) if what is meant is the restricted mentioned in al-Dhakhira, then there is no meaning to its rejection because he will transmit its correction and that what is in the original is carried upon it, so it is in the ruling of what is mentioned in the apparent transmission. And if what is meant is what he added in al-Siraj, then likewise, because justice is a condition among Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, what do you think of others? And in Fath al-Qadir, Muhammad said: The testimony of the Khawarij is accepted if they have belief and do not fight; if they fight, their testimony is rejected.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing multiple rulings on the acceptance of testimony. It begins by mentioning the matn's list of relatives whose testimony is accepted: brother, uncle, foster parents, in-laws, etc., due to lack of suspicion (تہمة). The commentator expands on the reasoning, noting that properties and benefits are separate, so no partiality is expected. A problematic case arises when testifying for a brother while the father is alive: the analogy suggests rejection because the brother's benefit connects to the father. The answer distinguishes that testimony for a brother is not for oneself, unlike for a father. Then, from al-Qunyah, a scenario where prolonged pleading in a dispute disqualifies witnesses, extended by Ibn Wahban to any similar relationship. From Khizanat al-Fatawa, a conflicting statement accepting testimony if witnesses are just, resolved by harmonization: the rejection applies only when witnesses are not just. Next, the matn states that people of innovation (أهل الأهواء) are accepted except the Khattabiyya. The commentator explains their sin is in belief, so they are not unjust. However, the commentary then transitions to an aside about lowly professions (الصناعة الدنية), quoting al-Ramli that justice, not profession, is the criterion. The passage returns to the topic of disputes with a comment from al-Ramli reconciling the sources, emphasizing justice as the relied-upon standard. Finally, a discussion on the condition in Zahir al-Riwaya regarding the acceptance of innovators, noting that the condition (they are not disbelievers or immoral) is not from the apparent transmission, but the relied-upon position is that justice is required even for Ahl al-Sunnah, so for others it is even stricter. Imam Muhammad's opinion on Khawarij is cited: accepted if they only hold beliefs but do not fight; if they fight, rejected.

Key Terms
تہمة (tuhma): Suspicion of partiality or bias due to a personal interest.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; sworn statement in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, testimony for a brother is accepted even when the father is alive. What is the primary reason?
A) The brother is not a close relative.
B) The witness has no direct benefit in the brother's property.
C) The father's property is not connected to the brother's.
D) The matn explicitly includes brother without exception.

Key Takeaway
Testimony for a brother is accepted because the benefits of property are separate; direct benefit connection is required for rejection.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony of People of Innovation: The Hanafi Exception
Expands ruling on innovators' testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule on accepting testimony from people of innovation (ahl al-ahwa'), identify the exception for al-Khattabiyya, and apply the condition regarding fighting derived from Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Hanafis accept innovators' testimony unless they fight or are extremists like al-Khattabiyya.

The matn states that testimony of people of innovation (ahl al-ahwa') is accepted except for the Khattabiyya. But what about those who curse the Companions or engage in armed rebellion? The commentary expands on this, clarifying that justice (adalah) remains the benchmark, and that fighting disqualifies. This lesson explores the Hanafi position and the intra-school nuance from Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The matn: testimony of ahl al-ahwa' is accepted except the Khattabiyya. This is because their innovation is a matter of belief, not necessarily moral corruption.
The basis: they are considered just in their dealings, despite doctrinal deviation.
2
Identify the Khattabiyya exception
The Khattabiyya are a subsect known for bearing false witness for their comrades, so their testimony is rejected entirely.
This is not based on mere belief but on proven untrustworthiness.
3
Incorporate the condition from Muhammad al-Shaybani
Imam Muhammad adds that if innovators engage in fighting (as Khawarij did), their testimony is rejected. If they only hold beliefs and do not fight, it is accepted.
This is a condition not originally in the matn but derived from the principle that fighting indicates lack of justice.
4
Understand the nuance on cursing
Cursing the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar) is considered disbelief, so the testimony of such a person is rejected regardless of innovation status.
This aligns with the general rule that disbelievers' testimony is not accepted.

Source Text

His statement: (And it is not among them lowly professions) al-Ramli said: It is established that the criterion is justice not occupation, and this is what should be relied upon and given fatwa, for we see some people of lowly professions have of religion and piety what many people of prestige, office holders, and rank owners do not have, and 'Indeed the most noble of you to Allah is the most righteous' (49:13). His statement: (And in Khizanat al-Fatawa: If the witnesses and the defendant have disputed...) al-Ramli said: Its implication is that if they are concealed (masturin) it is not accepted even if the dispute did not extend due to suspicion of the dispute, and if they are just it is accepted even if it extended due to the removal of suspicion with justice. So what is in al-Qunyah is interpreted as when they are not just, because it is absolute, and what is in Khizanat is restricted, so the absolute is carried on the restricted for harmonization. What we said is more appropriate because the relied upon in the chapter of testimony is justice. Consider his statement: (And this condition is not in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah)) if what is meant is the restricted mentioned in al-Dhakhira, then there is no meaning to its rejection because he will transmit its correction and that what is in the original is carried upon it, so it is in the ruling of what is mentioned in the apparent transmission. And if what is meant is what he added in al-Siraj, then likewise, because justice is a condition among Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, what do you think of others? And in Fath al-Qadir, Muhammad said: The testimony of the Khawarij is accepted if they have belief and do not fight; if they fight, their testimony is rejected.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing multiple rulings on the acceptance of testimony. It begins by mentioning the matn's list of relatives whose testimony is accepted: brother, uncle, foster parents, in-laws, etc., due to lack of suspicion (تہمة). The commentator expands on the reasoning, noting that properties and benefits are separate, so no partiality is expected. A problematic case arises when testifying for a brother while the father is alive: the analogy suggests rejection because the brother's benefit connects to the father. The answer distinguishes that testimony for a brother is not for oneself, unlike for a father. Then, from al-Qunyah, a scenario where prolonged pleading in a dispute disqualifies witnesses, extended by Ibn Wahban to any similar relationship. From Khizanat al-Fatawa, a conflicting statement accepting testimony if witnesses are just, resolved by harmonization: the rejection applies only when witnesses are not just. Next, the matn states that people of innovation (أهل الأهواء) are accepted except the Khattabiyya. The commentator explains their sin is in belief, so they are not unjust. However, the commentary then transitions to an aside about lowly professions (الصناعة الدنية), quoting al-Ramli that justice, not profession, is the criterion. The passage returns to the topic of disputes with a comment from al-Ramli reconciling the sources, emphasizing justice as the relied-upon standard. Finally, a discussion on the condition in Zahir al-Riwaya regarding the acceptance of innovators, noting that the condition (they are not disbelievers or immoral) is not from the apparent transmission, but the relied-upon position is that justice is required even for Ahl al-Sunnah, so for others it is even stricter. Imam Muhammad's opinion on Khawarij is cited: accepted if they only hold beliefs but do not fight; if they fight, rejected.

Key Terms
أهل الأهواء (ahl al-ahwa'): People of innovation; those holding theological deviant beliefs.
الخطابية (al-Khattabiyya): A subsect known for false testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for rejecting the testimony of a person of innovation?
A) The person belongs to al-Khattabiyya.
B) The person engages in armed rebellion (fighting).
C) The person holds beliefs different from Ahl al-Sunnah.
D) The person curses the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar).

Key Takeaway
Innovators' testimony is accepted unless they are from Khattabiyya or engage in fighting; justice in actions is key.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Lowly Professions and Justice: The Criterion for Testimony
Expands ruling on lowly professions and reconciles sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that justice (adalah) is the sole criterion for accepting testimony, regardless of occupation, and reconcile apparent conflicts in the sources.

Core Idea
Justice matters more than profession; lowly trades do not disqualify witnesses.

The matn mentions that lowly professions (like street sweepers) are not among those disqualified from testifying. The commentary, quoting al-Ramli, affirms that justice (adalah) is the criterion, citing the Quranic verse (49:13). It also reconciles conflicting reports from al-Qunyah and Khizanat al-Fatawa regarding the effect of prolonged disputes on witness reliability. This lesson teaches you to prioritize justice over social status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on lowly professions
The matn states that lowly professions (صناعة دنية) are not among those whose testimony is rejected. This means a person's humble occupation does not per se disqualify them.
This overrides the misconception that certain jobs make a person unreliable.
2
Extract the Quranic proof
Al-Ramli cites the verse إِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِندَ اللَّهِ أَتْقَاكُمْ (49:13) to show that honor is by taqwa, not occupation.
The proof is based on the general principle of justice.
3
Understand the reconciliation of conflicting reports
Al-Qunyah says if witnesses plead for a party for years, their testimony is rejected. Khizanat says it is accepted if they are just. The author reconciles: rejection applies when witnesses are not just; acceptance when they are just.
The key is the witnesses' justice, not the duration of pleading.
4
Apply the principle to a modern scenario
A janitor (lowly profession) witnesses an accident. His testimony is accepted if he is just, despite his job.
Justice is determined by his religious and moral conduct, not his income.

The book of testimonies, chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. And his two foster parents, and the mother of his wife and her daughter, and the husband of his daughter, and his father's wife and his son, and the people of innovation except the Khattabiyya among them. The author and others: if he appears cursing a Muslim, it would be better because justice falls due to a Muslim even if not from the predecessors as in al-Nihaya and others. Their statement here of non-acceptance includes whether the cursing is sin or disbelief, so it includes cursing the two shaykhs, may Allah be pleased with them; the testimony of one who curses them is not accepted because he is a disbeliever as in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, and we have presented it in the chapter of apostasy. The difference between predecessor (salaf) and successor (khalaf): the righteous predecessors are the first generation of the Successors, and the successors (with fatha on the lam) are those after them in good and with sukun in evil; thus in Mukhtasar al-Nihaya. And the inclusion of Abu Hanifa among the Successors is either a specific inclusion in a general category based on what is in Manaqib al-Kardari and stated in al-Inaya, or he is not among them based on what Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar stated, for he made him of the sixth class of those who met the younger Successors but he did not establish meeting any Companion; mentioned in Taqrib al-Tahdhib. His statement: (And it is accepted for his brother, his uncle, his two foster parents, the mother of his wife and her daughter, the husband of his daughter, his father's wife and his son due to lack of suspicion because properties and their benefits are separate and none has authority over the property of another. And in al-Muhit al-Burhani: This answer is not problematic when he testifies for his brother and the father is dead; it is only problematic when he testifies for his brother and the father is alive, and it should not be accepted because the benefits of properties between his brother and father are connected, as if he testified for his father. The answer: testimony of a person for his father is not accepted because the benefits of properties between father and son are connected, so testifying for the father is testifying for himself in a sense, therefore not accepted. As for his testimony for his brother, it is not for himself at all due to separation of properties. End quote. And in al-Qunyah: If the dispute extended for years and the plaintiff has a brother and paternal cousin who plead for him against the defendant, then they testify for him in this dispute after these pleadings, their testimony is not accepted. End quote. And Ibn Wahban mentioned: By analogy, this applies to every relative or companion who frequently accompanies his relative or companion to the plaintiff in the dispute for years and pleads for him with him against the plaintiff, then testifies after that; it should not be accepted. The fiqh of it is that when the frequent accompanying of the one being pleaded against and the one pleaded for with the defendant becomes like being a litigant against the defendant. End quote. And in Khizanat al-Fatawa: If the witnesses and the defendant have disputed, it is accepted if they are [just], and it should be. It is interpreted as when they did not assist in the dispute or did not do so frequently, harmonizing. His statement: (And people of innovation except the Khattabiyya) means their testimony is accepted because their sin is in terms of belief. End quote. He then turned to excusing with something close to his mind. His statement: (And it is not among them lowly professions) al-Ramli said: It is established that the criterion is justice not occupation, and this is what should be relied upon and given fatwa, for we see some people of lowly professions have of religion and piety what many people of prestige, office holders, and rank owners do not have, and 'Indeed the most noble of you to Allah is the most righteous' (49:13). His statement: (And in Khizanat al-Fatawa: If the witnesses and the defendant have disputed...) al-Ramli said: Its implication is that if they are concealed (masturin) it is not accepted even if the dispute did not extend due to suspicion of the dispute, and if they are just it is accepted even if it extended due to the removal of suspicion with justice. So what is in al-Qunyah is interpreted as when they are not just, because it is absolute, and what is in Khizanat is restricted, so the absolute is carried on the restricted for harmonization. What we said is more appropriate because the relied upon in the chapter of testimony is justice. Consider his statement: (And this condition is not in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah)) if what is meant is the restricted mentioned in al-Dhakhira, then there is no meaning to its rejection because he will transmit its correction and that what is in the original is carried upon it, so it is in the ruling of what is mentioned in the apparent transmission. And if what is meant is what he added in al-Siraj, then likewise, because justice is a condition among Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, what do you think of others? And in Fath al-Qadir, Muhammad said: The testimony of the Khawarij is accepted if they have belief and do not fight; if they fight, their testimony is rejected.

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing multiple rulings on the acceptance of testimony. Key Terms
الصناعة الدنية (al-sina'a al-daniyya): Lowly profession; manual or low-status occupation.
مستور (mastur): Concealed; a person whose justice is not known (transparently good or bad).

According to the passage, what is the basis for reconciling the conflicting reports in al-Qunyah and Khizanat al-Fatawa?
A) The longer the dispute, the less credible the witnesses.
B) The witnesses must be just; the absolute report is restricted to those who are not just.
C) The witnesses must have a high profession to be accepted.
D) The reports are irreconcilable.

Key Takeaway
Justice (adalah) is the sole criterion for accepting testimony, regardless of profession; conflicting reports are harmonized by conditioning on justice.
