Testimony of a Disbelieving Slave Trader
States the ruling on testimony of a disbelieving slave trader and the reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the testimony of a disbelieving slave trader and explain the reasoning behind the distinction between testifying against a non-Muslim versus a Muslim.

Core Idea
A disbelieving slave trader's testimony is accepted against non-Muslims but not Muslims, because the debt impacts the Muslim master indirectly.

This lesson examines the first ruling in the passage: when can a disbelieving slave who engages in trade testify? The rule hinges on whether the testimony is against a non-Muslim or a Muslim, and the reasoning involves the slave's master's property interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness and the ruling
The witness is a disbelieving slave who is a trader. His testimony is accepted when testifying against a disbeliever, even if his master is Muslim.
The phrase 'العبد الكافر التاجر' is key: a slave who is a disbeliever and engages in trade.
2
Understand the converse
His testimony is not accepted when testifying against a Muslim. This is the opposite scenario.
3
Analyze the reasoning for acceptance against non-Muslims
When testifying against a non-Muslim, the debt is established against the slave himself. The master's property is not necessarily affected because the debt is on the slave, and the master's liability is not a necessary consequence.
The text says: 'لأن الدين يثبت على العبد واستحقاق مالية المولى غير مضاف إلى الشهادة'.
4
Analyze the reasoning for rejection against Muslims
Testifying against a Muslim would establish a claim against a Muslim, which requires Muslim witnesses. A non-Muslim's testimony is insufficient to prove a matter against a Muslim.
5
Recognize the analogy
The agent (wakil) with the principal (muwakkil) is like the slave with the master: the agent's testimony against a non-Muslim is accepted even if the principal is Muslim, but not against a Muslim.
This analogy helps extend the ruling to other relationships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اثنان العبد الكافر التاجر وإن كان مولاه مسلماً وعلى العكس لا تقبل لأن في الأول قامت على إثبات أمر على الكافر لأن الدين يثبت على العبد واستحقاق مالية المولى غير مضاف إلى الشهادة لأنه ليس من ضرورة وجوب الدين عليه استحقاق مالية المولى لا محالة بل ينفك عنه في الجملة، وفي الثانية قامت على إثبات أمر على المسلم والوكيل مع الموكل بمنزلة العبد مع المولى. ولا تقبل شهادة كافرين على شهادة مسلمين وعلى العكس تقبل، وتقبل شهادة الذمي بدين على ذمي ميت وإن كان وصيه مسلماً بشرط أن لا يكون عليه دين لمسلم فإن كان فقد كتبناه عن الجامع. وفي الخانية : ذمي مات فشهد عشرة من النصارى أنه أسلم لا يصلى عليه بشهادتهم، وكذا لو شهد فساق من المسلمين. ولو كان لهذا الميت ولي مسلم وبقية أوليائه كفار من أهل دينه فادعى الولي المسلم أنه أسلم وأنه أوصى إليه وأزاد أن يأخذ ميراثه وشهد من أهل الكفر بذلك يأخذ المولى المسلم ميراثه بشهادتهما لأن شهادتهم على الإسلام في حكم الميراث قامت على أوليائه الكفار، ويصلى عليه بشهادة وليه المسلم إن كان عدلاً، ولو لم يشهد على إسلامه غير الولي يصلى عليه بقول وليه المسلم ولا ميراث له ا هـ . ثم قال : لو شهد على نصراني أربعة من النصارى أنه زنى بأمة مسلمة فإن شهدوا أنه استكرهها حد الرجل، وإن قالوا طاوعته درئ الحد عنهما ويعزر الشهود لحق المسلمة لقذفهم الأمة ا هـ . وفي البدائع من النكاح : لو ادعى مسلم عبداً في يد ذمي أنه عبده وشهد كافران أنه عبده قضى به القاضي فلان لم تقبل لكونها شهادة على القاضي المسلم. وفي خزانة الأكمل : ولو شهد كافران على شهادة مسلمين لكافر على كافر لم تجز، ولو شهد مسلمان على شهادة كافر أنه لا بد من التزكية في شهادة الذمي قال في الولوالجية : تزكية الذمي إن تزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة ا هـ . وأفتى به قارئ الهداية وأصله في النوازل. وفي خزانة الأكمل معزياً إلى العيون شهد كافران على كافر فعدلا ثم أسلم وأسلما يؤمران أن يعيد الشهادة ويكفي تعديلهما في الكفر وإنما تعديل الكافر إلى المسلمين فإن تعديل الكافر للكافر لا يجوز ثم يسأل أولئك عن الشهود ا هـ. وقدمنا في مسائل التعديل أن تعديل الكافر بالمسلمين إن وجد وإلا فيسأل من عدول الكفار. وفي الملتقط : إذا سكر الذمي لا تقبل شهادته ا هـ . خاصة مسلمين فالمال بينهما في قولهم اهـ قوله : (وعلى العكس لا تقبل أي شهادة الكافر على العبد جازت ا هـ . ثم اعلم المسلم التاجر وإن كان مولاه كافراً. قوله : (فقد كتبناه عن الجامع قال الرملي في الكتاب : أجزت بينة المسلم وأعطيت حقه فإن بقي شيء كان للكافر، وروى الحسن بن زياد أن التركة تقسم بينهما على مقدار دينهما اهـ. من التتارخانية . ثم قال : ولو كان النصراني حياً وفي يده عبد ادعاه مسلم ونصراني وأقام كل منهما
Two: The disbelieving slave [who is] a trader, even if his master is Muslim, [his testimony is accepted]; and conversely it is not accepted because in the first case it is based on proving a matter against a disbeliever, because the debt is established against the slave, and the entitlement to the property of the master is not attributed to the testimony, because it is not necessarily entailed from the obligation of the debt on him; rather it can be separate from it. In the second case, it is based on proving a matter against a Muslim. And the agent with the principal is like the slave with the master. And the testimony of two disbelievers against the testimony of two Muslims is not accepted; conversely it is accepted. And the testimony of a dhimmi regarding a debt against a deceased dhimmi is accepted, even if his executor is Muslim, provided that there is no debt owed to a Muslim; if there is, we have already written it from al-Jami'. And in al-Khaniyah: A dhimmi died; ten Christians testified that he had become Muslim: the funeral prayer is not performed for him based on their testimony. Likewise, if immoral Muslims testified. And if this deceased had a Muslim guardian and the rest of his guardians were disbelievers of his religion, and the Muslim guardian claimed that he had become Muslim and that he had appointed him as executor and he wants to take his inheritance, and some of the disbelievers testified to that: the Muslim guardian takes his inheritance based on their testimony, because their testimony regarding Islam in the context of inheritance is established against his disbelieving guardians. And the funeral prayer is performed based on the testimony of his Muslim guardian if he is upright. And if no one other than the guardian testified to his Islam, the funeral prayer is performed based on the statement of his Muslim guardian, but he has no inheritance. End. Then he said: If four Christians testified against a Christian that he committed zina with a Muslim slave woman: if they testified that he compelled her, the man is hadded; and if they said she consented, the hadd is averted from both, and the witnesses are punished by ta'zir for the right of the Muslim woman because they slandered the slave woman. End. And in al-Bada'i' of Nikah: If a Muslim claimed a slave in the hand of a dhimmi that it is his slave, and two disbelievers testified that it is his slave, the judge [named] Flan judged it; it is not accepted because it is testimony against the Muslim judge. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: If two disbelievers testified to the testimony of two Muslims for a disbeliever against a disbeliever, it is not permissible. And if two Muslims testified to the testimony of a disbeliever, it is necessary to verify the integrity (tazkiyah) in the testimony of a dhimmi. Al-Walwaliji said: Verification of a dhimmi is that he is verified for trustworthiness in his religion, his tongue, and his hand, and that he is vigilant. End. Qari' al-Hidayah gave a fatwa to this; its origin is in al-Nawazil. And in Khizanat al-Akmal, citing al-'Uyun: Two disbelievers testified against a disbeliever and were declared upright, then they [the witness or the parties?] became Muslim: they are ordered to repeat the testimony, and their declaration of uprightness while in disbelief suffices. However, the verification of a disbeliever is by Muslims, for verification of a disbeliever by a disbeliever is not permissible. Then those [Muslims] are asked about the witnesses. End. We have already mentioned in the issues of tazkiyah that the verification of a disbeliever by Muslims is if found; otherwise, one asks from the upright among the disbelievers. And in al-Multaqat: If a dhimmi is intoxicated, his testimony is not accepted. End. ... specifically Muslims, the property is between them in their statement. End. His statement: (And conversely it is not accepted) i.e., the testimony of a disbeliever against the slave is permissible. End. Then know: the Muslim trader even if his master is a disbeliever. His statement: (We have already written it from al-Jami') al-Ramli said in the book: I allowed the evidence of the Muslim and gave him his right; if anything remains, it belongs to the disbeliever. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that the estate is divided between them according to their debts. End. from al-Tatarkhaniyah. Then he said: And if the Christian was alive and in his hand was a slave claimed by a Muslim and a Christian, and each one produced...
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage from page 160 continues the discussion on testimony of non-Muslims, focusing on specific cases. First, the testimony of a disbelieving slave who is a trader (i.e., engages in commerce) is accepted when testifying against a disbeliever, even if his master is Muslim. Conversely, it is not accepted against a Muslim because the debt is on the slave and the master's property interest is not directly affected by the testimony; the ruling is analogous to an agent and principal. Then, a series of rulings: the testimony of two disbelievers against the testimony of two Muslims is not accepted, but the reverse (Muslims against disbelievers) is accepted. A dhimmi's testimony on a debt against a deceased dhimmi is accepted even if the executor is Muslim, provided there is no Muslim creditor; if there is, a prior ruling from al-Jami' applies. Next, from al-Khaniyah: if ten Christians testify that a dhimmi became Muslim, the funeral prayer is not performed based on their testimony (as conversion requires strong proof). If the deceased has a Muslim guardian and other disbelieving guardians, the Muslim guardian can inherit based on the testimony of disbelievers that the deceased converted, because that testimony is against the disbelieving guardians. The funeral prayer can be performed based on the Muslim guardian's testimony alone, but he does not inherit without additional witnesses. Then, a case of zina: four Christians testify against a Christian for zina with a Muslim slave woman; if they say he compelled her, he is stoned/hadded; if they say she consented, no hadd on either, but witnesses are ta'zired for slander. From al-Bada'i': if a Muslim claims a slave in a dhimmi's possession, two disbelievers' testimony for the Muslim is not accepted because it would be testimony against the Muslim judge (i.e., the claim is against the dhimmi, but the potential impact on the Muslim judge's ruling is problematic). From Khizanat al-Akmal: two disbelievers cannot testify to the testimony of two Muslims (i.e., they cannot be secondary witnesses for Muslim witnesses); however, two Muslims can testify to the testimony of a disbeliever, but tazkiyah of the dhimmi is required. Al-Walwaliji details that tazkiyah of a dhimmi involves honesty in religion, tongue, and hand. Then, a case of witnesses who later convert: if two disbelievers testified and were deemed upright, then all become Muslim, they must retestify; their previous tazkiyah as disbelievers is sufficient, but tazkiyah of a disbeliever must be done by Muslims. Finally, from al-Multaqat: a dhimmi's testimony when intoxicated is not accepted. The passage ends with a reference to a case of a living Christian with a slave claimed by a Muslim and a Christian, which is incomplete. The commentary relates each ruling to its source and notes the underlying principles, emphasizing that non-Muslim testimony is only accepted in limited contexts and never against Muslims or in matters that would harm a Muslim's right.

Key Terms
العبد الكافر التاجر (al-'abd al-kāfir al-tājir): A disbelieving slave who engages in trade; his testimony is accepted for claims against non-Muslims.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony; the text discusses various conditions for its acceptance, including the religion and status of the witness.
وكيل (wakīl): Agent; the passage draws an analogy between an agent/principal relationship and slave/master for testimony rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the testimony of a disbelieving slave trader accepted?
A) When testifying against a Muslim.
B) When testifying against a non-Muslim, even if his master is Muslim.
C) Only if his master is also a disbeliever.
D) It is never accepted.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a disbelieving slave trader is accepted only against non-Muslims, due to the indirect effect on the Muslim master's property.

Shahadat — Testimony

12 min
Testimony of Dhimmis and Conversion Scenarios
States rulings on dhimmi testimony for debts and conversion scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings on dhimmi testimony regarding debts, inheritance, and funeral prayer in cases of claimed conversion.

Core Idea
Dhimmi testimony is accepted for debts against other dhimmis, but not if a Muslim is involved; conversion claims require strong proof.

This lesson focuses on the middle portion of the passage, which details the acceptance of dhimmi testimony for debts, and the complex scenario when a dhimmi claims to have converted to Islam. The rulings cover inheritance and funeral prayer, showing how testimony from non-Muslims can be used in limited contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for dhimmi testimony on debts
The testimony of a dhimmi concerning a debt against a deceased dhimmi is accepted, even if the executor is Muslim, provided there is no Muslim creditor.
The condition 'لا يكون عليه دين لمسلم' is crucial.
2
Understand the exception when a Muslim creditor exists
If the deceased dhimmi owes a debt to a Muslim, the ruling differs and is recorded in al-Jami'.
The text says 'فإن كان فقد كتبناه عن الجامع'.
3
Analyze the conversion case for funeral prayer
If ten Christians testify that a dhimmi became Muslim, the funeral prayer is not performed based on their testimony. Only the testimony of upright Muslims is accepted for establishing conversion for funeral purposes.
This shows that conversion to Islam requires strong evidence.
4
Apply the inheritance scenario
If a deceased dhimmi has a Muslim guardian and other disbelieving guardians, and the Muslim guardian claims the deceased converted, the testimony of the disbelieving guardians is accepted to establish the conversion for inheritance purposes (because the testimony is against the disbelieving guardians).
The key: the testimony is for the benefit of a Muslim against other non-Muslims.
5
Recognize the limit for the Muslim guardian's testimony
The Muslim guardian's testimony alone suffices for funeral prayer (if he is upright) but does not grant him inheritance; additional witnesses are needed.
This balances between facilitating prayer and protecting inheritance rights.

الدين عليه استحقاق مالية المولى لا محالة بل ينفك عنه في الجملة، وفي الثانية قامت على إثبات أمر على المسلم والوكيل مع الموكل بمنزلة العبد مع المولى. ولا تقبل شهادة كافرين على شهادة مسلمين وعلى العكس تقبل، وتقبل شهادة الذمي بدين على ذمي ميت وإن كان وصيه مسلماً بشرط أن لا يكون عليه دين لمسلم فإن كان فقد كتبناه عن الجامع. وفي الخانية : ذمي مات فشهد عشرة من النصارى أنه أسلم لا يصلى عليه بشهادتهم، ميراثه بشهادتهما لأن شهادتهم على الإسلام في حكم الميراث قامت على أوليائه الكفار، ويصلى عليه بشهادة وليه المسلم إن كان عدلاً، ولو لم يشهد على إسلامه غير الولي يصلى عليه بقول وليه المسلم ولا ميراث له ا : لو ادعى مسلم عبداً في يد ذمي أنه عبده وشهد كافران أنه عبده قضى به القاضي فلان لم تقبل لكونها شهادة على القاضي المسلم. وفي خزانة الأكمل : ولو شهد كافران على شهادة مسلمين لكافر على كافر لم تجز، ولو شهد مسلمان على شهادة كافر أنه لا بد من التزكية في شهادة الذمي قال في الولوالجية : تزكية الذمي إن تزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة ا هـ . وأفتى به قارئ الهداية وأصله في النوازل. وفي Two: The disbelieving slave [who is] a trader, even if his master is Muslim, [his testimony is accepted]; and conversely it is not accepted because in the first case it is based on proving a matter against a disbeliever, because the debt is established against the slave, and the entitlement to the property of the master is not attributed to the testimony, because it is not necessarily entailed from the obligation of the debt on him; rather it can be separate from it. Tazkiyah of Dhimmis and Special Cases
Covers tazkiyah of dhimmis, intoxication, and special cases like zina and conflicting claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the process of tazkiyah for dhimmi witnesses and apply the rulings on intoxication, zina testimony, and conflicting claims.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah of a dhimmi verifies his honesty; it must be done by Muslims if possible. Intoxication invalidates testimony.

This lesson covers the final part of the passage, which includes details on verifying the integrity (tazkiyah) of dhimmi witnesses, the effect of intoxication, and a case of zina with a Muslim slave woman. It also touches on a scenario where a slave is claimed by both a Muslim and a Christian.

Guided Path
1
Understand tazkiyah of a dhimmi
Tazkiyah involves verifying that the dhimmi is trustworthy in his religion, tongue, and hand, and that he is vigilant. This is the standard for accepting his testimony.
The text from al-Walwaliji: 'تزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة'.
2
Note who performs tazkiyah
Tazkiyah of a dhimmi must be done by Muslims if available. If not, upright dhimmis may be asked. The testimony of a dhimmi is not accepted without proper tazkiyah.
This ensures the integrity of the process.
3
Apply the intoxication rule
If a dhimmi is intoxicated, his testimony is not accepted. This indicates that sobriety is a condition for testimony.
From al-Multaqat: 'إذا سكر الذمي لا تقبل شهادته'.
4
Analyze the zina case
Four Christians testify against a Christian for zina with a Muslim slave woman. If they testify that he compelled her, the man is subject to hadd. If they say she consented, no hadd on either, but the witnesses are ta'zired for slander against the slave woman.
This shows how non-Muslim testimony is treated in criminal cases involving Muslims.
5
Recognize the incomplete conflicting claims case
The passage ends with a case where a Muslim and a Christian both claim a slave in the possession of a Christian, and each produces witnesses. The ruling is cut off.
The text from Khizanat al-Akmal is incomplete; we only have the beginning.

العكس لا تقبل أي شهادة الكافر على العبد جازت ا هـ . ثم اعلم المسلم التاجر وإن كان مولاه كافراً. قوله : (فقد كتبناه عن الجامع قال الرملي في الكتاب : أجزت بينة المسلم وأعطيت حقه فإن بقي شيء كان للكافر، وروى الحسن بن زياد أن التركة تقسم بينهما على مقدار دينهما اهـ. من التتارخانية . ثم قال : ولو كان النصراني حياً وفي يده عبد ادعاه مسلم ونصراني وأقام كل منهما
Two: The disbelieving slave [who is] a trader, even if his master is Muslim, [his testimony is accepted]; and conversely it is not accepted because in the first case it is based on proving a matter against a disbeliever, because the debt is established against the slave, and the entitlement to the property of the master is not attributed to the testimony, because it is not necessarily entailed from the obligation of the debt on him; rather it can be separate from it. In the second case, it is based on proving a matter against a Muslim. And the agent with the principal is like the slave with the master. And the testimony of two disbelievers against the testimony of two Muslims is not accepted; conversely it is accepted. And the testimony of a dhimmi regarding a debt against a deceased dhimmi is accepted, even if his executor is Muslim, provided that there is no debt owed to a Muslim; if there is, we have already written it from al-Jami'. And in al-Khaniyah: A dhimmi died; ten Christians testified that he had become Muslim: the funeral prayer is not performed for him based on their testimony. Likewise, if immoral Muslims testified. And if this deceased had a Muslim guardian and the rest of his guardians were disbelievers of his religion, and the Muslim guardian claimed that he had become Muslim and that he had appointed him as executor and he wants to take his inheritance, and some of the disbelievers testified to that: the Muslim guardian takes his inheritance based on their testimony, because their testimony regarding Islam in the context of inheritance is established against his disbelieving guardians. And the funeral prayer is performed based on the testimony of his Muslim guardian if he is upright. And if no one other than the guardian testified to his Islam, the funeral prayer is performed based on the statement of his Muslim guardian, but he has no inheritance. End. Then he said: If four Christians testified against a Christian that he committed zina with a Muslim slave woman: if they testified that he compelled her, the man is hadded; and if they said she consented, the hadd is averted from both, and the witnesses are punished by ta'zir for the right of the Muslim woman because they slandered the slave woman. End. And in al-Bada'i' of Nikah: If a Muslim claimed a slave in the hand of a dhimmi that it is his slave, and two disbelievers testified that it is his slave, the judge [named] Flan judged it; it is not accepted because it is testimony against the Muslim judge. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: If two disbelievers testified to the testimony of two Muslims for a disbeliever against a disbeliever, it is not permissible. And if two Muslims testified to the testimony of a disbeliever, it is necessary to verify the integrity (tazkiyah) in the testimony of a dhimmi. Al-Walwaliji said: Verification of a dhimmi is that he is verified for trustworthiness in his religion, his tongue, and his hand, and that he is vigilant. End. Qari' al-Hidayah gave a fatwa to this; its origin is in al-Nawazil. And in Khizanat al-Akmal, citing al-'Uyun: Two disbelievers testified against a disbeliever and were declared upright, then they [the witness or the parties?] became Muslim: they are ordered to repeat the testimony, and their declaration of uprightness while in disbelief suffices. However, the verification of a disbeliever is by Muslims, for verification of a disbeliever by a disbeliever is not permissible. Then those [Muslims] are asked about the witnesses. End. We have already mentioned in the issues of tazkiyah that the verification of a disbeliever by Muslims is if found; otherwise, one asks from the upright among the disbelievers. And in al-Multaqat: If a dhimmi is intoxicated, his testimony is not accepted. End. ... specifically Muslims, the property is between them in their statement. End. His statement: (And conversely it is not accepted) i.e., the testimony of a disbeliever against the slave is permissible. End. Then know: the Muslim trader even if his master is a disbeliever. His statement: (We have already written it from al-Jami') al-Ramli said in the book: I allowed the evidence of the Muslim and gave him his right; if anything remains, it belongs to the disbeliever. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that the estate is divided between them according to their debts. End. from al-Tatarkhaniyah. Then he said: And if the Christian was alive and in his hand was a slave claimed by a Muslim and a Christian, and each one produced...
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage from page 160 continues the discussion on testimony of non-Muslims, focusing on specific cases. First, the testimony of a disbelieving slave who is a trader (i.e., engages in commerce) is accepted when testifying against a disbeliever, even if his master is Muslim. Conversely, it is not accepted against a Muslim because the debt is on the slave and the master's property interest is not directly affected by the testimony; the ruling is analogous to an agent and principal. Then, a series of rulings: the testimony of two disbelievers against the testimony of two Muslims is not accepted, but the reverse (Muslims against disbelievers) is accepted. A dhimmi's testimony on a debt against a deceased dhimmi is accepted even if the executor is Muslim, provided there is no Muslim creditor; if there is, a prior ruling from al-Jami' applies. Next, from al-Khaniyah: if ten Christians testify that a dhimmi became Muslim, the funeral prayer is not performed based on their testimony (as conversion requires strong proof). If the deceased has a Muslim guardian and other disbelieving guardians, the Muslim guardian can inherit based on the testimony of disbelievers that the deceased converted, because that testimony is against the disbelieving guardians. The funeral prayer can be performed based on the Muslim guardian's testimony alone, but he does not inherit without additional witnesses. Then, a case of zina: four Christians testify against a Christian for zina with a Muslim slave woman; if they say he compelled her, he is stoned/hadded; if they say she consented, no hadd on either, but witnesses are ta'zired for slander. From al-Bada'i': if a Muslim claims a slave in a dhimmi's possession, two disbelievers' testimony for the Muslim is not accepted because it would be testimony against the Muslim judge (i.e., the claim is against the dhimmi, but the potential impact on the Muslim judge's ruling is problematic). From Khizanat al-Akmal: two disbelievers cannot testify to the testimony of two Muslims (i.e., they cannot be secondary witnesses for Muslim witnesses); however, two Muslims can testify to the testimony of a disbeliever, but tazkiyah of the dhimmi is required. Al-Walwaliji details that tazkiyah of a dhimmi involves honesty in religion, tongue, and hand. Then, a case of witnesses who later convert: if two disbelievers testified and were deemed upright, then all become Muslim, they must retestify; their previous tazkiyah as disbelievers is sufficient, but tazkiyah of a disbeliever must be done by Muslims. Finally, from al-Multaqat: a dhimmi's testimony when intoxicated is not accepted. The passage ends with a reference to a case of a living Christian with a slave claimed by a Muslim and a Christian, which is incomplete. The commentary relates each ruling to its source and notes the underlying principles, emphasizing that non-Muslim testimony is only accepted in limited contexts and never against Muslims or in matters that would harm a Muslim's right.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): The process of verifying the integrity ('adalah) of a witness before accepting his testimony.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen under Islamic protection; his testimony is accepted in limited cases.
سكر (sukr): Intoxication; a condition that invalidates a dhimmi's testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Walwaliji, what does tazkiyah of a dhimmi verify?
A) That he is wealthy.
B) That he is trustworthy in his religion, tongue, and hand, and that he is vigilant.
C) That he has Muslim friends.
D) That he is literate.

Key Takeaway
Tazkiyah of a dhimmi must be done by Muslims, verifying his honesty in religion, speech, and actions; intoxication invalidates his testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony of a Kafir Slave: Ruling and Reasoning
Explains acceptance of testimony from a Kafir slave and mirror case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of a Kafir slave and explain the legal reasoning (talil) that distinguishes acceptance based on the party against whom testimony is given.

Core Idea
Testimony of a Kafir is accepted against a Kafir, not a Muslim—the object of testimony determines permissibility.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a critical distinction in Hanafi shahadat: the testimony of a Kafir slave is accepted when it establishes a claim against a Kafir, but rejected when against a Muslim. The author not only states the ruling but unpacks the underlying legal reasoning (talil), enabling you to apply the same logic to analogous cases such as the agent (wakil) and principal (muwakkil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the specific ruling: testimony of a Kafir slave merchant is accepted when testifying against a Kafir, even if his master is a Muslim. Conversely, it is not accepted when testifying against a Muslim, even if his master is a Kafir.
The ruling is stated at the outset: 'اثنان العبد الكافر التاجر... وعلى العكس لا تقبل'.
2
Isolate the distinguishing factor
Note that the acceptance hinges on the status of the party against whom testimony is given (Kafir vs. Muslim), not the witness's own status or the master's religion.
The factor is 'Against whom is the testimony?'
3
Trace the talil (reasoning)
The author explains: In the first case, testimony proves a matter against a Kafir, which is permissible. Though the debt is against the slave, it does not necessarily entail a claim against the master's property. In the second case, it proves a matter against a Muslim, which is not permitted.
The reasoning is explicitly given after 'لأن'.
4
Apply to the converse case (agent and principal)
The analogy is drawn: the agent (wakil) with the principal (muwakkil) is like the slave with the master. The same ruling applies to the agent's testimony.
Text: 'والوكيل مع الموكل بمنزلة العبد مع المولى.'
5
Expand to related rulings on Dhimmi testimony
The passage then covers acceptance of a Dhimmi's testimony under conditions, including tazkiya. Recognize that these are applications of the same principle: testimony is assessed based on the parties involved and the need for reliability (tazkiya).
Read the tazkiya conditions: 'تزكية الذمي إن تزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة.'

Book of Testimonies, Chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose not. Two [sections]. The slave [who is a] Kafir merchant, even if his master is Muslim, and conversely [i.e., testimony of a Kafir on a Muslim slave] is not accepted. Because in the first case, it is established to prove a matter against a Kafir, since the debt is established against the slave and the entitlement to the master's property is not attributed to the testimony because it is not necessarily entailed by the obligation of the debt upon him that the master's property is inevitably claimed, rather it is separable in general. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings regarding acceptance of testimony from a Kafir slave and related cases. It begins by stating that the testimony of a Kafir slave who is a merchant is accepted against a Kafir, even if his master is Muslim, but not against a Muslim. The reasoning is that in the first case, the testimony is to prove a claim against a Kafir, which is permissible, while in the second case it is against a Muslim, which is not accepted. The same applies to the agent (wakil) and principal (muwakkil). 

The passage then covers multiple specific cases: testimony of two Kafirs against two Muslims is not accepted, but the reverse is accepted; testimony of a Dhimmi for a debt against a deceased Dhimmi is accepted with conditions; a Dhimmi's death and testimony about his Islam; testimony of four Christians against a Christian for zina with a Muslim slave; a Muslim claiming a slave from a Dhimmi; testimony on testimony; tazkiya of a Dhimmi; two Kafirs testifying, then becoming Muslim; and a drunk Dhimmi's testimony. Each case is explained with its reasoning and source from earlier Hanafi works.

Key Terms
على العكس (ala al-aks): Converse case: testimony of a Kafir against a Muslim slave merchant.
التزكية (al-tazkiya): Process of declaring a witness upright (adl), here specifically for a Dhimmi: trustworthy in religion, tongue, and hand, and vigilant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Kafir's testimony is accepted against a Kafir but not a Muslim, with specific conditions for Dhimmi witnesses including tazkiya and sobriety.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Testimony of a Harbi (Musta'min)
Opening segment on testimony of Harbi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting the testimony of a Harbi (musta'min) and identify the exception for different abodes (dar).

Core Idea
A Harbi's testimony is accepted only against his like, not across different abodes.

This part of the passage clarifies who qualifies as a Harbi for testimony and when their testimony is accepted. The ruling hinges on legal authority (wilaya) – a concept that also affects inheritance and jurisdiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness
The Harbi in this context is specifically the musta'min – a non-Muslim from enemy territory who enters Muslim lands with safe conduct. A mere Harbi without aman would be enslaved and cannot testify.
No wilaya for slaves.
2
State the general ruling
The testimony of a Harbi (musta'min) is accepted against another Harbi (musta'min), but not against a Dhimmi, because the Harbi has no authority over the Dhimmi.
Wilaya is derived from religion and abode.
3
Apply the exception
If the two Harbis belong to different abodes (e.g., Franks vs. Abyssinians), the testimony is not accepted because there is no mutual authority between their respective realms. This parallels the rule that they do not inherit from each other.
Dar differs by strength and kingship.
4
Understand the rationale
The underlying principle is that testimony requires some form of legal connection (wilaya). Without it, the witness cannot be trusted to have the necessary concern for justice across conflicting polities.

Source Text

كانا
قوله : (والحربي على مثله أي وتقبل شهادته على مثله لا على الذمي لأنه لا ولاية له على الذمي. والمراد بالحربي المستأمن لأنه لا يتصور غيره فإن الحربي لو دخل بلا أمان فهذا استرقاق ولا شهادة للعبيد على أحد ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ويستثنى من الحربي على مثله ما إذا من دارين مختلفين كالإفرنج والحبس لانقطاع الولاية بينهما ولهذا لا يتوارثان والدار تختلف باختلاف المنعة والملك قوله : ( ومن ألم بصغيرة إن اجتنب الكبائر) أي تقبل شهادة من ارتكب صغيرة إن اجتنب الكبائر كلها وقد أشار هنا إلى العدالة فإنها شرط قبول الشهادة وهي الاستقامة وهي بالإسلام واعتدال العقل ويعارضه هوى يضله ويصده، وليس لكمالها حد يدرك مداه ويكتفى لقبولها بأدناه كيلا يضيع الحقوق وهو رجحان جهة الدين والعقل على الهوى والشهوة وأحسن ما قيل فيه ما عن أبي يوسف العدل أن يكون مجتنباً للكبائر غير مصر على الصغائر وأن تكون مروءته ظاهرة فعدمها مفوت لها وزاد في المحيط أن يعتاد الصدق ويجتنب الكذب ديانة ومروءته. وفي الولوالجية : وينبغي أن يكون الشاهد مسناً عفيفاً ذا مال ذا فضل لأنه إذا كان كذلك لا يطمع في أموال الناس ويستحي من ارتكاب ما لا يحل في الشرع فكان أولى بالاستشهاد ا.هـ. وبه يعلم من ينصبه القاضي شاهداً. بین الناس. وفي الخانية : الفاسق إذا تاب لا تقبل شهادته ما لم يمض عليه زمان تظهر التوبة ثم بعضهم قدره بستة أشهر وبعضهم قدره بسنة والصحيح أن ذلك مفوض إلى رأي القاضي والمعدل ا هـ. وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان عدلاً فشهد بزور ثم تاب فشهد تقبل من غير مدة ا هـ. وقدمنا أن الشاهد إذا كان فاسقاً سراً لا ينبغي أن يخبر بفسقه كيلا يبطل حق المدعي وصرح به في العمدة أيضاً. وفي العتابية من أجر بيته لمن يبيع الخمر لم تسقط عدالته قوله : (والأقلف) أي الكبير الذي لم يختتن تقبل شهادته لأن العدالة لا تخل بترك الختان لكونه سنة عندنا. أطلقه وقيده قاضيخان بأن يتركه لخوف على نفسه، أما إذا تركه بغير عذر لم تقبل. وقيده في الهداية بأن لا يتركه استخفافاً بالدين أما إذا تركه استخفافاً لم تقبل شهادته لأنه لم يبق عدلاً وكما تقبل شهادته تصح إمامته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يقدر الإمام للختان وقتاً معلوماً لعدم
شاهدين نصرانيين فهو للمسلم . قال محمد : هو قول أبي يوسف أيضاً وروى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي يوسف أن العبد بينهما نصفان اهـ قوله : (فلان) بدل من القاضي قوله : (ولو كان عدلاً فشهد بزور ثم تاب الخ) المعروف بالعدالة إذا شهد بزور عن أبي يوسف أنه لا تقبل شهادته أبداً لأنه لا تعرف توبته، وروى الفقيه أبو جعفر أنه تقبل شهادته وعليه الاعتماد خانية قبيل التزكية والتعديل قوله : (لا ينبغي أن يخبر بفسقه الظاهر أن المراد لا يحل وفي الخانية : الشاهد إذا كان فاسقاً . في السر وهو في الظاهر عدل فأراد القاضي أن يقضي بشهادته فأخبر الشاهد عن نفسه أنه ليس بعدل صح إقراره على نفسه إلا أنه إذا كان صادقاً في الشهادة لا أن يسعه يخبر عن نفسه أنه ليس بعدل لأن فيه إبطال
حق المدعي اهـ.
...they were. His statement: (And the Harbi against his like) i.e., his testimony is accepted against his like, not against the Dhimmi, because he has no authority over the Dhimmi. And the intended meaning of Harbi is the musta'min (one given safe conduct), because nothing else is conceivable. For if a Harbi enters without safe conduct, then it is enslavement and there is no testimony for slaves against anyone. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And an exception is made from the Harbi against his like in the case of two different abodes like the Franks and the Abyssinians, due to the lack of authority between them, and for this reason they do not inherit from each other, and the abode differs by strength and kingship. His statement: (And whoever does a minor sin if he avoids major sins) i.e., the testimony of one who commits a minor sin is accepted if he avoids all major sins. And he indicated here 'adala (integrity), which is a condition for acceptance of testimony, and it is uprightness, and it is through Islam and soundness of mind, and it is opposed by desire that misguides and prevents him. And its perfection has no limit that can be reached, and the minimum sufficing for acceptance is taken so that rights are not lost. It is the preponderance of the aspect of religion and intellect over desire and lust. And the best said about it is what is from Abu Yusuf: The upright person is one who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and whose chivalry is apparent, so its absence destroys it. And in al-Muhit it added: he should be accustomed to truthfulness and avoid lying in religion and chivalry. And in al-Walwalijiyya: It is recommended that the witness be older, chaste, wealthy, virtuous; because if he is so, he does not covet people's wealth and is ashamed of committing what is unlawful in Shari'a, so he is more deserving of being taken as a witness. End. And by this it is known whom the judge appoints as witness among the people. And in al-Khaniyya: If an immoral person repents, his testimony is not accepted until a time passes in which repentance appears; then some scholars estimated it as six months, some as a year, and the correct view is that it is delegated to the opinion of the judge and the one who declares uprightness. End. And in al-Khulasa: If one was upright and gave false testimony, then repented and testifies, it is accepted without any time period. End. And we previously stated that if a witness is secretly immoral, he should not inform of his immorality so as not to invalidate the claimant's right, and this was explicitly stated in al-Umda as well. And in al-Atabiyya: One who rents out his house to someone who sells wine, his uprightness is not nullified. His statement: (And the aqlaf) i.e., the adult who has not been circumcised, his testimony is accepted because uprightness is not undermined by leaving circumcision since it is sunnah in our school. It is unrestricted, but Qadikhan restricted it to one who leaves it due to fear for himself; but if he leaves it without excuse, it is not accepted. And in al-Hidaya it is restricted to one who does not leave it out of contempt for religion; if he leaves it out of contempt, his testimony is not accepted because he is no longer upright. And just as his testimony is accepted, his leading of prayer is valid. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the Imam did not set a known time for circumcision due to lack of... two Christian witnesses, so it is for the Muslim. Muhammad said: This is also the view of Abu Yusuf, and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Yusuf that the slave is half and half between them. End. His statement: (So-and-so) is a substitute for the judge. His statement: (And if one who was upright gave false testimony, then repented, etc.) The one known for uprightness, if he gives false testimony, according to Abu Yusuf his testimony is never accepted because his repentance is not known, and Faqih Abu Ja'far narrated that his testimony is accepted, and reliance is upon it, as in al-Khaniyya before the section on tazkiya and ta'dil. His statement: (It is not appropriate to inform of his immorality) apparently the meaning is that it is not permissible. And in al-Khaniyya: If a witness is immoral in secret while outwardly upright, and the judge wants to judge based on his testimony, and the witness informs about himself that he is not upright, his admission against himself is valid, except that if he is truthful in his testimony, it is not permissible for him to inform about himself that he is not upright because it invalidates the claimant's right. End.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on testimony, starting with the ruling for a Harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory). The testimony of a Harbi (specifically a musta'min) is accepted against another Harbi but not against a Dhimmi because there is no legal authority (wilaya) over the Dhimmi. An exception is made for Harbis from different abodes (dar) like Franks and Abyssinians, as they lack mutual authority and do not inherit from each other.

The passage then discusses the condition of 'adala (integrity) for witnesses. The key principle is that one who commits minor sins is still acceptable if he avoids major sins. 'Adala is defined as uprightness through Islam and soundness of mind, and its minimum is accepted to avoid loss of rights. Abu Yusuf's definition is given: avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, and manifest chivalry (muru'a). Additional qualities from al-Muhit and al-Walwalijiyya include truthfulness, chastity, and wealth to avoid temptation.

The text then addresses repentance of a fasiq (immoral person): his testimony is not accepted until a period passes demonstrating his repentance, though the exact duration is delegated to the judge. However, if an originally upright person gives false testimony and repents, his testimony is accepted immediately per one narration. A witness who is secretly immoral should not reveal his own immorality if it would void a valid claim.

Finally, the testimony of an uncircumcised adult (aqlaf) is accepted because circumcision is only a sunnah in the Hanafi school, not a condition of 'adala. It is restricted: it must not be due to contempt for religion, and if left out of fear, it is acceptable.

Key Terms
الحربي (al-harbi): A non-Muslim from enemy territory; here specifically the musta'min (one under safe conduct).
الدار (al-dar): Legal territory/abode; a dar is defined by the predominant ruling power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason a musta'min's testimony is not accepted against a Dhimmi?
A) The Dhimmi is a Muslim, so his word prevails.
B) The musta'min has no authority (wilaya) over the Dhimmi.
C) Testimony between non-Muslims is always rejected.
D) The musta'min is not a trustworthy person.

Key Takeaway
A musta'min's testimony is accepted only against another musta'min from the same abode; otherwise it is rejected.

Shahadat — Testimony

Conditions of Adala for Witnesses
Definition and conditions of adala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of adala (integrity) and apply it to scenarios involving minor sins, major sins, and repentance.

Core Idea
Adala requires avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins; its minimum is enough to preserve rights.

This section of the passage delves into the condition of 'adala (uprightness) required for a witness. It provides a practical definition based on the statements of Abu Yusuf and other Hanafi authorities, and discusses exceptions for minor sins, repentance, and secret immorality.

Guided Path
1
Define adala
The passage gives Abu Yusuf's definition: avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, and manifest chivalry (muru'a). It is the preponderance of religion and intellect over desire.
No fixed upper limit; minimum is accepted to avoid loss of rights.
2
Identify the effect of minor sins
Committing minor sins does not negate adala, provided the person avoids all major sins. Persistence in minor sins (israr) does negate adala.
Israr means continuing in minor sins without repentance.
3
Apply repentance rules
If a fasiq (immoral person) repents, his testimony is not accepted until a period demonstrating sincerity passes (delegated to judge). However, if an originally upright person gives false testimony and repents, his testimony is accepted immediately (according to the relied-upon narration of Abu Ja'far).
Abu Yusuf's view: never accepted. The mufta bihi is immediate acceptance.
4
Handle secret immorality
If a witness is secretly immoral but outwardly upright, he should not reveal his own immorality because it would invalidate the claimant's right.
This is a case of not harming the claimant.

Commentary

Key Terms
العدالة (al-adala): Integrity/uprightness of a witness: avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, manifest chivalry, truthfulness.
الإصرار (al-israr): Persistence in a sin by repeatedly committing it without repentance.

According to the passage, what is the ruling on the testimony of a person who was originally upright, gave false testimony, and then repented?
A) His testimony is never accepted.

Testimony of the Uncircumcised Adult (Aqlaf)
Ruling on testimony of uncircumcised adult

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accepting testimony from an uncircumcised adult, identify the restrictions, and evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Circumcision is sunnah, not wajib; omission does not affect adala unless done out of contempt.

This final part of the passage addresses the special case of the aqlaf (uncircumcised adult). It confirms the Hanafi position that such a witness is acceptable because circumcision is not a condition of adala. However, restrictions are added: if he leaves it out of contempt, his testimony is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness
The aqlaf is an adult male who has not been circumcised. The Hanafi school generally accepts his testimony.
Circumcision is considered sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
State the Hanafi position
The testimony is accepted because adala is not undermined by leaving circumcision, since it is sunnah in the Hanafi school.
This is the plain ruling from the matn.
3
Apply the restrictions
Qadikhan restricted acceptance to cases where he leaves it due to fear (e.g., for health). Al-Hidaya restricts it to cases where he does not leave it out of contempt for religion. If he leaves it out of contempt, the testimony is rejected.
These restrictions ensure the behavior is not a sign of religious disregard.
4
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school considers circumcision wajib and necessary for adala, so they would reject the testimony of an uncircumcised adult. This is a key point of ikhtilaf.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is in the acceptance of testimony.

حق المدعي اهـ.
...they were. His statement: (And the Harbi against his like) i.e., his testimony is accepted against his like, not against the Dhimmi, because he has no authority over the Dhimmi. And the intended meaning of Harbi is the musta'min (one given safe conduct), because nothing else is conceivable. For if a Harbi enters without safe conduct, then it is enslavement and there is no testimony for slaves against anyone. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And an exception is made from the Harbi against his like in the case of two different abodes like the Franks and the Abyssinians, due to the lack of authority between them, and for this reason they do not inherit from each other, and the abode differs by strength and kingship. His statement: (And whoever does a minor sin if he avoids major sins) i.e., the testimony of one who commits a minor sin is accepted if he avoids all major sins. And he indicated here 'adala (integrity), which is a condition for acceptance of testimony, and it is uprightness, and it is through Islam and soundness of mind, and it is opposed by desire that misguides and prevents him. And its perfection has no limit that can be reached, and the minimum sufficing for acceptance is taken so that rights are not lost. It is the preponderance of the aspect of religion and intellect over desire and lust. And the best said about it is what is from Abu Yusuf: The upright person is one who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and whose chivalry is apparent, so its absence destroys it. And in al-Muhit it added: he should be accustomed to truthfulness and avoid lying in religion and chivalry. And in al-Walwalijiyya: It is recommended that the witness be older, chaste, wealthy, virtuous; because if he is so, he does not covet people's wealth and is ashamed of committing what is unlawful in Shari'a, so he is more deserving of being taken as a witness. End. And by this it is known whom the judge appoints as witness among the people. And in al-Khaniyya: If an immoral person repents, his testimony is not accepted until a time passes in which repentance appears; then some scholars estimated it as six months, some as a year, and the correct view is that it is delegated to the opinion of the judge and the one who declares uprightness. End. And in al-Khulasa: If one was upright and gave false testimony, then repented and testifies, it is accepted without any time period. End. And we previously stated that if a witness is secretly immoral, he should not inform of his immorality so as not to invalidate the claimant's right, and this was explicitly stated in al-Umda as well. And in al-Atabiyya: One who rents out his house to someone who sells wine, his uprightness is not nullified. His statement: (And the aqlaf) i.e., the adult who has not been circumcised, his testimony is accepted because uprightness is not undermined by leaving circumcision since it is sunnah in our school. It is unrestricted, but Qadikhan restricted it to one who leaves it due to fear for himself; but if he leaves it without excuse, it is not accepted. And in al-Hidaya it is restricted to one who does not leave it out of contempt for religion; if he leaves it out of contempt, his testimony is not accepted because he is no longer upright. And just as his testimony is accepted, his leading of prayer is valid. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the Imam did not set a known time for circumcision due to lack of... two Christian witnesses, so it is for the Muslim. Muhammad said: This is also the view of Abu Yusuf, and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Yusuf that the slave is half and half between them. End. His statement: (So-and-so) is a substitute for the judge. His statement: (And if one who was upright gave false testimony, then repented, etc.) The one known for uprightness, if he gives false testimony, according to Abu Yusuf his testimony is never accepted because his repentance is not known, and Faqih Abu Ja'far narrated that his testimony is accepted, and reliance is upon it, as in al-Khaniyya before the section on tazkiya and ta'dil. His statement: (It is not appropriate to inform of his immorality) apparently the meaning is that it is not permissible. And in al-Khaniyya: If a witness is immoral in secret while outwardly upright, and the judge wants to judge based on his testimony, and the witness informs about himself that he is not upright, his admission against himself is valid, except that if he is truthful in his testimony, it is not permissible for him to inform about himself that he is not upright because it invalidates the claimant's right. End.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on testimony, starting with the ruling for a Harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory). The testimony of a Harbi (specifically a musta'min) is accepted against another Harbi but not against a Dhimmi because there is no legal authority (wilaya) over the Dhimmi. An exception is made for Harbis from different abodes (dar) like Franks and Abyssinians, as they lack mutual authority and do not inherit from each other.

The passage then discusses the condition of 'adala (integrity) for witnesses. The key principle is that one who commits minor sins is still acceptable if he avoids major sins. 'Adala is defined as uprightness through Islam and soundness of mind, and its minimum is accepted to avoid loss of rights. Abu Yusuf's definition is given: avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, and manifest chivalry (muru'a). Additional qualities from al-Muhit and al-Walwalijiyya include truthfulness, chastity, and wealth to avoid temptation.

The text then addresses repentance of a fasiq (immoral person): his testimony is not accepted until a period passes demonstrating his repentance, though the exact duration is delegated to the judge. However, if an originally upright person gives false testimony and repents, his testimony is accepted immediately per one narration. A witness who is secretly immoral should not reveal his own immorality if it would void a valid claim.

Finally, the testimony of an uncircumcised adult (aqlaf) is accepted because circumcision is only a sunnah in the Hanafi school, not a condition of 'adala. It is restricted: it must not be due to contempt for religion, and if left out of fear, it is acceptable.

Key Terms
الأقلف (al-aqlaf): An adult male who has not been circumcised.
الختان (al-khitan): Circumcision; a practice considered sunnah in Hanafi and wajib in Shafi'i school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is accepted, because circumcision is sunnah.
B) It is not accepted, because he is no longer upright.
C) It is accepted only after he repents.
D) It is accepted if he fears for his health.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an uncircumcised adult may testify, except when the omission is due to contempt for religion.

Testimony of a Harbi Against His Like
Ruling on the testimony of a harbi musta'min

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a harbi musta'min's testimony is accepted in Hanafi fiqh and identify the exception when testimony is rejected.

Core Idea
A harbi musta'min’s testimony is accepted only against another harbi from the same territory.

The testimony of non-Muslims is a nuanced area of Islamic jurisprudence. The Hanafi school specifies that a harbi (specifically a musta'min) can testify only against another harbi from the same territory (dar). This ruling hinges on the concept of legal authority (wilaya) and the practical relationship between the parties. Let's explore the conditions and the exception for different territories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testifier
The text says 'al-harbi' but clarifies that the intended meaning is the musta'min, because a harbi without aman would be enslaved and thus ineligible.
Harbi in this context is not the original enemy combatant, but a temporary resident with aman.
2
Determine against whom testimony is accepted
His testimony is accepted 'against his like' (i.e., another harbi), not against a dhimmi or a Muslim, because he has no authority over them.
The reason cited is lack of wilaya over the dhimmi.
3
Recognize the condition of same dar
The harbi must be from the same dar (territory) as the person he testifies against. If they are from different dar (e.g., Franks vs. Abyssinians), the testimony is rejected due to severed authority.
The dar differs based on protection and dominion (al-mun'a wal-mulk).
4
Note the exception for different dar
The text explicitly states an exception: when the two are from different dar, the testimony is not accepted. This is because there is no mutual inheritance or authority between such territories.
This exception reinforces the principle of wilaya as the basis for testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والحربي على مثله أي وتقبل شهادته على مثله لا على الذمي لأنه لا ولاية له على الذمي. والمراد بالحربي المستأمن لأنه لا يتصور غيره فإن الحربي لو دخل بلا أمان فهذا استرقاق ولا شهادة للعبيد على أحد ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ويستثنى من الحربي على مثله ما إذا من دارين مختلفين كالإفرنج والحبس لانقطاع الولاية بينهما ولهذا لا يتوارثان والدار تختلف باختلاف المنعة والملك
His saying: 'And the harbi (non-Muslim from dar al-harb) against his like' means his testimony is accepted against his like, not against a dhimmi because he has no authority over the dhimmi. And what is meant by 'harbi' is the musta'min (one who has been granted aman) because no other is conceivable, for if a harbi enters without aman, then he is subject to enslavement and there is no testimony for slaves against anyone; so in Fath al-Qadir. And an exception from the harbi against his like is when they are from two different dar (territories) like the Franks and the Abyssinians, due to the cessation of authority between them, and for this reason they do not inherit from each other, and the dar differs according to protection and dominion.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It clarifies the testimony of a harbi, specifically a musta'min (harbi given temporary safe passage). His testimony is accepted only against another harbi, not against a dhimmi, because he has no legal authority (wilaya) over a dhimmi. If a harbi enters without aman, he becomes a slave, and slaves' testimony is rejected. An exception is made when the harbi and the party he testifies against are from different dar (e.g., Franks vs. Abyssinians), because there is no mutual authority or inheritance between such territories.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under Islamic rule and not granted aman; but in this context, it specifically refers to a musta'min (one given safe passage).
مستأمن (musta'min): A harbi who has been granted aman (safe passage) to enter Islamic territory temporarily.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim permanently residing under Islamic rule with a covenant of protection.
دار (dar): Territory; dar al-harb vs. dar al-Islam. Here it refers to different political entities like Franks and Abyssinians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Against a dhimmi
B) Against another harbi from the same dar
C) Against any Muslim
D) Against a slave

Key Takeaway
A harbi musta'min can testify only against another harbi from the same territory, due to the principle of legal authority (wilaya).

Testimony of One Who Commits Minor Sins
Conditions for accepting testimony despite minor sins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a witness's 'adala and apply them to scenarios involving minor sins and repentance.

Core Idea
A witness's testimony is accepted if he avoids major sins and does not persist in minor sins; repentance requires a judge-determined period.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key issue in Islamic evidence law: when is the testimony of a person who commits sins acceptable? The Hanafi school distinguishes between major and minor sins, and defines moral uprightness ('adala) as avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, and having apparent decency (muru'a). The commentary also discusses the repentance of a sinner and the judge's role in determining the waiting period for testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states that the testimony of one who commits minor sins is accepted if he avoids all major sins. This establishes the baseline: minor sins do not automatically disqualify.
The key is avoiding major sins (kaba'ir) entirely.
2
Define 'Adala per Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf's definition: the 'adl (upright witness) avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and has apparent muru'a. Muru'a includes honesty, propriety, and not engaging in disgraceful behavior.
Persistence (israr) on minor sins is equivalent to committing major sins.
3
Apply the Rule to Repentance
A fasiq (sinner) who repents must wait a period for his repentance to become evident. Some scholars said 6 months, others 1 year; the correct view is that it is left to the judge's discretion. However, if the person was previously 'adl and then testified falsely and repents, his testimony is accepted immediately.
The judge evaluates the sincerity of repentance.
4
Note the Exception
Renting a house to a wine seller does not nullify 'adala, as per al-Atabiyya. This shows that not every contact with sin destroys uprightness.
The 'adala is judged by the witness's own actions, not those of others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ومن ألم بصغيرة إن اجتنب الكبائر) أي تقبل شهادة من ارتكب صغيرة إن اجتنب الكبائر كلها وقد أشار هنا إلى العدالة فإنها شرط قبول الشهادة وهي الاستقامة وهي بالإسلام واعتدال العقل ويعارضه هوى يضله ويصده، وليس لكمالها حد يدرك مداه ويكتفى لقبولها بأدناه كيلا يضيع الحقوق وهو رجحان جهة الدين والعقل على الهوى والشهوة وأحسن ما قيل فيه ما عن أبي يوسف العدل أن يكون مجتنباً للكبائر غير مصر على الصغائر وأن تكون مروءته ظاهرة فعدمها مفوت لها وزاد في المحيط أن يعتاد الصدق ويجتنب الكذب ديانة ومروءته. وفي الولوالجية : وينبغي أن يكون الشاهد مسناً عفيفاً ذا مال ذا فضل لأنه إذا كان كذلك لا يطمع في أموال الناس ويستحي من ارتكاب ما لا يحل في الشرع فكان أولى بالاستشهاد ا.هـ. وبه يعلم من ينصبه القاضي شاهداً. بین الناس. وفي الخانية : الفاسق إذا تاب لا تقبل شهادته ما لم يمض عليه زمان تظهر التوبة ثم بعضهم قدره بستة أشهر وبعضهم قدره بسنة والصحيح أن ذلك مفوض إلى رأي القاضي والمعدل ا هـ. وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان عدلاً فشهد بزور ثم تاب فشهد تقبل من غير مدة ا هـ. وقدمنا أن الشاهد إذا كان فاسقاً سراً لا ينبغي أن يخبر بفسقه كيلا يبطل حق المدعي وصرح به في العمدة أيضاً. وفي العتابية من أجر بيته لمن يبيع الخمر لم تسقط عدالته
His saying: '(And whoever is afflicted with a minor sin, if he avoids major sins)' means the testimony of one who commits a minor sin is accepted if he avoids all major sins. And here he points to 'adala (moral uprightness), which is a condition for accepting testimony. It is uprightness, which consists of Islam and soundness of intellect, being opposed by desires that mislead and prevent him. There is no limit to its perfection that can be grasped, and the minimum is sufficient for acceptance so that rights are not lost. It is the preponderance of the aspect of religion and intellect over desire and passion. The best expression is from Abu Yusuf: 'The 'adl is one who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and whose muru'a (decency) is apparent; its absence forfeits it.' And al-Muhit added: 'He should be accustomed to truthfulness and avoid lying in his religion and muru'a.' In al-Walwalijiyya: 'It is fitting that the witness be elderly, chaste, wealthy, and virtuous, because if he is so, he will not covet people's wealth and will be ashamed of committing what is unlawful in the Shari'a, so he is more deserving to be chosen as a witness.' End. By this, it is known whom the judge should appoint as a witness among people. In al-Khaniyya: 'If a fasiq (sinner) repents, his testimony is not accepted until a time passes in which his repentance becomes apparent; some estimated it as six months, others as a year; the correct view is that this is left to the opinion of the judge and the one who evaluates witnesses.' End. In al-Khulasa: 'If one was 'adl and then testified falsely and then repented and testifies, it is accepted without any period.' End. And we have already stated that if a witness is secretly fasiq, he should not inform about his fisq so as not to nullify the right of the claimant; it is explicitly stated in al-Umda as well. In al-Atabiyya: 'One who rents his house to someone who sells wine, his 'adala is not nullified.'
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with additional details on 'adala (moral uprightness). The matn states that testimony is accepted from one who commits minor sins as long as he avoids major sins. The commentary expands on the definition of 'adala from Abu Yusuf: avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, and having apparent muru'a. It also discusses repentance of a fasiq: some require a period (6 months or a year) for repentance to be evident, but the correct view is that it is left to the judge's discretion. For a person who was 'adl and then testified falsely and repented, his testimony is accepted immediately without waiting period. A secretly fasiq witness should not expose himself to protect the plaintiff's right. Renting a house to a wine seller does not nullify 'adala.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adala): Moral uprightness: avoiding major sins, not persisting in minor sins, and having apparent muru'a (decency). It is a condition for witness acceptance.
مروءة (muru'a): Decency and propriety; a witness must have apparent muru'a, which includes honesty and avoidance of disreputable behavior.
صغيرة (saghira): A minor sin. Persistence on it or committing major sins nullifies 'adala.
كبيرة (kabira): A major sin. Avoiding major sins is a necessary condition for 'adala.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must avoid major sins and not persist in minor sins.
C) He must be elderly and wealthy.
D) He must never have committed a sin.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from one who commits minor sins if he avoids major sins and does not persist; the judge determines the period for repentance.

Testimony of the Uncircumcised Adult: Hanafi Conditions for Acceptance
Ruling on testimony of uncircumcised adult with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony from an uncircumcised adult and identify the conditions that affect its acceptance.

Core Idea
Circumcision is sunnah, so testimony is accepted unless left out of contempt or without excuse.

The Hanafi school holds that an uncircumcised adult is generally a qualified witness because circumcision is sunnah, not fard. However, this default is qualified by conditions: if he leaves it out of contempt for religion or without a valid excuse, his testimony is rejected. This passage also addresses the age of circumcision and the opposing view of Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
State the default Hanafi ruling
Identify the basic ruling from the matn: testimony of an uncircumcised adult is accepted because circumcision is sunnah and does not affect 'adala.
The default is acceptance, not rejection.
2
Identify conditions from Qadikhan and Al-Hidayah
Qadikhan restricts acceptance to those who leave circumcision out of fear (e.g., medical reason). Al-Hidayah adds that if left out of contempt for religion, testimony is rejected.
These conditions modify the general ruling; they are not contradictory but supplementary.
3
Compare with Ibn Abbas's absolute rejection
Ibn Abbas completely rejected the testimony and slaughter of an uncircumcised person. The Hanafi school accepts both conditionally.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with a companion.
4
Understand the practical application of excuses
An excuse (e.g., fear of harm) preserves 'adala; without it, the witness is not reliable. Contempt for religion breaks 'adala entirely.
The mufta bihi position is that testimony is accepted if there is an excuse.
5
Note the additional benefit about adult circumcision
If an adult can circumcise himself, he must; otherwise he may hire a circumciser or go to a bath attendant.
This is a separate ruling but related to the same topic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والأقلف) أي الكبير الذي لم يختتن تقبل شهادته لأن العدالة لا تخل بترك الختان لكونه سنة عندنا. أطلقه وقيده قاضيخان بأن يتركه لخوف على نفسه، أما إذا تركه بغير عذر لم تقبل. وقيده في الهداية بأن لا يتركه استخفافاً بالدين أما إذا تركه استخفافاً لم تقبل شهادته لأنه لم يبق عدلاً وكما تقبل شهادته تصح إمامته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولم يقدر الإمام للختان وقتاً معلوماً لعدم ورود النص به وقدره المتأخرون واختلفوا والمختار أن أول وقته سبع سنين وآخره اثنتا عشر ؛ كذا في الخلاصة من باب اليمين في الطلاق وقدمنا في أول الطهارة أنه سنة للرجال مكرمة للنساء إذ جماع المختونة ألذ قال الحلواني : كان النساء يختتن في زمن أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وفي النوازل أن ابن عباس كان لا يجيز شهادة الأقلف ولا ذبيحته، وعلماؤنا قالوا تؤكل ذبيحته وتقبل شهادته إن كان لعذر وإلا لا تقبل وبه نأخذ ا هـ . فائدة من كراهية فتاوى العتابي وقيل في ختان الكبير إذا أمكن أن يختن نفسه فعل وإلا لم يفعل إلا أن يمكنه أن يتزوج أو يشتري ختانة فتختنه . وذكر الكرخي في الكبير يختنه الحمامي وكذا عن ابن مقاتل لا بأس للحمامي أن يطلي عورة غيره بالنورة ا هـ
His saying: '(And the aqlaf)' i.e., the adult who has not been circumcised, his testimony is accepted because 'adala is not harmed by leaving circumcision since it is sunnah in our school. It was unrestricted and Qadikhan restricted it to one who leaves it out of fear for himself; but if he leaves it without an excuse, it is not accepted. Al-Hidayah restricted it to one who does not leave it out of contempt for religion; but if he leaves it out of contempt, his testimony is not accepted because he is no longer 'adl. Just as his testimony is accepted, his leading prayer is valid; so in Fath al-Qadir. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) did not set a specific time for circumcision due to the absence of a text; later scholars estimated and differed, and the chosen view is that its earliest time is seven years and its latest twelve; so in al-Khulasa from the chapter of oaths in divorce. And we have stated earlier at the beginning of tahara that it is sunnah for men and an honor for women, because intercourse with a circumcised woman is more pleasurable. Al-Halwani said: 'Women used to be circumcised at the time of the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him.' In al-Nawazil: Ibn Abbas did not accept the testimony of an uncircumcised person nor his slaughtered meat, but our scholars said: 'His slaughtered meat is eaten and his testimony is accepted if he has an excuse; otherwise it is not accepted, and we take this view.' End. Benefit: From the disliked rulings of al-Atabi, it is said regarding the circumcision of an adult: if he can circumcise himself, he does; otherwise he does not, unless he can marry or buy a circumciser to circumcise him. Al-Karkhi mentioned that the adult can be circumcised by the bath attendant, and similarly from Ibn Muqatil: there is no harm for the bath attendant to apply depilatory to the private parts of another. End.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with conditions. The matn states that the testimony of an uncircumcised adult (aqlaf) is accepted because circumcision is sunnah, not fard, so leaving it does not break 'adala. However, Qadikhan restricts it to one who leaves it out of fear (e.g., medical reason); without excuse, testimony is rejected. Al-Hidayah adds: if he leaves it out of contempt for religion, his testimony is rejected because he loses 'adala. The commentary also discusses the age for circumcision: the preferred time is between 7 and 12 years, though no explicit text sets it. The passage also mentions that Ibn Abbas did not accept testimony or slaughtered meat of an uncircumcised person, but Hanafis accept the meat and testimony if there is an excuse. A fā'ida (benefit) discusses circumcision of an adult: he must do it if possible; otherwise he may hire a circumciser, and a bath attendant may assist.

Key Terms
أقلف (aqlaf): An adult male who has not been circumcised.
ختان (khitan): Circumcision; for men it is sunnah, for women it is honorable (makruma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Hidayah, when is the testimony of an uncircumcised adult rejected?
A) When he leaves circumcision out of fear for himself
B) When he leaves circumcision without any excuse
C) When he leaves circumcision out of contempt for religion
D) Always

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of testimony from an uncircumcised adult depends on whether the omission is due to a valid excuse or contempt; with an excuse, it is accepted; without, it is rejected.

Testimony of Eunuch, Child of Zina, and Hermaphrodite
Acceptance of testimony from eunuch, illegitimate child, and hermaphrodite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of a eunuch, a child of zina, and a hermaphrodite, and apply the ruling that a hermaphrodite is treated as a woman in testimony.

Core Idea
Eunuch, child of zina, and hermaphrodite are accepted; the hermaphrodite counts as a woman for testimony.

In Hanafi law, certain potential witnesses raise questions: does physical alteration (eunuch), illegitimate birth, or ambiguous gender disqualify them? This passage clarifies that none of these factors prevent testimony, based on the practice of Umar (ra) and legal analogy. Understanding these rulings ensures correct application of shahada in diverse circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: testimony of a eunuch, a child of zina, and a hermaphrodite is accepted. Note that the hermaphrodite is treated as a woman (i.e., two such witnesses equal one man).
2
Examine the proof for the eunuch
The text cites the action of Umar (ra) accepting the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch, and draws an analogy: removal of testicles unjustly is like removal of a hand, which does not disqualify.
The eunuch is not at fault; the legal capacity for testimony remains.
3
Examine the proof for the child of zina
The sin of the parents does not transfer to the child, just as disbelief of parents does not make the child a disbeliever. Thus the child's 'adala (integrity) is unaffected by birth status.
This principle is general, including testimony about zina itself.
4
Identify the disputed point
Imam Malik differs regarding a child of zina testifying in a zina case. The Hanafi position rejects this restriction, maintaining the unrestricted acceptance.
The dispute is recorded as 'khilafan li Malik fi al-awwal'.
5
Apply the hermaphrodite ruling
The ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) is legally considered a woman for testimony. Therefore, two such witnesses are required where two women are needed, and one equals half a male witness.
This is based on the principle of treating gender ambiguity in a cautionary manner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والخصي وولد الزنا والخنثى فإن عمر رضي الله عنه قبل شهادة علقمة الخصي ولأنه قطع عضو منه ظلماً فصار كما إذا قطعت يده والخصي بفتح الخاء على وزن فعيل منزوع البناية. وفسق الأبوين لا يوجب فسق الولد ككفرهما . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا شهد بالزنا في أو بغيره خلافاً لمالك في الأول. والمراد بالخنثى المشكل وهو امرأة في الشهادة؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج
His saying: '(And the eunuch, the child of zina, and the hermaphrodite)' - for Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch, and because a limb of his was removed unjustly, so he is like one whose hand was cut off. Al-Khasi (eunuch) is with a fatha on the kha', on the measure of fa'il, deprived of testicles. And the sin of the two parents does not necessitate the sin of the child, just like their disbelief. He gave it unrestrictedly, so it includes whether he testifies about zina or other than it, contrary to Malik in the first case. And what is meant by al-khuntha al-mushkil (ambiguous hermaphrodite) is that he is considered a woman in testimony; so in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof from the practice of Umar (ra) who accepted testimony of Alqamah the eunuch. The reasoning is that a eunuch has had a limb unjustly removed, similar to one with a cut hand. The child of zina is not burdened by the sin of his parents, just as he is not considered a disbeliever due to their disbelief, so his testimony is accepted. The matn is general, including testimony about zina itself, which differs from Malik who does not accept the testimony of a child of zina in zina cases. The hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) is considered a woman for the purpose of testimony, meaning he is treated as a female witness (two women equal one man).

Key Terms
خصي (khasi): A eunuch, one whose testicles have been removed.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): Child born out of wedlock; his testimony is accepted because his parents' sin does not affect his 'adala.
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose gender is ambiguous; for testimony, such a person is considered a woman (i.e., two such witnesses equal one man).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is a hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) treated in testimony?
A) As a man
B) As a woman
C) His testimony is rejected
D) He is considered a slave

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law accepts testimony of a eunuch, child of zina, and hermaphrodite, treating the hermaphrodite as a woman; the child's parents' sin does not affect his 'adala.
