Testimony of Workers: Conditions and the Lowly Profession Debate
Ruling statement with intra-madhhab debate and author's tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of workers, identify the conditions for acceptance, and explain why lowly profession does not disqualify if the witness is 'adl.

Core Idea
Workers' testimony is accepted unless they assist injustice; lowly profession alone does not disqualify if the witness is trustworthy.

The testimony of workers (al-ummal) is a nuanced area in Hanafi fiqh. The term can refer to government employees or manual laborers. While some earlier scholars restricted testimony based on profession or lineage, the relied-upon view emphasizes 'adala (integrity) over occupation. This lesson unpacks the conditions and the intra-madhhab debate about lowly professions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of 'workers'
Determine the two primary interpretations: government employees (workers of the sultan) vs. manual laborers. Understand that both are accepted unless they are helpers in injustice.
The text mentions two opinions: majority shaykhs favor sultan's workers; another view includes all hired laborers.
2
State the conditions for acceptance
List the conditions discussed: not assisting in injustice, having muru'a, profession should be suitable to lineage (according to some), and not frequently lying or breaking promises.
The author critiques the lineage condition later, but it appears in the earlier quoted views.
3
Analyze the debate on lowly professions
Examine the restriction that one who adopts a base profession (hirfa daniya) loses muru'a and thus testimony is rejected. Then study the counter-argument: if the person is 'adl, profession is irrelevant, especially if he was raised in that trade.
The author (Ibn Nujaym) sides with al-Ramli: 'adala is the criterion, not profession.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Conclude that the relied-upon view is acceptance of testimony from any worker who is 'adl, regardless of the lowliness of the profession, unless there is clear evidence of lack of 'adala.
This is supported by the author's final argument and the phrase 'so our conclusion is confirmed'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعمال) أي تقبل شهادتهم، والمراد عمال السلطان عند عامة المشايخ لأن نفس العمل ليس بفسق إلا إذا كانوا أعواناً على الظلم. وقيل: العامل إذا كان وجيهاً في الناس ذا مروءة لا يجازف في كلامه تقبل شهادته كما مر عن أبي يوسف في الفاسق لوجاهته لا يقدم على الكذب كذا في الهداية. يعني ولو كان عوناً على الظلم كما في العناية . وقيل : أراد بالعمال الذين يعملون ويؤاجرون أنفسهم للعمل لأن من الناس من رد شهادات أهل الصناعات الخسيسة فأفرد هذه المسألة لإظهار مخالفتهم وكيف لا وكسبهم أطيب كسب. وينبغي تقييد القبول بأن تكون تلك الحرفة لائقة به بأن تكون حرفة آبائه وأجداده وإلا فلا مروءة له إذا كانت حرفة دنية فلا شهادة له لما عرف في حد العدالة . ينبغي تقييد القبول بأن لا يكثر الكذب والخلف في الوعد. وذكر الصدر الشهيد أن شهادة الرئيس لا تقبل وكذا الجابي والصراف الذي يجمع عنده الدراهم ويأخذها طوعاً لا تقبل. وقدمنا عن البزدوي أن القائم بتوزيع هذه النوائب السلطانية والجبابات بالعدل بين المسلمين وكذا قوله : ( وينبغي تقييد القبول الخ قال الرملي وعندي في هذا التقييد نظر يظهر لمن له نظر فتأمل اهـ . قلت : وجهه ما مر عند قوله أو يبول أو يأكل أن الصحيح قبول ذي الحرفة الدنية إذا كان عدلاً فحيث كان المعتبر العدالة فلا نظر إلى الحرفة نعم قد يقال عدوله عن حرفة آبائه الشريفة إلى الحرفة الخسيسة يدل على رذالته وعدم مروءته ومبالاته لكن هذا حيث كان بلا داع إليه من عجز أو عدم أسباب أو قله يد تقصره عن حرفة أبيه ولا سيما إذا كان أبوه أو وصيه علمه في صغره هذه الحرفة الدنية فكبر وهو لا يعرف غيرها، فإذا كان عدلاً فما وجه رد شهادته؟ فتعين ما قلنا تأمل
His saying: '(And the workers)' i.e., their testimony is accepted. What is meant by 'workers' is the workers of the sultan according to the majority of the shaykhs, because the work itself is not fisq (sin) unless they are helpers in injustice. And it is said: The worker, if he is influential among people, having muru'a, not reckless in his speech, his testimony is accepted, as passed from Abu Yusuf about the fasiq, because his influence prevents him from lying; so in al-Hidayah. Meaning even if he is a helper in injustice, as in al-Inaya. And it is said: What is meant by 'workers' is those who work and hire themselves out for labor, because among people there are those who reject the testimony of those in base professions; so this issue is singled out to show opposition to them, and why not? Since their earning is the purest earning. It is necessary to restrict acceptance to when that profession is suitable for him, i.e., it is the profession of his fathers and forefathers; otherwise, he has no muru'a if it is a lowly profession, so his testimony is not accepted, as known in the definition of 'adala. It is also necessary to restrict acceptance to when he does not frequently lie or break promises. Al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned that the testimony of a president is not accepted, nor is that of a tax collector (jabi) or a money changer (sarraf) who collects dirhams and takes them voluntarily. And we have already mentioned from al-Bazdawi that one who distributes these sultanial taxes and collections justly among the Muslims... Also his saying: ('And it is necessary to restrict acceptance, etc.') al-Ramli said: 'In my view there is consideration in this restriction; it is apparent to one who considers, so contemplate.' End. I say: Its justification is what passed at his saying 'or he urinates or eats' that the correct view is acceptance of one of a lowly profession if he is 'adl. So where 'adala is considered, there is no regard for profession. Yes, it may be said that his turning away from the noble profession of his fathers to a base profession indicates his wickedness and lack of muru'a and carelessness, but this is when there is no necessity like inability, lack of means, or limited ability that prevents him from his father's profession, especially if his father or guardian taught him this base profession in his childhood and he grew up knowing nothing else. So if he is 'adl, what justification is there to reject his testimony? So our conclusion is confirmed; contemplate.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about accepting testimony of workers (al-ummal). The primary interpretation is that it refers to government employees (workers of the sultan) because their work is not inherently sinful unless they assist in injustice. Another interpretation is that it refers to manual laborers, whose earnings are pure, countering those who reject testimony of lowly professions. The commentary discusses conditions: the profession should be suitable to one's lineage; otherwise, if one adopts a base profession without excuse, it may indicate lack of muru'a. However, the author (Ibn Nujaym) critiques this restriction, quoting al-Ramli, and argues that if the person is 'adl, his profession should not matter, especially if he was raised in that profession. Al-Sadr al-Shahid rejects testimony of certain officials like presidents, tax collectors, and money changers, but al-Bazdawi exempts those who distribute justly.

Key Terms
عمال ('ummal): Workers; primarily government employees or laborers hired for work.
حرفة دنية (hirfa daniya): Lowly or base profession; some restrict testimony if one adopts a lowly profession without excuse.
مروءة (muru'a): Social dignity, integrity, and respectable conduct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding testimony of someone in a lowly profession?
A) It is never accepted
B) It is accepted only if the profession suits his lineage
C) It is accepted if he is 'adl regardless of profession
D) It is accepted only for sultan's workers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from any worker, regardless of profession, if the witness is 'adl and does not assist in injustice.

Shahadat — Testimony

Acceptance of Testimony from Five Categories: Eunuchs, Illegitimate Children, Hermaphrodites, Workers, and Freed Slaves
Commentary expanding on five categories whose testimony is accepted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings regarding the testimony of eunuchs, illegitimate children, hermaphrodites, workers, and freed slaves, and identify the conditions and proofs for each.

Core Idea
External status does not disqualify a witness; probity (adala) is the key.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on five categories whose testimony the Hanafi school accepts. For each category, the author provides proofs from the practice of the Companions and analogies, and discusses internal disagreements. We will examine each category's ruling, proof, and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories and general ruling
List the five types: eunuch, illegitimate child, hermaphrodite, workers, freed slave. For each, the ruling is that their testimony is accepted (maqbul) unless specific disqualifiers exist.
The text begins with 'والخصي وولد الزنا والخنثى والعمال والمعتق للمعتق'.
2
Analyze the proof for the eunuch
The proof is Umar's acceptance of Alqamah's testimony and a qiyas to amputation of hand. Note the dispute with Malik regarding zina.
The qiyas panel in the analysis illustrates the reasoning.
3
Understand the ruling for illegitimate child
The sin of the parents does not taint the child. Testimony is accepted subject to general conditions of probity.
Key phrase: 'وفسق الأبوين لا يوجب فسق الولد'.
4
Define the hermaphrodite
The ambiguous hermaphrodite is considered a woman in testimony, so her testimony has the legal weight of a woman's testimony.
The text says: 'وهو امرأة في الشهادة'.
5
Examine the conditions for workers
Testimony of workers is accepted unless they assist in injustice. There is an intra-Hanafi difference on the effect of lowly profession.
Al-Ramli argues that probity alone suffices regardless of profession.
6
Determine the condition for freed slaves
Testimony of a freed slave for his manumitter is accepted unless there is tuhma (suspicion of bias). Shuraih accepted Qanbar's testimony for Ali.
The condition is absence of tuhma; testifying to establish manumission for own benefit is rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل والخصي وولد الزنا والخنثى والعمال والمعتق للمعتق ولو شهد أن أباهما أوصى إليه ورد النص به وقدره المتأخرون واختلفوا والمختار أن أول وقته سبع سنين وآخره اثنتا عشر ؛ كذا في الخلاصة من باب اليمين في الطلاق وقدمنا في أول الطهارة أنه سنة للرجال مكرمة للنساء إذ جماع المختونة ألذ قال الحلواني : كان النساء يختتن في زمن أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وفي النوازل أن ابن عباس كان لا يجيز شهادة الأقلف ولا ذبيحته، وعلماؤنا قالوا تؤكل ذبيحته وتقبل شهادته إن كان لعذر وإلا لا تقبل وبه نأخذ ا هـ . فائدة من كراهية فتاوى العتابي وقيل في ختان الكبير إذا أمكن أن يختن نفسه فعل وإلا لم يفعل إلا أن يمكنه أن يتزوج أو يشتري ختانة فتختنه . وذكر الكرخي في الكبير يختنه الحمامي وكذا عن ابن مقاتل لا بأس للحمامي أن يطلي عورة غيره بالنورة ا هـ قوله : (والخصي وولد الزنا والخنثى فإن عمر رضي الله عنه قبل شهادة علقمة الخصي ولأنه قطع عضو منه ظلماً فصار كما إذا قطعت يده والخصي بفتح الخاء على وزن فعيل منزوع البناية. وفسق الأبوين لا يوجب فسق الولد ككفرهما . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا شهد بالزنا أو بغيره خلافاً لمالك في الأول. والمراد بالخنثى المشكل وهو امرأة في الشهادة؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. قوله : (والعمال) أي تقبل شهادتهم، والمراد عمال السلطان عند عامة المشايخ لأن نفس العمل ليس بفسق إلا إذا كانوا أعواناً على الظلم. وقيل: العامل إذا كان وجيهاً في الناس ذا مروءة لا يجازف في كلامه تقبل شهادته كما مر عن أبي يوسف في الفاسق لوجاهته لا يقدم على الكذب كذا في الهداية. يعني ولو كان عوناً على الظلم كما في العناية . وقيل : أراد بالعمال الذين يعملون ويؤاجرون أنفسهم للعمل لأن من الناس من رد شهادات أهل الصناعات الخسيسة فأفرد هذه المسألة لإظهار مخالفتهم وكيف لا وكسبهم أطيب كسب. وينبغي تقييد القبول بأن تكون تلك الحرفة لائقة به بأن تكون حرفة آبائه وأجداده وإلا فلا مروءة له إذا كانت حرفة دنية فلا شهادة له لما عرف في حد العدالة . ينبغي تقييد القبول بأن لا يكثر الكذب والخلف في الوعد. وذكر الصدر الشهيد أن شهادة الرئيس لا تقبل وكذا الجابي والصراف الذي يجمع عنده الدراهم ويأخذها طوعاً لا تقبل. وقدمنا عن البزدوي أن القائم بتوزيع هذه النوائب السلطانية والجبابات بالعدل بين المسلمين وكذا قوله : ( وينبغي تقييد القبول الخ قال الرملي وعندي في هذا التقييد نظر يظهر لمن له نظر فتأمل اهـ . قلت : وجهه ما مر عند قوله أو يبول أو يأكل أن الصحيح قبول ذي الحرفة الدنية إذا كان عدلاً فحيث كان المعتبر العدالة فلا نظر إلى الحرفة نعم قد يقال عدوله عن حرفة آبائه الشريفة إلى الحرفة الخسيسة يدل على رذالته وعدم مروءته ومبالاته لكن هذا حيث كان بلا داع إليه من عجز أو عدم أسباب أو قله يد تقصره عن حرفة أبيه ولا سيما إذا كان أبوه أو وصيه علمه في صغره هذه الحرفة الدنية فكبر وهو لا يعرف غيرها، فإذا كان عدلاً فما وجه رد شهادته؟ فتعين ما قلنا تأمل وضمان مأجور وإن كان أصله ظلماً، فعلى هذا تقبل شهادته والمراد بالرئيس رئيس القرية وهو المسمى في بلادنا شيخ البلد، ومثله المعرفون في المراكب والعرفاء في جميع الأصناف الجهات في بلادنا لأنهم كلهم أعوان على الظلم ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي السراجية معزياً إلى الفقيه أبي الليث : إن كان العامل مثل عمر بن عبد العزير فشهادته جائزة، وإن كان مثل يزيد بن معاوية فلا ا هـ . وفي إطلاق العامل على الخليفة نظر والظاهر منه أنه من قبل عملاً من الخليفة. وفي شرح المنظومة : أمير كبير ادعى فشهد له عماله ودواوينه ونوابه ورعاياهم لا تقبل كشهادة المزارع لرب الأرض ا هـ. وفي إجارات البزازية لا تقبل شهادة الدلال ومحضر قضاة العهد والوكلاء المفتعلة والصكاك ا هـ . قوله : (والمعتق للمعتق أي تقبل شهادته كعكسه لأنه لا تهمة وقد قبل شريح شهادة قنبر لعلي رضي الله عنه وكان عتيقه وهو بفتح القاف والباء، وأما قنبر فهو جد سيبويه ذكره الذهبي في مشتبه الأسماء والأنساب وفي تقرير التهذيب للحافظ بن حجر : شريح بن الحادث بن قيس الكوفي النخعي القاضي أبو أمية ثقة وقيل له صحبة مات قبل الثمانين أو بعدها وله مائة وثماني سنين أو أكثر يقال حكم سبعين سنة ا هـ . قيدنا بعدم التهمة لأن العتيق لو كان متهماً لم تقبل لمن أعتقه ولذا قال في الخلاصة: ولو شهد العبدان بعد العتق على أن الثمن كذا عند اختلاف البائع والمشتري لا تقبل ا هـ . لأنهما يجران لأنفسهما نفعاً بإثبات العتق لأنه لولا شهادتهما لتحالفا وفسخ البيع المقتضي لإبطال العتق ولا يعارضه ما في الخلاصة أيضاً معزياً إلى العيون لو اشترى غلامين فأعتقهما فشهدا لمولاهما على البائع أنه قد استوفى الثمن جازت شهادتهما ا هـ . لأنهما لا يجران بها نفعاً ولا يدفعان مغرماً وشهادتهما بأن البائع أبرأ المشتري من الثمن كشهادتهما بالإيفاء كما في الخانية. وأشار إلى قبول شهادته على مولاه بالأولى إلا في مسألة ذكرناها عن الكافي عند قوله والمملوك والصبي» وذكر في المحيط البرهاني في مسألة المعتقين الثلاث هنا تركناها لكثرة شعبها. وفي العتابية: لو أعتق أم ولده فشهدت له في العدة تقبل ا هـ . وهي فعلى هذا يفرق بين المعتدة طلاق من ومن عتق قوله: (أمير كبير ادعى الخ) قال الرملي : يؤخذ منه أن شهادة خدامه الملازمين له ملازمة كملازمة العبد لمولاه كذلك لا تقبل وهو ظاهر ولا سيما في زماننا هذا تأمل. وقد أفتيت به مراراً والله تعالى الموفق للصواب ومثله في شهادات جامع الفتاوى بصيغة أعوان الحكام والوكلاء على باب القضاة لا تسمع شهادتهم لأنهم ساعون في إبطال حق المستحق وهم فساق والله تعالى أعلم قوله: (وفي إجارات البزازية الخ) قال الرملي محله في الكل ما لم يغلب عليهم الصلاح، أما إذا غلب عليهم الصلاح فتقبل كما صرح به في البزازية أيضاً في الصكاك في كتاب الشهادة، ولا فارق بينه وبين الدلال والمحضر والوكيل يدل عليه قوله في الوكلاء المفتعلة تأمل.
The Book of Testimonies: Chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. And the eunuch, the illegitimate child, the hermaphrodite, the workers, and the freed slave (testimony is accepted). And if he witnesses that his father bequeathed to him... and the text is transmitted and the later scholars estimated it and they differed, and the chosen opinion is that its first time is seven years and its last is twelve years; as in al-Khulasa from the chapter of oath in divorce. And we mentioned at the beginning of Taharah that it is a sunnah for men and a honor for women because intercourse with a circumcised woman is more pleasurable. Al-Halwani said: Women used to be circumcised in the time of the Companions of the Messenger of Allah. And in al-Nawazil that Ibn Abbas did not accept the testimony of the uncircumcised nor his slaughter, but our scholars said: His slaughter is eaten and his testimony is accepted if there is an excuse, otherwise not, and we take that. End quote. A benefit from the dislike fatwas of al-Atabi. And it was said regarding circumcision of an adult: if he can circumcise himself he does so, otherwise he does not unless he can marry or buy a circumciser to circumcise him. Al-Karkhi mentioned in al-Kabir: The bath attendant circumcises him, and similarly from Ibn Muqatil: There is no harm for the bath attendant to apply depilatory to another's private parts. End quote. His statement: (The eunuch, the illegitimate child, and the hermaphrodite): Because Umar accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch, and because it is a limb cut from him unjustly, so it is like when his hand is cut. The eunuch (al-khasi) is with fath of the kha on the pattern of fa'il, one whose testicles are removed. The sin of the parents does not necessitate the sin of the child, just as their disbelief does not. He made it general, so it includes when he testifies about zina or other, contrary to Malik in the first. And by 'hermaphrodite' is meant the ambiguous one, and he is a woman in testimony; as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His statement: (And the workers) i.e., their testimony is accepted, and what is meant by workers are the sultan's workers according to the general mashayikh, because the work itself is not fisq unless they are assistants in injustice. And it was said: If the worker is influential among people, having manliness, not reckless in his speech, his testimony is accepted, as mentioned from Abu Yusuf about the sinful due to his prestige, he does not advance to lying; as in al-Hidaya. Meaning even if he is an assistant in injustice, as in al-Inaya. And it was said: He meant by workers those who work and hire themselves out for work, because some people reject the testimonies of people of base professions, so he singled out this issue to show their opposition, and how not? For their earning is the purest earning. And it is appropriate to restrict acceptance to when that profession is suitable for him, such that it is the profession of his fathers and grandfathers; otherwise he has no manliness if he has a lowly profession, so he has no testimony based on what is known in the definition of probity. It is appropriate to restrict acceptance to when he does not lie frequently nor break promises. And al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned that the testimony of the headman is not accepted, and similarly the tax collector and the money changer who collects dirhams and takes them voluntarily is not accepted. And we mentioned earlier from al-Bazdawi that the one distributing these sultan's levies and taxes with justice among Muslims, similarly. His statement: (And it is appropriate to restrict acceptance, etc.) al-Ramli said: In my view, there is a problem with this restriction, apparent to one who reflects, so ponder. End quote. I said: Its justification is what passed at his statement 'or urinates or eats' that the correct view is acceptance of one of a lowly profession if he is just; since probity is the consideration, there is no regard to profession. Yes, it may be said that his deviating from his fathers' noble profession to a base profession indicates his vileness and lack of manliness and care, but this is when there is no motivation of incapacity, lack of means, or insufficient skill that prevents him from his father's profession, especially if his father or guardian taught him this base profession in his childhood and he grew up knowing only it. If he is just, what is the basis for rejecting his testimony? So our statement is determined, ponder. And the guarantee of a hired person even if its origin is unjust, so on this his testimony is accepted. And by 'headman' is meant the head of the village, called in our lands the shaykh of the town, and similarly the identifiers on ships and the foremen in all categories and areas in our lands, because they are all assistants in injustice; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Sirajiyya attributed to Abu al-Layth: If the worker is like Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, his testimony is permissible, but if he is like Yazid ibn Muawiya, then no. End quote. And applying the term 'worker' to the caliph is questionable, and the apparent is that he is one who undertook a work from the caliph. In Sharh al-Manzuma: A great amir claimed, and his workers, clerks, deputies, and subjects testified for him, it is not accepted, like the testimony of a farmer for the landowner. End quote. In Ijarat al-Bazzaziyya: The testimony of a broker, a presenter (mahdar) of judges of the era, fabricated agents, and document forgers is not accepted. End quote. His statement: (And the freed slave for his manumitter) i.e., his testimony is accepted, like the reverse, because there is no accusation (tuhma). Shuraih accepted the testimony of Qanbar for Ali, and he was his freed slave, and it is with fath of qaf and ba. As for Qanbar, he is the grandfather of Sibawayh, mentioned by al-Dhahabi in Mushaabbah al-Asma' wa al-Ansab. In Taqrir al-Tahdhib by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar: Shuraih ibn al-Harith ibn Qays al-Kufi al-Nakhai al-Qadi Abu Umayya is reliable, and it is said he had companionship (suhba), he died before eighty or after, and was one hundred and eight years old or more, and it is said he judged for seventy years. End quote. We restricted by 'no accusation' because if the freed slave were accused, his testimony for his manumitter would not be accepted. That is why it was said in al-Khulasa: If two slaves after manumission testify about the price being such when the seller and buyer differ, it is not accepted. End quote. Because they bring benefit to themselves by establishing the manumission, because without their testimony they would take oaths and the sale would be rescinded, which would necessitate nullification of the manumission. And it is not contradicted by what is in al-Khulasa also attributed to al-Uyun: If someone bought two slaves then manumitted them, and they testified for their master against the seller that he had received the price, their testimony is valid. End quote. Because they do not bring benefit nor repel harm by it. And their testimony that the seller discharged the buyer from the price is like their testimony of payment, as in al-Khaniyya. And he indicated the acceptance of his testimony against his master a fortiori, except for an issue we mentioned from al-Kafi at his statement 'and the slave and the child'. And al-Muhit al-Burhani mentioned an issue about three manumitted slaves here which we left due to its numerous branches. In al-Atabiyya: If a man manumits his umm walad and she testifies for him during her idda, it is accepted. End quote. So on this, a distinction is made between the woman in idda of divorce and the one manumitted. His statement: (A great amir claimed, etc.) al-Ramli said: From this it is taken that the testimony of his servants who are constantly with him like the constant companionship of a slave to his master is similarly not accepted, and it is apparent, especially in our time, ponder. And I have given fatwa on it repeatedly. And Allah the Exalted grants success to correctness. And similarly in Shahadat Jami' al-Fatawa: The testimony of assistants of judges and agents at the doors of judges is not heard because they are striving to nullify the right of the rightful, and they are sinful. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And in Ijarat al-Bazzaziyya, etc.) al-Ramli said: Its place in all is as long as righteousness does not prevail over them; but if righteousness prevails, then it is accepted as stated in al-Bazzaziyya also regarding document forgers in Kitab al-Shahada, and there is no difference between him and the broker, presenter, and agent; it is indicated by his statement about fabricated agents, ponder.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Raiq commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the acceptance of testimony from five categories: eunuchs, illegitimate children, hermaphrodites, workers, and freed slaves for their manumitters. The author provides proofs, conditions, and intra-Hanafi differences. For the eunuch, the proof is the practice of Caliph Umar accepting testimony of Alqamah the eunuch, and a qiyas: removing testicles is similar to cutting off a hand, which does not disqualify testimony. The ruling is general, including testimony about zina, contrary to Malik who disallows it in zina cases. For the illegitimate child, the reasoning is that the sin of parents does not affect the child's probity. For the hermaphrodite, it is defined as a person of ambiguous gender who is considered a woman in testimony. For workers, there is a major discussion: the majority of scholars consider them as sultan's workers, and they are not inherently sinful unless they assist in injustice. However, some differentiate based on prestige and manliness (muru'a). Al-Sadr al-Shahid and others reject testimony of headmen, tax collectors, and those who assist in injustice. Al-Ramli critiques the restriction of acceptance based on profession, arguing that if the person is just, his testimony should be accepted regardless of profession, though he acknowledges that deviation from noble profession may indicate lack of manliness if done willingly. For freed slaves, the ruling is that their testimony for their manumitter is accepted due to absence of accusation (tuhma), supported by the practice of Shuraih accepting testimony of Qanbar for Ali. Conditions are added: if the freed slaves could benefit themselves by testifying, e.g., establishing manumission to save a sale, their testimony is rejected. The passage concludes with fatwas from later scholars regarding the testimony of assistants of judges and brokers, emphasizing that they are generally not accepted unless righteousness dominates.

Key Terms
الخصي (al-khasi): A male whose testicles have been removed (eunuch).
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): A child born from unlawful intercourse.
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite of ambiguous gender; considered a woman in testimony.
العمال (al-ummāl): Workers, specifically those employed by the sultan or in various professions.
المعتق للمعتق (al-mu'tiq li'l-mu'taq): A freed slave testifying for the person who manumitted him.
المروءة (al-murū'a): Manliness, probity, social decorum – a quality required for witness competence.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Accusation or suspicion that the witness is biased or has a personal interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is the testimony of a sultan's worker accepted?
A) Only if he is from a noble family.
B) Only if he does not assist in injustice.
C) Only if he is the sultan himself.
D) Always accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is inclusive in accepting testimony from various categories, focusing on the individual's probity rather than external attributes.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
12 min
Testimony for Executor vs Agent: Qiyas and Istihsan in Hanafi Fiqh
Commentary on testimony rules with qiyas/istihsan and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of sons for a will vs agency, and explain the application of qiyas and istihsan in deriving the acceptance for the executor.

Core Idea
Qiyas rejects testimony for both; istihsan accepts for the executor because the judge's authority neutralizes self-interest.

In Hanafi law, two sons testifying that their father appointed someone as executor (wasiyy) is accepted, but their testimony for an agent (wakil) is not. This distinction is not arbitrary—it rests on a careful legal analysis using qiyas and istihsan. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the reasoning, including a critique from Fath al-Qadir and an intra-Hanafi dispute on a related case involving freed slaves. By understanding this ruling, you will see how Hanafi jurists balance analogy with juristic preference to achieve practical justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn states: testimony of two sons for a will is accepted if the executor claims; for an agency to collect debts, it is not accepted whether the agent claims or denies. Note the difference in outcome.
The executor must accept the role; mere testimony is not enough without his claim.
2
Examine the qiyas argument
By qiyas, both testimonies should be rejected because the sons bring benefit to themselves (jarr al-naf') by designating a person who will manage their father's estate or debts. This self-interest is the 'illa (effective cause) for rejection.
The qiyas panel in the toolbox shows the asl (agency) and far' (will) share the same 'illa.
3
Understand the istihsan override for the will
The judge has authority (wilayat al-nasb) to appoint an executor. The testimony only helps identify a suitable person; the judge's independent appointment removes the taint of self-interest. Death is a known fact, so the testimony is akin to a lottery (qur'a) that identifies a candidate.
This istihsan is based on necessity and the judge's role, not on a direct text.
4
Analyze the critique from Fath al-Qadir
Al-Marghinani argued that the ruling is actually consistent with qiyas because the testimony does not establish anything—the judge's appointment is the real basis. Thus, there is no need to invoke istihsan.
This internal debate shows that even within the Hanafi school, reasoning may be contested.
5
Apply the rule to related cases
The passage extends the rule: testimony of creditors, executors, and legatees about the will is accepted only if they claim. Also, testimony for agency is rejected absolutely because the judge cannot appoint an agent for a living principal (except in missing person cases).
The fifth scenario involves two executors already appointed; the judge may still accept testimony to replace them if they admit inability.

كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل
والوصي يدعى جاز وإن أنكر لا كما لو شهدا إن أباهما وكله بقبض ديونه وادعى الوكيل أو أنكر ولا يسمع القاضي الشهادة على الجرح ومن شهد ولم يبرح حتى قال وفيها : لو نفى ولد أم ولده ثم أعتقه فشهد له لم يجز، وسئل محمد عن عربي ادعى على رجل مولاه أعتقه فشهد موليان أعتقهما الرجل للمدعي لم تجز لأنهما يثبتان أن العربي مولى مولاهما. وقال أبو يوسف: يجوز كما لو شهد أن أباهما أعتق هذا والبنات يجحدون هذا أنه اهـ.
قوله : (ولو شهدا أن أباهما أوصى إليه والوصي يدعي جاز وإن أنكر لا كما لو شهدا أن أباهما وكله بقبض ديونه وادعى الوكيل أو أنكر) والقياس عدم القبول في الوصي أيضاً لكونها شهادة للشاهد للعود المنفعة إليه وجه الاستحسان أن للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصي إذا كان طالباً والموت معروف فيكفي القاضي بهذه الشهادة مؤنة التعيين لا أنه يثبت بها شيء فصار كالقرعة؛ كذا في الهداية. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بقوله : وإذا تحققت ما ذكر في وجه الاستحسان ظهر أن قبول الشهادة ثابت قياساً واستحساناً إذ ظهر أنه لم يثبت بها شيء وإنما ثبت عندها نصب القاضي وصياً اختاره وليس هنا موضع غير هذا يصرف إليه القياس والاستحسان، ولو اعتبرا في نفس إيصاء القاضي إليه فالقياس لا يأباه فلا وجه لجعل المشايخ فيها قياساً واستحساناً، والمنقول عن أصحاب المذهب الحكم المذكور مع السكوت عن القياس والاستحسان ا هـ . وقد ذكر القياس والاستحسان في عامة كتب أصحابنا، ومنهم شرح الجامع الصغير للحسامي والكافي والتبيين والهداية وشروحها والموضع الذي يصرفا إليه أن ظاهرها عدم القبول لأن الشاهد يجر نفعاً لنفسه فلا يكون المشهود له وصياً عن الميت، وفي الاستحسان جعلناه وصياً عن الميت ولم يعتبر نفع الشاهد لأن للقاضي ولاية النصب والسبب الحامل لاعتراض المحقق أنه أنه فهم من جهة القاضي وحينئذ فلا معنى للقياس والاستحسان وليس كذلك، وإنما هو وصي من جهة الميت، وقد كرنا في وصايا الفوائد من الأشباه والنظائر أن . القاضي كوصي الميت إلا في مسائل. وأشار بشهادة الابنين إلى أن شهادة الغريمين لهما على الميت دين أو للميت عليهما دين بأن الميت أوصى إلى فلان أو الوصيين بأن الميت أوصى إلى فلان معهما كذلك أو الموصى له بأن الميت أوصى إلى فلان ففي الخمس: إن ادعى قبلت وإلا لا. وأورد على الرابعة بأن الميت إذا كان له وصيان فالقاضي لا يحتاج إلى نصب آخر. وأجيب بأنه يملكه لإقرارهما بالعجز عن القيام بأمور

قول المصنف : والوصي يدعي قال في الحواشي :السعدية أي والوصي يرضى هكذا للبال. ثم رأيت في شرح الجامع الصغير لمولانا علاء الدين الأسود ما نصه: والمراد من الدعوى في قوله والوصي يدعي هو الرضا إذ الجوز لا يتوقف على الدعوى بل للقاضي أن : ينصب وصياً إذا رضي هو به اهـ قوله: (وليس كذلك وإنما هو وصي من جهة الميت لا يخفى أنه لا يوافق كلام
الميت، ولا بد من كون الموت معروفاً في الكل أي ظاهراً إلا في مسألة الغريمين للميت عليهما دين فإنها تقبل وإن لم يكن الموت معروفاً لأنهما يقران على أنفسهما بثبوت ولاية القبض للمشهود له فانتفت التهمة وثبت موت رب الدين بإقرارهما في حقهما . وقيل : معنى الثبوت أمر القاضي إياهما بأداء ما عليهما إليه لابراءتهما عن الدين بهذا الأداء لأن استيفاء الدين منهما حق عليهما فيقبل منهما والبراءة حق لهما فلا يقبل فيها؛ كذا في الكافي. وإنما لا تقبل شهادة الابنين في الوكالة مطلقاً لأنه ليس للقاضي ولاية نصب الوكيل عن الغائب إلا في المفقود فلو ثبتت هذه الولاية لكانت بشهادتهما وفيها تهمة (١) لأنهما يشهدان لأبيهما ولاحتمال التواضع على أخذ المال. وقوله بقبض ديونه اتفاقي لأنهما لو شهدا في غيبة أبيهما أنه وكله بالخصومة لم تقبل أيضاً كما في الخلاصة. وفرق بينهما في المحيط البرهاني من وجه آخر فقال : وإذا شهدا أن أباهما وكل هذا الرجل بقبض ديونه بالكوفة لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما بشهادتهما يعينان من يقوم بحقوق الأب واستيفائه فكانا شاهدين لأبيهما فلا تقبل شهادتهما، ولكن هذا إن كان المطلوب يجحد الوكالة فأما إذا أقر المطلوب به جازت هذه المسألة الشهادة. فرق بين مسألة ذكرها في كتاب الوكالة أن من وكل رجلاً بالخصومة في دار بعينها وقبضها وغاب فشهد ابنا الموكل أن أباهما وكل هذا الرجل بالخصومة هذه الدار وقبضها لا تقبل شهادتهما، سواء جحد المطلوب الوكالة أو أقر بها. ووجه الفرق أن في مسألة الدين المطلوب إذا كان مقراً بالوكالة يجبر على دفع المال بإقراره بدون الشهادة فإنما قامت الشهادة لإبراء المطلوب عند الدفع إلى الوكيل إذا حضر الطالب وأنكر الوكالة فكانت هذه الشهادة على أبيهما وشهادته على أبيه ،مقبولة، أما في مسألة كتاب الوكالة المطلوب وإن كان مقراً لا يجبر على دفع الدار إلى الوكيل بحكم إقراره وإنما يجبر عليه بالشهادة فكانت واقعة لأبيهما فلا تقبل ا.هـ. وبهذا ظهر أن المؤلف ترك قيداً . أن وهو المطلوب وأشار إلى عدم قبول شهادة ابني الوكيل مطلقاً بالأولى، وكذا شهادة أبويه وأجداده وأحفاده كما . في الخلاصة. وعلى هذا فالابنان في الكتاب مثال والمراد عدم قبولها في الوكالة من كل من لا تقبل شهادته للموكل وبه صرح في البزازية. ولم يقيد المصنف بغيبة الأب في شهادتهما بالوكالة لأنه لو كان حاضراً لا يمكن الدعوى بها ليشهد لأن التوكيل لا تسمع الدعوى به لأنه من العقود الجائزة لكن يحتاج إلى بيان صورة شهادتهما في غيبته مع جحد

الهداية الذي قصد الانتصار له من قوله أن للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصي وقوله فيكفي القاضي مؤنه التعيين، وكذا ما يأتي قريباً من قوله وأورد أنه إذا كان له وصيان فالقاضي لا يحتاج إلى نصب آخر فالحق ما فهمه المحقق من أن الوصي من جهة القاضي .
(۱) قوله لأنهما يشهدان لغاية قوله اتفاقي هو زائد في بعض النسخ فليتأمل فيه إهـ مصححه.
Book of Testimonies, Chapter: Whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. And the executor, if he claims, it is accepted; if he denies, it is not, unlike if the two (sons) testify that their father appointed him to collect his debts, and the agent claims or denies. And the judge does not hear testimony regarding discrediting (jarh), and whoever testified without leaving until he said: 'In it: if someone disowns the child of his umm walad, then frees him, so he testifies for him, it is not valid.' And Muhammad was asked about an Arab who claimed that a man was his freed slave, so the man freed him. Then two freed slaves whom the man had freed testified for the claimant: it is not valid because they confirm that the Arab is the patron of their patron. And Abu Yusuf said: it is valid, just as if two (sons) testify that their father freed this one, and the daughters deny this.' End. His statement: (And if they testify that their father bequeathed to him, and the executor claims, it is accepted; if he denies, it is not; similar to if they testify that their father appointed him to collect his debts, and the agent claims or denies). By analogy, non-acceptance would also apply to the executor because it is testimony for the witness bringing benefit to himself. The basis of istihsan is that the judge has authority to appoint an executor if he is eligible, and death is known, so the judge is satisfied by this testimony for the trouble of identification; it does not establish anything, so it becomes like a lottery. Thus in al-Hidayah. And [al-Marghinani] critiqued this in Fath al-Qadir saying: if you realize what is mentioned in the basis of istihsan, it appears that acceptance of testimony is established both by qiyas and istihsan, since it became clear that nothing is established by it; rather, at the time of it, the judge appoints an executor he chooses, and there is no other place to divert qiyas and istihsan. And if they consider it in the very appointment of the judge, then qiyas does not forbid it, so there is no reason for the scholars to consider it as qiyas and istihsan. What is transmitted from the followers of the madhhab is the mentioned ruling with silence about qiyas and istihsan. End. And qiyas and istihsan have been mentioned in most of the books of our scholars, including Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Hisami, al-Kafi, al-Tabyin, al-Hidayah and its commentaries. The place to divert them is that the apparent meaning is non-acceptance because the witness brings benefit to himself, so the one for whom he testifies is not an executor of the deceased. In istihsan, we make him an executor of the deceased and do not consider the benefit of the witness because the judge has authority of appointment. And the reason for the scholar's objection is that he understood from the aspect of the judge, and then there is no meaning to qiyas and istihsan. It is not so; rather, he is an executor from the aspect of the deceased. And we have repeated in Wasa'ya al-Fawa'id from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir that the judge is like the executor of the deceased except in some issues. And by the testimony of the two sons, he refers to the testimony of two creditors: either they have a debt against the deceased, or the deceased has a debt against them, or that the deceased bequeathed to so-and-so, or two executors that the deceased bequeathed to so-and-so along with them, similarly, or the legatee that the deceased bequeathed to so-and-so. In these five, if he claims, it is accepted; otherwise not. And an objection was raised on the fourth: if the deceased had two executors, the judge does not need another appointment. The answer is that he can appoint them because they admit inability to manage affairs. The author's statement: 'And the executor claims' – it is said in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya: meaning the executor accepts, thus for the mature. Then I saw in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by our master 'Ala' al-Din al-Aswad the text: what is meant by 'claim' in his statement 'and the executor claims' is acceptance, because permissibility is not dependent on claim; rather, the judge may appoint an executor if he accepts. End. His statement: (It is not so; rather, he is an executor from the aspect of the deceased) – it is not hidden that this does not agree with the statement of the deceased. And it is necessary that death be known in all, i.e., apparent, except in the issue of two creditors against whom the deceased had a debt, for it is accepted even if death is not known, because they affirm against themselves the establishment of the right of collection for the one for whom they testify, so suspicion is removed, and the death of the creditor is established by their admission against themselves. And it is said: meaning of establishment is the judge's order to them to pay what is due to him to discharge them from the debt by this payment, because collecting the debt from them is a right against them, so it is accepted from them, and discharge is a right for them, so it is not accepted. Thus in al-Kafi. And the testimony of the two sons regarding agency is absolutely not accepted because the judge has no authority to appoint an agent for an absent person except in the case of a lost person. If this authority were established, it would be by their testimony, and there is suspicion in it because they testify for their father and due to the possibility of collusion to take the property. And his statement 'to collect his debts' is incidental, because if they testify in the absence of their father that he appointed him for litigation, it would also not be accepted. As in al-Khulasa. And a distinction was made between them in al-Muhit al-Burhani from another aspect: if they testify that their father appointed this man to collect his debts in Kufa, their testimony is not accepted because by their testimony they specify who will perform the father's rights and collect them, so they are witnesses for their father, so their testimony is not accepted. But this is if the defendant denies the agency; if the defendant admits it, then the testimony is permitted. A distinction is made between an issue mentioned in the book of agency: if someone appoints a man for litigation over a specific house and its collection, and then goes away, and the two sons of the principal testify that their father appointed this man for litigation over this house and its collection, their testimony is not accepted, whether the defendant denies the agency or admits it. The aspect of difference is that in the debt issue, if the defendant admits the agency, he is compelled to pay the money by his admission without testimony; the testimony only serves to discharge the defendant when paying the agent if the claimant appears and denies the agency. So this testimony is against their father, and testimony against the father is accepted. In the issue from the book of agency, even if the defendant admits, he is not compelled to hand over the house to the agent by virtue of his admission; rather, he is compelled by testimony. So it is a testimony for their father, so it is not accepted. End. By this, it is clear that the author omitted a condition, that is the defendant. And he indicated non-acceptance of the testimony of the sons of the agent a fortiori, likewise testimony of his parents, grandparents, and grandchildren. As in al-Khulasa. On this basis, the two sons in the book are examples, and the intent is non-acceptance of testimony in agency from anyone whose testimony is not accepted for the principal. This is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya. And the author did not restrict to absence of the father in their testimony for agency because if he were present, the claim could not be made by it to testify, since agency is not heard by claim because it is a permissive contract. Rather, it needs to clarify the scenario of their testimony in his absence with denial. The Hidayah which he intended to support: from his statement that the judge has authority to appoint an executor, and his statement that the judge is satisfied by the trouble of identification. Similarly, what will soon come: his statement: 'And it was objected that if he has two executors, the judge does not need another appointment.' So the truth is what the scholar understood, that the executor is from the aspect of the judge. (Footnote: His statement 'because they testify for' up to his statement 'incidental' is extra in some copies, so ponder. End. The corrector.)
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expounding the rules of testimony in cases of wills and agency. The author first presents the matn: the testimony of two sons regarding their father's appointment of an executor is accepted if the executor claims (i.e., accepts the appointment), but not if he denies. In contrast, testimony regarding an agent (wakil) for collecting debts is not accepted regardless of claim or denial. The passage then includes three additional rulings: (1) a slave child of umm walad, if disowned and then freed, cannot testify for the father; (2) an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad reports that testimony of two freed slaves regarding the status of a third person as a master is not accepted, while Abu Yusuf holds it valid, analogizing to testimony of sons about their father's freeing; (3) a detailed discussion of the underlying reasoning using qiyas and istihsan. The commentary explains that by qiyas, testimony for an executor should also be rejected due to self-interest (jar al-naf'), but istihsan allows it because the judge has authority to appoint an executor. The death is a known fact, so the testimony only helps identify a suitable person, not establish a fact. This is likened to a lottery (qur'a). The commentator then reviews a critique from Fath al-Qadir arguing that the ruling is actually consistent with qiyas, not a departure. Further discussion covers the five scenarios of testimony by creditors/executors, the need for death to be known, and the distinction between cases where the defendant admits or denies, based on whether the testimony benefits the father (against him) or is for him. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the two sons are just an example; the rule applies to all relatives whose testimony would be rejected for the principal.

Key Terms
وصي (wasiyy): A person appointed by the deceased or the judge to execute the will and manage the estate.
وكيل (wakil): A person appointed by another (the principal) to act on their behalf, here specifically to collect debts or handle litigation.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that sets aside an analogy (qiyas) in favor of a different ruling due to necessity, custom, or a stronger textual indication.
جر النفع (jarr al-naf'): Bringing benefit to oneself, which is a reason to reject testimony due to self-interest.
ولاية النصب (wilayat al-nasb): The judge's authority to appoint an executor or guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the testimony of two sons for their father's will accepted, while for agency it is not?
A) Because the judge has authority to appoint an executor but not an agent for a living person.
B) Because the will produces more benefit to the sons than agency.
C) Because the death is unknown in agency cases.
D) Because agency is a binding contract.

Key Takeaway
Testimony for a will is accepted via istihsan due to the judge's authority to appoint an executor, while testimony for an agency is rejected by qiyas due to the witness's self-interest.

Shahadat — Testimony

8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Testimony of Freed Slaves
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony of freed slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the testimony of freed slaves regarding patronage, and apply the principle of jarr al-naf' to distinguish the two views.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf accepts testimony of freed slaves; Abu Hanifa rejects it due to direct self-interest.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq includes a famous intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (reporting Abu Hanifa) on the acceptance of testimony from two freed slaves who testify that a third person is the patron of their own patron. This case tests the limits of the jarr al-naf' (self-interest) principle. By studying this argument, you will see how Hanafi imams applied analogical reasoning differently to similar fact patterns.

Guided Path
1
Understand the factual scenario
An Arab claims that a man is his freed slave (mawla). That man had freed two slaves. Those two freed slaves now testify that the Arab is the patron (mawla) of their patron (i.e., the man who freed them). They are essentially testifying that the Arab is the ultimate master of their own master.
The witnesses are freed by the man, and they are affirming that the Arab freed that man, which indirectly establishes a chain of patronage benefiting their own patron.
2
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad (representing Abu Hanifa's view) says the testimony is not accepted. The reason: the witnesses confirm that the Arab is the patron of their patron, so they are testifying for their own patron, bringing benefit to him (jarr al-naf').
This is a stricter application of the self-interest principle.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf says the testimony is accepted. He analogizes to the case of two sons testifying that their father freed someone: even if the daughters deny, the sons' testimony is accepted despite potential benefit to themselves.
Abu Yusuf sees the benefit as too indirect to reject the testimony.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The passage does not explicitly endorse either view, but the majority Hanafi position (as transmitted by Muhammad) seems more cautious. The response to Abu Yusuf is that in the sons' case, the father's death is known and the benefit is indirect, whereas here, the freed slaves are directly affirming the lineage of their own patron.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear: in a court case, the testimony would be accepted or rejected depending on which imam's view is followed.
5
Relate to the main ruling
This dispute is embedded within the larger discussion of will vs agency. Both cases revolve around the principle of jarr al-naf'. The issue of freed slaves is a separate application of the same underlying concern.
Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of how Hanafi scholars interpret self-interest in testimony.

كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل
والوصي يدعى جاز وإن أنكر لا كما لو شهدا إن أباهما وكله بقبض ديونه وادعى الوكيل أو أنكر ولا يسمع القاضي الشهادة على الجرح ومن شهد ولم يبرح حتى قال وفيها : لو نفى ولد أم ولده ثم أعتقه فشهد له لم يجز، وسئل محمد عن عربي ادعى على رجل مولاه أعتقه فشهد موليان أعتقهما الرجل للمدعي لم تجز لأنهما يثبتان أن العربي مولى مولاهما. وقال أبو يوسف: يجوز كما لو شهد أن أباهما أعتق هذا والبنات يجحدون هذا أنه اهـ.
قوله : (ولو شهدا أن أباهما أوصى إليه والوصي يدعي جاز وإن أنكر لا كما لو شهدا أن أباهما وكله بقبض ديونه وادعى الوكيل أو أنكر) والقياس عدم القبول في الوصي أيضاً لكونها شهادة للشاهد للعود المنفعة إليه وجه الاستحسان أن للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصي إذا كان طالباً والموت معروف فيكفي القاضي بهذه الشهادة مؤنة التعيين لا أنه يثبت بها شيء فصار كالقرعة؛ كذا في الهداية. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بقوله : وإذا تحققت ما ذكر في وجه الاستحسان ظهر أن قبول الشهادة ثابت قياساً واستحساناً إذ ظهر أنه لم يثبت بها شيء وإنما ثبت عندها نصب القاضي وصياً اختاره وليس هنا موضع غير هذا يصرف إليه القياس والاستحسان، ولو اعتبرا في نفس إيصاء القاضي إليه فالقياس لا يأباه فلا وجه لجعل المشايخ فيها قياساً واستحساناً، والمنقول عن أصحاب المذهب الحكم المذكور مع السكوت عن القياس والاستحسان ا هـ . وقد ذكر القياس والاستحسان في عامة كتب أصحابنا، ومنهم شرح الجامع الصغير للحسامي والكافي والتبيين والهداية وشروحها والموضع الذي يصرفا إليه أن ظاهرها عدم القبول لأن الشاهد يجر نفعاً لنفسه فلا يكون المشهود له وصياً عن الميت، وفي الاستحسان جعلناه وصياً عن الميت ولم يعتبر نفع الشاهد لأن للقاضي ولاية النصب والسبب الحامل لاعتراض المحقق أنه أنه فهم من جهة القاضي وحينئذ فلا معنى للقياس والاستحسان وليس كذلك، وإنما هو وصي من جهة الميت، وقد كرنا في وصايا الفوائد من الأشباه والنظائر أن . القاضي كوصي الميت إلا في مسائل. وأشار بشهادة الابنين إلى أن شهادة الغريمين لهما على الميت دين أو للميت عليهما دين بأن الميت أوصى إلى فلان أو الوصيين بأن الميت أوصى إلى فلان معهما كذلك أو الموصى له بأن الميت أوصى إلى فلان ففي الخمس: إن ادعى قبلت وإلا لا. وأورد على الرابعة بأن الميت إذا كان له وصيان فالقاضي لا يحتاج إلى نصب آخر. وأجيب بأنه يملكه لإقرارهما بالعجز عن القيام بأمور

أباهما وكل هذا الرجل بقبض ديونه بالكوفة لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما بشهادتهما يعينان من يقوم بحقوق الأب واستيفائه فكانا شاهدين لأبيهما فلا تقبل شهادتهما، ولكن هذا إن كان المطلوب يجحد الوكالة فأما إذا أقر المطلوب به جازت هذه المسألة الشهادة. فرق بين مسألة ذكرها في كتاب الوكالة أن من وكل رجلاً بالخصومة في دار بعينها وقبضها وغاب فشهد ابنا الموكل أن أباهما وكل هذا الرجل بالخصومة هذه الدار وقبضها لا تقبل شهادتهما، سواء جحد المطلوب الوكالة أو أقر بها. ووجه الفرق أن في مسألة الدين المطلوب إذا كان مقراً بالوكالة يجبر على دفع المال بإقراره بدون الشهادة فإنما قامت الشهادة لإبراء المطلوب عند الدفع إلى الوكيل إذا حضر الطالب وأنكر الوكالة فكانت هذه الشهادة على أبيهما وشهادته على أبيه ،مقبولة، أما في مسألة كتاب الوكالة المطلوب وإن كان مقراً لا يجبر على دفع الدار إلى الوكيل بحكم إقراره وإنما يجبر عليه بالشهادة فكانت واقعة لأبيهما فلا تقبل ا.هـ. وبهذا ظهر أن المؤلف ترك قيداً . أن وهو المطلوب وأشار إلى عدم قبول شهادة ابني الوكيل مطلقاً بالأولى، وكذا شهادة أبويه وأجداده وأحفاده كما . في الخلاصة. وعلى هذا فالابنان في الكتاب مثال والمراد عدم قبولها في الوكالة من كل من لا تقبل شهادته للموكل وبه صرح في البزازية. ولم يقيد المصنف بغيبة الأب في شهادتهما بالوكالة لأنه لو كان حاضراً لا يمكن الدعوى بها ليشهد لأن التوكيل لا تسمع الدعوى به لأنه من العقود الجائزة لكن يحتاج إلى بيان صورة شهادتهما في غيبته مع جحد

الهداية الذي قصد الانتصار له من قوله أن للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصي وقوله فيكفي القاضي مؤنه التعيين، وكذا ما يأتي قريباً من قوله وأورد أنه إذا كان له وصيان فالقاضي لا يحتاج إلى نصب آخر فالحق ما فهمه المحقق من أن الوصي من جهة القاضي .
(۱) قوله لأنهما يشهدان لغاية قوله اتفاقي هو زائد في بعض النسخ فليتأمل فيه إهـ مصححه.
Book of Testimonies, Chapter: Whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. And the executor, if he claims, it is accepted; if he denies, it is not, unlike if the two (sons) testify that their father appointed him to collect his debts, and the agent claims or denies. And the judge does not hear testimony regarding discrediting (jarh), and whoever testified without leaving until he said: 'In it: if someone disowns the child of his umm walad, then frees him, so he testifies for him, it is not valid.' And Muhammad was asked about an Arab who claimed that a man was his freed slave, so the man freed him. Then two freed slaves whom the man had freed testified for the claimant: it is not valid because they confirm that the Arab is the patron of their patron. And Abu Yusuf said: it is valid, just as if two (sons) testify that their father freed this one, and the daughters deny this.' End. His statement: (And if they testify that their father bequeathed to him, and the executor claims, it is accepted; if he denies, it is not; similar to if they testify that their father appointed him to collect his debts, and the agent claims or denies). By analogy, non-acceptance would also apply to the executor because it is testimony for the witness bringing benefit to himself. The basis of istihsan is that the judge has authority to appoint an executor if he is eligible, and death is known, so the judge is satisfied by this testimony for the trouble of identification; it does not establish anything, so it becomes like a lottery. Thus in al-Hidayah. And [al-Marghinani] critiqued this in Fath al-Qadir saying: if you realize what is mentioned in the basis of istihsan, it appears that acceptance of testimony is established both by qiyas and istihsan, since it became clear that nothing is established by it; rather, at the time of it, the judge appoints an executor he chooses, and there is no other place to divert qiyas and istihsan. And if they consider it in the very appointment of the judge, then qiyas does not forbid it, so there is no reason for the scholars to consider it as qiyas and istihsan. What is transmitted from the followers of the madhhab is the mentioned ruling with silence about qiyas and istihsan. End. And qiyas and istihsan have been mentioned in most of the books of our scholars, including Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Hisami, al-Kafi, al-Tabyin, al-Hidayah and its commentaries. The place to divert them is that the apparent meaning is non-acceptance because the witness brings benefit to himself, so the one for whom he testifies is not an executor of the deceased. In istihsan, we make him an executor of the deceased and do not consider the benefit of the witness because the judge has authority of appointment. And the reason for the scholar's objection is that he understood from the aspect of the judge, and then there is no meaning to qiyas and istihsan. It is not so; rather, he is an executor from the aspect of the deceased. And we have repeated in Wasa'ya al-Fawa'id from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir that the judge is like the executor of the deceased except in some issues. And by the testimony of the two sons, he refers to the testimony of two creditors: either they have a debt against the deceased, or the deceased has a debt against them, or that the deceased bequeathed to so-and-so, or two executors that the deceased bequeathed to so-and-so along with them, similarly, or the legatee that the deceased bequeathed to so-and-so. In these five, if he claims, it is accepted; otherwise not. And an objection was raised on the fourth: if the deceased had two executors, the judge does not need another appointment. The answer is that he can appoint them because they admit inability to manage affairs. The author's statement: 'And the executor claims' – it is said in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya: meaning the executor accepts, thus for the mature. Then I saw in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by our master 'Ala' al-Din al-Aswad the text: what is meant by 'claim' in his statement 'and the executor claims' is acceptance, because permissibility is not dependent on claim; rather, the judge may appoint an executor if he accepts. End. His statement: (It is not so; rather, he is an executor from the aspect of the deceased) – it is not hidden that this does not agree with the statement of the deceased. And it is necessary that death be known in all, i.e., apparent, except in the issue of two creditors against whom the deceased had a debt, for it is accepted even if death is not known, because they affirm against themselves the establishment of the right of collection for the one for whom they testify, so suspicion is removed, and the death of the creditor is established by their admission against themselves. And it is said: meaning of establishment is the judge's order to them to pay what is due to him to discharge them from the debt by this payment, because collecting the debt from them is a right against them, so it is accepted from them, and discharge is a right for them, so it is not accepted. Thus in al-Kafi. And the testimony of the two sons regarding agency is absolutely not accepted because the judge has no authority to appoint an agent for an absent person except in the case of a lost person. If this authority were established, it would be by their testimony, and there is suspicion in it because they testify for their father and due to the possibility of collusion to take the property. And his statement 'to collect his debts' is incidental, because if they testify in the absence of their father that he appointed him for litigation, it would also not be accepted. As in al-Khulasa. And a distinction was made between them in al-Muhit al-Burhani from another aspect: if they testify that their father appointed this man to collect his debts in Kufa, their testimony is not accepted because by their testimony they specify who will perform the father's rights and collect them, so they are witnesses for their father, so their testimony is not accepted. But this is if the defendant denies the agency; if the defendant admits it, then the testimony is permitted. A distinction is made between an issue mentioned in the book of agency: if someone appoints a man for litigation over a specific house and its collection, and then goes away, and the two sons of the principal testify that their father appointed this man for litigation over this house and its collection, their testimony is not accepted, whether the defendant denies the agency or admits it. The aspect of difference is that in the debt issue, if the defendant admits the agency, he is compelled to pay the money by his admission without testimony; the testimony only serves to discharge the defendant when paying the agent if the claimant appears and denies the agency. So this testimony is against their father, and testimony against the father is accepted. In the issue from the book of agency, even if the defendant admits, he is not compelled to hand over the house to the agent by virtue of his admission; rather, he is compelled by testimony. So it is a testimony for their father, so it is not accepted. End. By this, it is clear that the author omitted a condition, that is the defendant. And he indicated non-acceptance of the testimony of the sons of the agent a fortiori, likewise testimony of his parents, grandparents, and grandchildren. As in al-Khulasa. On this basis, the two sons in the book are examples, and the intent is non-acceptance of testimony in agency from anyone whose testimony is not accepted for the principal. This is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya. And the author did not restrict to absence of the father in their testimony for agency because if he were present, the claim could not be made by it to testify, since agency is not heard by claim because it is a permissive contract. Rather, it needs to clarify the scenario of their testimony in his absence with denial. The Hidayah which he intended to support: from his statement that the judge has authority to appoint an executor, and his statement that the judge is satisfied by the trouble of identification. Similarly, what will soon come: his statement: 'And it was objected that if he has two executors, the judge does not need another appointment.' So the truth is what the scholar understood, that the executor is from the aspect of the judge. (Footnote: His statement 'because they testify for' up to his statement 'incidental' is extra in some copies, so ponder. End. The corrector.)
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expounding the rules of testimony in cases of wills and agency. The author first presents the matn: the testimony of two sons regarding their father's appointment of an executor is accepted if the executor claims (i.e., accepts the appointment), but not if he denies. In contrast, testimony regarding an agent (wakil) for collecting debts is not accepted regardless of claim or denial. The passage then includes three additional rulings: (1) a slave child of umm walad, if disowned and then freed, cannot testify for the father; (2) an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad reports that testimony of two freed slaves regarding the status of a third person as a master is not accepted, while Abu Yusuf holds it valid, analogizing to testimony of sons about their father's freeing; (3) a detailed discussion of the underlying reasoning using qiyas and istihsan. The commentary explains that by qiyas, testimony for an executor should also be rejected due to self-interest (jar al-naf'), but istihsan allows it because the judge has authority to appoint an executor. The death is a known fact, so the testimony only helps identify a suitable person, not establish a fact. This is likened to a lottery (qur'a). The commentator then reviews a critique from Fath al-Qadir arguing that the ruling is actually consistent with qiyas, not a departure. Further discussion covers the five scenarios of testimony by creditors/executors, the need for death to be known, and the distinction between cases where the defendant admits or denies, based on whether the testimony benefits the father (against him) or is for him. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the two sons are just an example; the rule applies to all relatives whose testimony would be rejected for the principal.

Key Terms
مولى (mawla): Patron or freed slave; can refer to the master who frees a slave or the freed person. Context determines meaning.
جر النفع (jarr al-naf'): Bringing benefit to oneself, which is a reason to reject testimony due to self-interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Muhammad (reporting Abu Hanifa) reject the testimony of two freed slaves regarding another person's patronage?
A) Because the witnesses are not reliable.
B) Because the witnesses confirm that the Arab is the patron of their own patron, bringing benefit to themselves.
C) Because the witnesses are slaves and their testimony is never accepted.
D) Because the Arab did not present any other evidence.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa (via Muhammad) rejects the testimony of freed slaves due to indirect self-interest; Abu Yusuf accepts it by analogy to sons' testimony about their father's freeing.

Shahadat — Testimony

General Rule: Agent's Testimony Requires Prior Litigation
General rule and illustrative example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that an agent's testimony is not accepted without prior litigation and explain the deposit example given in the text.

Core Idea
An agent's testimony is only valid after litigation; the agent is not compelled to act except for deposit returns.

This lesson introduces the foundational principle that an agent (wakil) cannot testify in a matter unless litigation (da'wa) has already occurred. The author illustrates this with an example involving a deposit, and explains why the agent is not compelled to perform his agency except in specific cases like returning a deposit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule about agent's testimony
The author states that an agent's testimony is not heard except after litigation. This means the witness must have been involved in a lawsuit related to the matter.
2
Analyze the deposit example
The example: owner of a deposit claims delivery; agent denies; witnesses testify to delivery and also to collection of debts. The author notes that the agent is not compelled to perform except in returning deposits.
The testimony about debt collection is problematic because there was no litigation.
3
Understand the rationale
The agent's testimony is linked to the litigation because otherwise the testimony would be based on hearsay or self-interest. The marginal note clarifies the wording and the issue with the debt part.
Reflect on the commentator's note: why is the testimony about debt collection problematic?

كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل
الوكيل لأنها لا تسمع إلا بعد الدعوى، ولم يظهر هنا لها وجه ويمكن أن تصور بأن يدعي صاحب وديعة عليه تسليم وديعته الموكل في دفعها فيجحد فيشهدان به ويقبض ديون أبيهما، وإنما صورناه بذلك لأن الوكيل لا يجبر على فعل ما وكل به إلا في رد الوديعة ونحوها كما سيأتي فيه .
فروع: شهد الوصي بعد العزل للميت إن خاصم لا تقبل وإلا تقبل، ولو وكله بالخصومة عند القاضي فخاصم المطلوب بألف درهم عند القاضي ثم أخرجه الموكل عنها فشهد الوكيل أن للموكل على المطلوب مائة دينار تقبل، ولو وكله عند غير القاضي فأشهد على الوكالة فخاصم المطلوب بألف درهم وبرهن على الوكالة ثم عزله الموكل منها فشهد له على المطلوب بمائة دينار مما كان له عليه بعد القضاء بالوكالة لا تقبل؛ كذا في البزازية . ثم قال : وأما شهادة الوصي بحق للميت على غيره بعد ما أخرجه القاضي عن الوصاية قبل الخصومة أو بعدها لا تقبل وكذا لو شهد الوصي بحق للميت بعد ما أدركت الورثة لا تقبل، ودلت المسألة على أن القاضي إذا عزل الوصي ينعزل، ولو شهد لبعض الورثة على الميت إن كان المشهود له صغيراً لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وإن كان بالغاً فكذلك عنده، وعندهما يجوز. ولو شهد لكبير على أجنبي تقبل في ظاهر الرواية ولو شهد للوارث الكبير والصغير في غير ميراث لم تقبل، ولو شهد الوصيان على إقرار الميت بشيء معين لوارث بالغ تقبل ا هـ. وفيها أيضاً : ادعى داراً وبرهن وأبطل القاضي ببينة ثم جاء بعد ثلاثين سنة فشهدا أنها لآخر لا تقبل، وكذا لو قال هذه الدار لفلان لا حق لي فيها ثم شهد أنها لفلان آخر لا تقبل ا هـ . وفي العتابية : شهدا أن الميت أوصى لهما ولهذا تقبل في حق هذا ويضم إليه آخران اهـ. وفيها : ادعى الوكيل بالخصومة ديناً بحضرة الموكل فادعى المدعى عليه قضاءه فشهد الوكيل بذلك لا تسمع لأن دعواه أبطل شهادته، وكذا وكيلها ادعى المهر على الزوج لا تقبل شهادته للزوج بالخلع .
قوله : (تسليم وديعته الموكل في دفعها أي التي وكله الغائب بدفعها لصاحب وقوله «فيشهدان به أي بتسليم الوديعة الذي ادعاه المدعي، وقوله وبقبض ديون أبيهما» لم تجر فيه الدعوى فما شهادتهما به مع أن المقصود جريانها فيه من إجبار الوكيل ولا إجبار هنا فتأمل.
معنی
Book of Testimonies, Chapter: Whose Testimony is Accepted and Whose is Not. The agent because it is not heard except after litigation, and here there is no face for it. It can be pictured by the owner of a deposit claiming against him the delivery of his deposit which the absentee appointed him to deliver, so he denies, so they testify to it and collect the debts of their father. We only pictured it like that because the agent is not compelled to do what he is appointed for except in the return of the deposit and the like, as will come. Branches: If the executor testifies after removal for the deceased, if he litigates, it is not accepted; otherwise it is accepted. If he appointed him for litigation before the judge, and he litigated the defendant for a thousand dirhams before the judge, then the principal removed him from it, then the agent testified that the principal has against the defendant a hundred dinars, it is accepted. If he appointed him before a non-judge, and he took witnesses on the agency, and litigated the defendant for a thousand dirhams and proved the agency, then the principal removed him from it, and he testified for him against the defendant for a hundred dinars that he owed him after the judgment on the agency, it is not accepted; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Then he said: As for the testimony of the executor regarding a right of the deceased against others after the judge removed him from executorship, before or after litigation, it is not accepted. Similarly, if the executor testifies regarding a right of the deceased after the heirs have reached majority, it is not accepted. The issue indicates that if the judge removes the executor, he is removed. If he testifies for some of the heirs against the deceased: if the beneficiary is a minor, it is not allowed by agreement; if he is an adult, similarly according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them (the two disciples) it is allowed. If he testifies for an adult against a stranger, it is accepted in the apparent narration. If he testifies for an adult and minor heir in non-inheritance matters, it is not accepted. If the two executors testify about the deceased's acknowledgment of a specific thing for an adult heir, it is accepted, end. Also in it: He claimed a house and produced evidence, and the judge invalidated it with evidence, then after thirty years they came and testified that it belongs to another, not accepted. Similarly, if he said this house is for so-and-so, I have no right in it, then testified that it is for another, not accepted, end. In al-Utabiyya: They testified that the deceased bequeathed to them and to this, so it is accepted regarding this one, and two others are added to him, end. In it: If the agent in litigation claimed a debt in the presence of the principal, and the defendant claimed payment, and the agent testified to that, it is not heard because his claim invalidated his testimony. Similarly, if her agent claimed the dower against the husband, his testimony for the husband regarding khul' is not accepted. His statement: (Delivery of his deposit which the absentee appointed him to deliver) i.e. which the absentee appointed him to deliver to its owner. And his statement 'so they testify to it' i.e. to the delivery of the deposit which the plaintiff claimed. And his statement 'and collect the debts of their father' – there was no litigation in it, so what is their testimony with it? While the purpose is that litigation should occur in it to compel the agent, and there is no compulsion here, so reflect. Meaning.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on testimony discusses the acceptance of testimony given by an agent (wakil) and an executor (wasi). The author begins by explaining that an agent's testimony is generally not heard until after litigation (da'wa) has occurred. He gives an example: the owner of a deposit claims that the agent appointed by an absentee to deliver the deposit has not done so; the agent denies, and witnesses testify that the agent did deliver the deposit and also collected debts of the absentee. The author notes that the agent is not compelled to perform his agency except in returning a deposit and similar matters, as will be detailed later. Then a series of branches (furu') are presented: 

1. If an executor testifies after being removed from executorship by the judge, his testimony regarding the deceased is not accepted if he litigates; if he does not litigate, it is accepted. 
2. If a principal appoints an agent for litigation before a judge, the agent litigates, then the principal revokes the agency, after which the agent testifies that the principal has a debt against the defendant, such testimony is accepted. 
3. But if the appointment was made before a non-judge and the agent proved his agency, then was removed, his testimony for the principal about a debt that was due after the judgment on the agency is not accepted. 
4. An executor's testimony for the deceased after removal by the judge is not accepted, whether before or after litigation. Similarly, if the executor testifies after the heirs have gained majority, it is not accepted. 
5. If an executor testifies for some heirs against the deceased, it is not allowed if the beneficiary is a minor (by consensus). If the beneficiary is an adult, Abu Hanifa also says it is not allowed, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is allowed. 
6. If the executor testifies for an adult heir against a stranger, it is accepted in the apparent narration. 
7. Testimony for both adult and minor heirs in non-inheritance matters is not accepted. 
8. If two executors testify about the deceased's acknowledgment (iqrar) of a specific thing to an adult heir, it is accepted. 
9. Other branches: If someone claims a house, proves it, and the judge invalidates the evidence, then after thirty years two witnesses testify it belongs to another, not accepted. Similarly, if someone says 'this house is for so-and-so, I have no right' then later testifies it is for another, not accepted. 
10. In al-Utabiyya: Two testify that the deceased bequeathed to them and to a third person; the testimony is accepted only for the testators themselves, and two others must be added for the third. 
11. If an agent in litigation claims a debt in the presence of the principal, and the defendant claims to have paid, and the agent testifies to the payment, it is not heard because his own claim invalidates his testimony. Similarly, if the wife's agent claims the dower from the husband, his testimony for the husband regarding khul' is not accepted. 

Lastly, a marginal note explains the phrase 'delivery of his deposit' and clarifies that the witnesses here testify to the delivery and to the collection of debts, but since there was no litigation regarding the debt collection, the testimony about that part may be problematic because the purpose was to have litigation to compel the agent, but here there is no compulsion. The commentator asks the reader to reflect.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by another (the principal) to perform a specific task, such as litigation or delivery of property.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court to establish a fact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is an agent's testimony accepted?
A) Always
B) Only after litigation
C) Only if the agent is also a heir
D) Only if the principal is present

Key Takeaway
An agent's testimony is only valid after litigation; without it, the testimony is not heard.

Shahadat — Testimony

Branches on Executor's (Wasi) Testimony
Branches on executor's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings on an executor's testimony after removal, before/after litigation, and for various heirs, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples.

Core Idea
An executor's testimony is affected by his removal, the heir's age, and whether the testimony is for or against the deceased.

This lesson covers several branches (furu') regarding the testimony of an executor (wasi). The rulings depend on when the testimony is given (before or after removal from executorship), the age of the heir, and whether the testimony is for the deceased or against him. A key internal dispute exists between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding testimony for an adult heir against the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings on executor's testimony after removal
If the executor testifies after the judge has removed him, his testimony is not accepted if he litigates; if he does not litigate, it is accepted. Also, if he testifies after removal regarding a right of the deceased, it is not accepted.
Removal by the judge terminates the executor's capacity.
2
Understand the ruling for testimony for heirs against the deceased
If the heir is a minor, testimony is not allowed by consensus. If the heir is an adult, Abu Hanifa says it is not allowed, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it.
This is the main dispute.
3
Examine testimony for an adult heir against a stranger
In the apparent narration, the executor's testimony for an adult heir against a stranger is accepted.
4
Consider testimony for both adult and minor in non-inheritance matters
Such testimony is not accepted.
5
Analyze the case of two executors testifying about the deceased's acknowledgment
If two executors testify that the deceased acknowledged a specific thing for an adult heir, it is accepted.
