كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل
الوكيل لأنها لا تسمع إلا بعد الدعوى، ولم يظهر هنا لها وجه ويمكن أن تصور بأن يدعي صاحب وديعة عليه تسليم وديعته الموكل في دفعها فيجحد فيشهدان به ويقبض ديون أبيهما، وإنما صورناه بذلك لأن الوكيل لا يجبر على فعل ما وكل به إلا في رد الوديعة ونحوها كما سيأتي فيه .
فروع: شهد الوصي بعد العزل للميت إن خاصم لا تقبل وإلا تقبل، ولو وكله بالخصومة عند القاضي فخاصم المطلوب بألف درهم عند القاضي ثم أخرجه الموكل عنها فشهد الوكيل أن للموكل على المطلوب مائة دينار تقبل، ولو وكله عند غير القاضي فأشهد على الوكالة فخاصم المطلوب بألف درهم وبرهن على الوكالة ثم عزله الموكل منها فشهد له على المطلوب بمائة دينار مما كان له عليه بعد القضاء بالوكالة لا تقبل؛ كذا في البزازية . ثم قال : وأما شهادة الوصي بحق للميت على غيره بعد ما أخرجه القاضي عن الوصاية قبل الخصومة أو بعدها لا تقبل وكذا لو شهد الوصي بحق للميت بعد ما أدركت الورثة لا تقبل، ودلت المسألة على أن القاضي إذا عزل الوصي ينعزل، ولو شهد لبعض الورثة على الميت إن كان المشهود له صغيراً لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وإن كان بالغاً فكذلك عنده، وعندهما يجوز. ولو شهد لكبير على أجنبي تقبل في ظاهر الرواية ولو شهد للوارث الكبير والصغير في غير ميراث لم تقبل، ولو شهد الوصيان على إقرار الميت بشيء معين لوارث بالغ تقبل ا هـ. وفيها أيضاً : ادعى داراً وبرهن وأبطل القاضي ببينة ثم جاء بعد ثلاثين سنة فشهدا أنها لآخر لا تقبل، وكذا لو قال هذه الدار لفلان لا حق لي فيها ثم شهد أنها لفلان آخر لا تقبل ا هـ . وفي العتابية : شهدا أن الميت أوصى لهما ولهذا تقبل في حق هذا ويضم إليه آخران اهـ. وفيها : ادعى الوكيل بالخصومة ديناً بحضرة الموكل فادعى المدعى عليه قضاءه فشهد الوكيل بذلك لا تسمع لأن دعواه أبطل شهادته، وكذا وكيلها ادعى المهر على الزوج لا تقبل شهادته للزوج بالخلع .
قوله : (تسليم وديعته الموكل في دفعها أي التي وكله الغائب بدفعها لصاحب وقوله «فيشهدان به أي بتسليم الوديعة الذي ادعاه المدعي، وقوله وبقبض ديون أبيهما» لم تجر فيه الدعوى فما شهادتهما به مع أن المقصود جريانها فيه من إجبار الوكيل ولا إجبار هنا فتأمل.
معنی
Book of Testimonies, Chapter: Whose Testimony is Accepted and Whose is Not. The agent because it is not heard except after litigation, and here there is no face for it. It can be pictured by the owner of a deposit claiming against him the delivery of his deposit which the absentee appointed him to deliver, so he denies, so they testify to it and collect the debts of their father. We only pictured it like that because the agent is not compelled to do what he is appointed for except in the return of the deposit and the like, as will come. Branches: If the executor testifies after removal for the deceased, if he litigates, it is not accepted; otherwise it is accepted. If he appointed him for litigation before the judge, and he litigated the defendant for a thousand dirhams before the judge, then the principal removed him from it, then the agent testified that the principal has against the defendant a hundred dinars, it is accepted. If he appointed him before a non-judge, and he took witnesses on the agency, and litigated the defendant for a thousand dirhams and proved the agency, then the principal removed him from it, and he testified for him against the defendant for a hundred dinars that he owed him after the judgment on the agency, it is not accepted; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Then he said: As for the testimony of the executor regarding a right of the deceased against others after the judge removed him from executorship, before or after litigation, it is not accepted. Similarly, if the executor testifies regarding a right of the deceased after the heirs have reached majority, it is not accepted. The issue indicates that if the judge removes the executor, he is removed. If he testifies for some of the heirs against the deceased: if the beneficiary is a minor, it is not allowed by agreement; if he is an adult, similarly according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them (the two disciples) it is allowed. If he testifies for an adult against a stranger, it is accepted in the apparent narration. If he testifies for an adult and minor heir in non-inheritance matters, it is not accepted. If the two executors testify about the deceased's acknowledgment of a specific thing for an adult heir, it is accepted, end. Also in it: He claimed a house and produced evidence, and the judge invalidated it with evidence, then after thirty years they came and testified that it belongs to another, not accepted. Similarly, if he said this house is for so-and-so, I have no right in it, then testified that it is for another, not accepted, end. In al-Utabiyya: They testified that the deceased bequeathed to them and to this, so it is accepted regarding this one, and two others are added to him, end. In it: If the agent in litigation claimed a debt in the presence of the principal, and the defendant claimed payment, and the agent testified to that, it is not heard because his claim invalidated his testimony. Similarly, if her agent claimed the dower against the husband, his testimony for the husband regarding khul' is not accepted. His statement: (Delivery of his deposit which the absentee appointed him to deliver) i.e. which the absentee appointed him to deliver to its owner. And his statement 'so they testify to it' i.e. to the delivery of the deposit which the plaintiff claimed. And his statement 'and collect the debts of their father' – there was no litigation in it, so what is their testimony with it? While the purpose is that litigation should occur in it to compel the agent, and there is no compulsion here, so reflect. Meaning.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on testimony discusses the acceptance of testimony given by an agent (wakil) and an executor (wasi). The author begins by explaining that an agent's testimony is generally not heard until after litigation (da'wa) has occurred. He gives an example: the owner of a deposit claims that the agent appointed by an absentee to deliver the deposit has not done so; the agent denies, and witnesses testify that the agent did deliver the deposit and also collected debts of the absentee. The author notes that the agent is not compelled to perform his agency except in returning a deposit and similar matters, as will be detailed later. Then a series of branches (furu') are presented: 

1. If an executor testifies after being removed from executorship by the judge, his testimony regarding the deceased is not accepted if he litigates; if he does not litigate, it is accepted. 
2. If a principal appoints an agent for litigation before a judge, the agent litigates, then the principal revokes the agency, after which the agent testifies that the principal has a debt against the defendant, such testimony is accepted. 
3. But if the appointment was made before a non-judge and the agent proved his agency, then was removed, his testimony for the principal about a debt that was due after the judgment on the agency is not accepted. 
4. An executor's testimony for the deceased after removal by the judge is not accepted, whether before or after litigation. Similarly, if the executor testifies after the heirs have gained majority, it is not accepted. 
5. If an executor testifies for some heirs against the deceased, it is not allowed if the beneficiary is a minor (by consensus). If the beneficiary is an adult, Abu Hanifa also says it is not allowed, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is allowed. 
6. If the executor testifies for an adult heir against a stranger, it is accepted in the apparent narration. 
7. Testimony for both adult and minor heirs in non-inheritance matters is not accepted. 
8. If two executors testify about the deceased's acknowledgment (iqrar) of a specific thing to an adult heir, it is accepted. 
9. Other branches: If someone claims a house, proves it, and the judge invalidates the evidence, then after thirty years two witnesses testify it belongs to another, not accepted. Similarly, if someone says 'this house is for so-and-so, I have no right' then later testifies it is for another, not accepted. 
10. In al-Utabiyya: Two testify that the deceased bequeathed to them and to a third person; the testimony is accepted only for the testators themselves, and two others must be added for the third. 
11. If an agent in litigation claims a debt in the presence of the principal, and the defendant claims to have paid, and the agent testifies to the payment, it is not heard because his own claim invalidates his testimony. Similarly, if the wife's agent claims the dower from the husband, his testimony for the husband regarding khul' is not accepted. 

Lastly, a marginal note explains the phrase 'delivery of his deposit' and clarifies that the witnesses here testify to the delivery and to the collection of debts, but since there was no litigation regarding the debt collection, the testimony about that part may be problematic because the purpose was to have litigation to compel the agent, but here there is no compulsion. The commentator asks the reader to reflect.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): An executor appointed by the deceased or by the judge to manage the deceased's estate and handle affairs for minor heirs.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court to establish a fact.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's position on an executor testifying for an adult heir against the deceased?
A) The testimony is accepted.
B) The testimony is not accepted.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the executor is also an heir.
D) The testimony is accepted only if the heir is a minor.

Key Takeaway
An executor's testimony is subject to many conditions, with a key internal dispute regarding testimony for adult heirs against the deceased.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Additional Branches: Contradictory Claims and Other Rulings
Additional branches on testimony, bequest, and contradictory claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings from additional branches, including cases of contradictory claims, bequest testimony, and agent's self-contradicting testimony.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected if it contradicts a prior claim or if the witness has previously disclaimed interest.

This lesson covers several miscellaneous branches (furu') from al-Bazzaziyya and al-Utabiyya. These include cases where a person claims a house then later testifies it belongs to another, testimony about bequests, and an agent's testimony that contradicts his own prior claim. Each ruling reinforces the principle that consistency and lack of self-interest are crucial for valid testimony.

Guided Path
1
Understand the house claim scenario
If someone claims a house and produces evidence, and the judge invalidates that evidence, then after thirty years two witnesses testify that the house belongs to another, their testimony is not accepted. Similarly, if someone says 'this house is for so-and-so, I have no right in it' then later testifies it is for another, not accepted.
These cases show that testimony contradicting a prior claim or admission is rejected.
2
Analyze the bequest testimony
Two witnesses testify that the deceased bequeathed to them and to a third person. The testimony is accepted only for the testators themselves; two additional witnesses are needed for the third person.
This relates to the rule that testimony for one's own benefit is sometimes restricted.
3
Examine the agent's contradictory testimony
If an agent appointed for litigation claims a debt in the presence of the principal, and the defendant claims payment, and the agent testifies to that payment, the testimony is not heard because his own claim invalidates his testimony. Similarly, if a wife's agent claims the dower from the husband, his testimony for the husband regarding khul' is not accepted.
An agent's testimony cannot contradict his own prior claim.

Source Text

كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل
الوكيل لأنها لا تسمع إلا بعد الدعوى، ولم يظهر هنا لها وجه ويمكن أن تصور بأن يدعي صاحب وديعة عليه تسليم وديعته الموكل في دفعها فيجحد فيشهدان به ويقبض ديون أبيهما، وإنما صورناه بذلك لأن الوكيل لا يجبر على فعل ما وكل به إلا في رد الوديعة ونحوها كما سيأتي فيه .

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by another (the principal) to perform a specific task, such as litigation or delivery of property.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually the dower or some property).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the testimony of two witnesses who claim the deceased bequeathed to them and to a third person?
A) The testimony is accepted for all three.
B) The testimony is accepted only for the two witnesses themselves, and two more witnesses are needed for the third.
C) The testimony is rejected entirely because it is self-serving.
D) The testimony is accepted only if the third person is also a witness.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected if it contradicts a prior claim or admission, or if it benefits the witness without additional corroboration.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

The Ruling on Testimony Based on Discrediting (Jarh) Witnesses
Definition and ruling on testimony regarding discrediting of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between pure jarh (jarh mujarrad) and non-pure jarh (ghayr mujarrad) and state the Hanafi ruling on each.

Core Idea
Pure discrediting is rejected; non-pure discrediting that also establishes a right is accepted.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines jarh and its two types. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines whether testimony discrediting a witness is admissible in court. The Hanafi school carefully balances the prohibition of spreading obscenity with the need to uphold rights.

Guided Path
1
Define jarh linguistically and terminologically
Jarh literally means to wound or defame. In legal terminology, it is revealing a witness's transgression (fisq).
The term comes from al-Misbah.
2
Identify the two types: mujarrad and ghayr mujarrad
Pure jarh does not involve establishing any right; non-pure jarh does involve establishing a right of Allah or humans.
3
Understand the ruling and reasons for rejecting pure jarh
Pure jarh is not accepted because it falls outside judicial enforcement and involves spreading obscenity without necessity.
The witness giving such testimony becomes a transgressor himself.
4
Recognize exceptions and the acceptance of non-pure jarh
Testimony on confession (iqrar) is accepted because it is enforceable. Non-pure jarh is accepted when needed to uphold rights.
Also, if the defendant has a direct financial interest, it becomes non-pure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يسمع القاضي الشهادة على الجرح وهو بفتح الجيم لغة من جرحه بلسانه جرحاً عابه ونقصه ومنه جرحت الشاهد إذا أظهرت فيه ما ترد به شهادته؛ كذا في المصباح. وفي الاصطلاح : إظهار فسق الشاهد فإن لم يتضمن ذلك إثبات حق الله تعالى أو للعبد فهو جرح مجرد، وإن تضمن إثبات حق الله تعالى أو للعبد فهو غير مجرد. والأول هو المراد من إطلاقه كما أفصح به في الكافي، وهو غير مقبول مثل أن يشهدوا أن شهود المدعي فسقة أو زناة أو أكلة الربا أو شربة اخمر أو على إقرارهم أنهم شهدوا بالزور أو على إقرارهم أنهم أجراء في هذه الشهادة أو على إقرارهم أن المدعي مبطل في هذه الدعوى أو على إقرارهم أنهم لا شهادة لهم على المدعى عليه في هذه الحادثة. وإنما لم تقبل لأن البينة إنما تقبل على ما يدخل تحت الحكم وفي وسع القاضي إلزامه والفسق مما لا يدخل تحت الحكم وليس في وسع القاضي إلزامه لأنه يدفعه بالتوبة ولأن الشاهد بهذه الشهادة صار فاسقاً لأن فيها إشاعة الفاحشة بلا ضرورة وهي حرام بالنص والمشهود به لا يثبت بشهادة الفاسق، ولا يقال إن فيه ضرورة وهي كف الظالم عن الظلم بأداء الشهادة الكاذبة وقال عليه السلام «انصر أخاك ظالماً أو مظلوماً» لأنا نقول لا ضرورة إلى هذه الشهادة على ملأ من الناس ويمكنه كفه عن الظلم بإخبار القاضي بذلك سراً إلا إذا شهدوا على إقرار المدعي أنهم فسقة أو شهدوا بزور أو نحوه لأنهم ما شهدوا بإظهار الفاحشة وإنما حكوا إظهارها عن غيرهم فلا يصيرون فسقة بذلك. وكذا الإقرار مما يدخل تحت الحكم ويقدر القاضي على الإلزام لأنه لا يرتفع بالتوبة، ولذا لو أقام المدعى عليه البينة أن المدعي استأجرهم لأداء الشهادة لم تقبل لأنه شهادة على جرح مجرد. وأما الاستئجار وإن كان أمراً زائداً على الجرح ولكنه لا خصم في إثباته إذ لا تعلق له بالأجرة حتى لو أقام المدعى عليه البينة أن المدعي استأجر الشهود بعشرة دراهم لأداء الشهادة وأعطاهم العشرة من مالي الذي كان في يده تقبل لأنه خصم في ذلك ويثبت الجرح بناء عليه. وكذا إذا أقام المدعى عليه البينة على أني صالحت الشهود على كذا من المال ودفعته اليهم على أن لا يشهدوا علي بهذا الباطل، فإن شهدوا فعليهم أن يردوا ذلك المال علي تقبل بينته لأن فيه ضرورة ليصل إلى ماله حتى لو قال لم أعطهم المال لم تقبل لأن فيه إظهار من غير ضرورة وأما الثاني أعني غير المجرد فهو كما لو أقام المدعى عليه البينة أنهم زنوا ووصفوا الزنا أو شربوا الخمر أو سرقوا مني كذا ولم يتقادم العهد أو أنهم عبيد أو أحدهم عبد أو شريك المدعي والمدعى مال أو قاذف والمقذوف يدعيه أو محدودون في القذف أو على إقرار المدعي أنه استأجرهم على هذه الشهادة تقبل لمكان الحاجة إلى إحياء هذه الحقوق وفيها : إذا شهدوا أنهم محدودون في قذف ليس فيه إشاعة الفاحشة لأن الإظهار حصل بالقضاء وإنما حكوا عن إظهار الفاحشة عن الغير ؛ كذا في الكافي بتمامه .
His statement: (The judge does not hear testimony regarding discrediting (jarh), and jarh with a fatha on the jim is linguistically from 'he wounded him with his tongue, wounding, defaming and diminishing him', and from it is 'I discredited the witness' when you reveal in him something that rejects his testimony; thus in al-Misbah. In terminology: it is the revealing of the witness's transgression (fisq). If it does not include establishing a right of Allah (ta'ala) or of a human, then it is pure discrediting (jarh mujarrad). If it includes establishing a right of Allah or of a human, then it is non-pure (ghayr mujarrad). The first is what is meant by its absolute usage, as clarified in al-Kafi, and it is not acceptable. Examples: that they testify that the plaintiff's witnesses are transgressors, or fornicators, or eaters of riba, or drinkers of wine, or that they confessed that they gave false testimony, or that they confessed that they were hired for this testimony, or that they confessed that the plaintiff is false in this claim, or that they confessed that they have no testimony against the defendant in this incident. The reason it is not accepted is that evidence is only accepted for what falls under judicial decree and within the judge's capacity to enforce, and transgression (fisq) does not fall under judicial decree and is not within the judge's capacity to enforce because it can be removed by repentance. Also because the witness giving such testimony becomes a transgressor himself, since it involves spreading obscenity (ifshā' al-fāḥisha) without necessity, which is forbidden by scripture, and what is testified to is not established by the testimony of a transgressor. It cannot be said that there is a necessity here, namely to prevent the oppressor from oppression by giving false testimony, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Support your brother whether he is an oppressor or oppressed.' We say: there is no necessity for this testimony in public; he can prevent him from oppression by informing the judge privately. Except if they testify about the plaintiff's confession that they are transgressors, or that they testified falsely, or the like, because they are not testifying by spreading obscenity; they are merely reporting the spreading of obscenity by others, so they do not become transgressors thereby. Similarly, confession (iqrar) falls under judicial decree and the judge can enforce it because it is not removed by repentance. Hence, if the defendant produces evidence that the plaintiff hired them to give testimony, it is not accepted because it is testimony on pure discrediting. As for hiring, although it is something additional to discrediting, there is no opponent in establishing it since it has no connection to the fee. So if the defendant produces evidence that the plaintiff hired the witnesses for ten dirhams to give testimony and gave them the ten from his property which was in the defendant's possession, it is accepted because he is an opponent in that and discrediting is established based on it. Similarly, if the defendant produces evidence that 'I settled with the witnesses for such and such property and gave it to them on condition that they do not testify against me in this false matter, and if they testify they must return that money to me', his evidence is accepted because there is a necessity to recover his property. Unless he says 'I did not give them the money', then it is not accepted because it is a revelation without necessity. As for the second, i.e., non-pure (ghayr mujarrad), it is like if the defendant produces evidence that they committed zina and describes the zina, or drank wine, or stole from me such-and-such without the lapse of time, or that they are slaves or one of them is a slave, or that they are a partner of the plaintiff and the plaintiff has money, or that they are a slanderer and the slandered person claims it, or that they are flogged for slander, or about the plaintiff's confession that he hired them for this testimony, it is accepted due to the need to revive these rights. In it: if they testify that they are flogged for slander, there is no spreading of obscenity because the revelation occurred through the judgment, and they are merely reporting the revelation of obscenity from someone else; thus in al-Kafi in full.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed definition and ruling on testimony regarding the discrediting (jarh) of witnesses. The commentator begins by defining jarh linguistically and terminologically. In legal terminology, jarh is the act of revealing a witness's transgression (fisq). The key distinction is between two types: pure jarh (jarh mujarrad) and non-pure jarh (ghayr mujarrad). Pure jarh does not involve establishing any right of Allah or of a human; it merely accuses a witness of fisq, such as testifying that the plaintiff's witnesses are fornicators, drunkards, or that they confessed to false testimony, etc. Such testimony is not accepted by the judge. The reason given is that evidence is only accepted for matters that are subject to judicial enforcement (taht al-hukm), and fisq is not subject to enforcement because it can be removed by repentance. Moreover, the act of testifying to such fisq itself constitutes spreading obscenity (ifshā' al-fāḥisha) without necessity, which is prohibited. The witness giving such discrediting testimony thus becomes a transgressor himself, and his testimony is therefore rejected. This is in accordance with the hadith 'Support your brother, oppressor or oppressed,' but the commentator clarifies that there is no necessity to spread this in public; one can inform the judge privately. However, an exception is made when the testimony is based on a confession (iqrar) by the plaintiff himself that his witnesses are transgressors or that they gave false testimony, because then the testifier is simply reporting the confession, not engaging in spreading obscenity themselves. Confession is also subject to judicial enforcement because it cannot be repented of (i.e., it has legal effect). The passage then covers further nuances: If the defendant brings evidence that the plaintiff hired witnesses to testify, this is still pure jarh because the hiring itself is not a matter that the defendant is directly opposing (no khasm). But if the defendant brings evidence that the plaintiff hired witnesses and paid the fee from property that was in the defendant's hand, then it is accepted because the defendant is an opponent in that financial claim. Similarly, if the defendant brings evidence that he settled with the witnesses (paid them to not testify), his evidence is accepted because there is a necessity to recover his money. However, if he merely claims he gave money without evidence, it is not accepted. The second type, non-pure jarh, involves evidence that also establishes a right (like proving theft, zina, or that a witness is a slave). This is accepted because it serves the need to uphold rights. The passage concludes with an example: testifying that witnesses have been flogged for slander is not spreading obscenity because the flogging was a judicial act; they are just reporting it. All this is from al-Kafi.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): To discredit a witness by revealing their transgression (fisq) to reject their testimony.
جرح مجرد (jarh mujarrad): Pure discrediting that does not involve establishing any right of Allah or humans.
جرح غير مجرد (jarh ghayr mujarrad): Non-pure discrediting that involves establishing a right (e.g., proving zina, theft, slavery).
إشاعة الفاحشة (ishā'at al-fāḥisha): Spreading obscenity or scandal, which is prohibited without necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is testimony on pure discrediting (jarh mujarrad) not accepted according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it involves spreading obscenity without necessity and the witness becomes a transgressor.
B) Because it is not based on personal knowledge.
C) Because it contradicts the statement of the plaintiff.
D) Because it requires two witnesses and they must be men.

Key Takeaway
Testimony discrediting a witness is only accepted in Hanafi law if it also serves to establish a right of Allah or of a human.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Accepting Jarh Mujarrad Before vs. After Tazkiyah
Analyzes the timing and acceptance of jarh mujarrad in testimony law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the acceptance of jarh mujarrad before tazkiyah (as a defense) from after tazkiyah (as a removal) and apply the Hanafi principle that defense is easier than removal.

Core Idea
Jarh mujarrad is accepted before tazkiyah as a defense, but not after tazkiyah—because defense is easier than removal.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a subtle but crucial point in the law of testimony: when can a mere accusation (jarh mujarrad) disqualify a witness? The Hanafi school distinguishes between discrediting a witness before their uprightness is established (tazkiyah) and after. The key is whether the discrediting serves as a defense (daf') against accepting unverified testimony or as a removal (raf') of already accepted testimony. This distinction turns on a well-known usul principle: defense is easier than removal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage focuses on the timing of accepting jarh mujarrad: before or after tazkiyah (formal attestation of uprightness). Understand that jarh mujarrad is a discrediting statement without a specific legal claim.
Jarh ghayr mujarrad (with details) is always accepted if proven.
2
Distinguish between defense (daf') and removal (raf')
Before tazkiyah, testimony is not yet fixed; jarh prevents acceptance (defense). After tazkiyah, testimony is fixed; jarh would overturn it (removal). The principle: daf' is easier than raf'.
This principle is from Hanafi usul.
3
State the two opposing positions within the Hanafi school
Some scholars (based on Sharh al-Wiqayah) hold that jarh mujarrad is never accepted. Others (Ibn al-Kamal, al-Durar) differentiate timing. The passage resolves that it is accepted before tazkiyah as a defense.
Ibn al-Humam and Mulla Khusraw supported the differentiated view.
4
Apply the principle of daf' easier than raf'
Since before tazkiyah testimony is unestablished, a single report of fisq suffices to prevent acceptance (daf'). After tazkiyah, removal requires full proof and witness count.
This explains why one reporter is enough before, but not after.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a single person reports fisq before tazkiyah, the judge will not accept the witness's testimony until tazkiyah. After tazkiyah, one report will not disqualify the witness; full proof is needed.
This contrasts with the view that jarh mujarrad is never effective.

وهنا تنبيهات مهمة يجب التنبيه عليها : الأول أن النظر في الجرح المجرد وغيره إنما هو بعد التزكية الشرعية كما في السراج الوهاج، فإذا سأل القاضي عن الشهود سراً وعلناً وثبت عنده عدالتهم فطعن الخصم فإن كان مجرداً لم تقبل وإلا قبل ولكن عدم قبول الشهادة على الجرح المجرد أعم من أن يكون قبل التعديل أو بعده. فإن قلت: أليس الخبر عن فسق الشهود قبل إقامة البيئة على عدالتهم يمنع القاضي عن قبول شهادتهم والحكم بها؟ قلت : نعم لكن ذلك للطعن في عدالتهم لا لثبوت أمر يسقطهم عن حيز القبول ولذا لو عدلوا بعد هذا تقبل شهادتهم، ولو كانت الشهادة على فسقهم مقبولة لسقطوا عن حيز الشهادة ولم يبق لهم مجال التعديل؛ ذكره ابن الكمال. وفي شرح الوقاية : لا تقبل الشهادة على الجرح المجرد إذا أقام البينة على العدالة، أما إذا لم يقم البينة عليها فأخبر مخبر أن الشهود فساق أو أكلوا الربا فإن الحكم لا يجوز قبل ثبوت العدالة لا سيما إذا أخبر مخبران أن الشهود فساق . الثاني أن

الإمام لأنه ليس من باب سماع الشهادة على الجرح المجرد تأمل قوله : (ولكن عدم القبول الخ) أتى بالاستدراك لأن الكلام السابق محتمل لقبول الجرح المجرد قبل التعديل كقبول غير المجرد ومحتمل لعدم قبوله تأمل قوله: (وفي شرح الوقاية لا تقبل الشهادة الخ) هذا غير مخالف لما قاله ابن الكمال لأن إخبار المخبر للطعن لا لإثبات الفسق كما قاله وقال في الدرر بعد نقله كلام صدر الشريعة أقول : تحقيقه أن جرح الشاهد قبل التعديل دفع للشهادة قبل ثبوتها وهي من باب الديانات ولهذا قبل فيه خبر الواحد، وبعد التعديل دفع للشهادة بعد ثبوتها حتى وجب على القاضي العمل بها إن لم يوجد الجرح المعتبر، ومن القواعد المقررة أن الدفع أسهل من الرفع وهو السر في كون الجرح المجرد مقبولاً قبل التعديل ولو من واحد، وغير مقبول بعده بل يحتاج إلى نصاب الشهادة وإثبات حق الشرع أو العبد فاضمحل بهذا التحقيق ما اعترض عليه بعض المتصلفين بلا شعور على مراد القائل ومع ذاهل عن القواعد وغافل حيث قال أقول : فيه نظر إذ الفرض أن مثل هذه الشهادة لا تعتبر، سواء كان قبل تعديل الشهود أو بعده، فلا حاجة إلى ما ذكره من الصورة المقيدة اهـ. والمراد بالصورة المقيدة قوله إذا أقام البينة على العدالة وفي العزمية : وقد يقال إنما لا تقبل البينة على الجرح المجرد لأنه لا يدخل تحت الحكم والبيئة إنما تقبل على ما يدخل تحت الحكم وفي وسع القاضي إلزامه، وهذا لا يختلف بكونه قبل إقامة البينة على العدالة وكونه .بعدها وبالجملة ينبغي أن يطالب صدر الشريعة فيما ادعاه بالنقل فليتدبر .اهـ. وفي شرح القهستاني : وفيه أي في كلام صدر الشريعة أن مراد الفقهاء أن القاضي لا يلتفت إلى هذه الشهادة ولكن يسأل عن شهود المدعي سراً وعلانية، فإذا ثبت عدالتهم تقبل كما في المضمرات .اهـ. أقول : وأنت إذا حققت النظر يظهر لك المخالفة كلامهم جميعاً فكلام السراج محتمل لقبولها على المجرد قبل التعديل نعم ظاهره عدم القبول والمراد به أنها لا تثبت أمراً يسقطهم عن حيز القبول، أما ثبوت الطعن بها وعدم الحكم بشهادة المجروحين ما لم يعدلوا فلا كلام فيه، وهذا ما قاله صدر الشريعة في شرح الوقاية وهو ما حققه ملاخسر، وأيضاً من

168. Book of Testimonies, Chapter: Whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. And here are important notes that must be attended to: First, that consideration of jarh mujarrad and others is only after legal tazkiyah (attestation of uprightness), as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. So when the judge inquires about the witnesses secretly and openly, and their uprightness is established, then if the opponent discredits, if it is jarh mujarrad it is not accepted; otherwise it is accepted. But the non-acceptance of testimony on jarh mujarrad is general, whether before or after ta'dil. If you say: does not the report of the witnesses' sin before evidence of their uprightness prevent the judge from accepting their testimony and judging by it? I say: Yes, but that is for challenging their uprightness, not for establishing a matter that removes them from the realm of acceptance. Hence if they are later declared upright, their testimony is accepted. If the testimony on their sin were acceptable, they would be removed from the realm of testimony and would have no room for ta'dil. Mentioned by Ibn al-Kamal. And in Sharh al-Wiqayah: Testimony on jarh mujarrad is not accepted if evidence of uprightness has been presented. But if evidence of uprightness has not been presented, and a reporter reports that the witnesses are sinners or are usurers, then judgment is not valid before establishing uprightness, especially if two reporters report that the witnesses are sinners. Second, that... the imam because it is not from the chapter of hearing testimony on jarh mujarrad. Reflect on his statement: 'But non-acceptance, etc.' He made an exception because the previous speech may imply acceptance of jarh mujarrad before ta'dil like acceptance of non-mere, or may imply non-acceptance. Reflect on his statement: 'And in Sharh al-Wiqayah: testimony on jarh mujarrad is not accepted...' This does not contradict Ibn al-Kamal's statement because the reporter's information is for challenging, not for establishing sin. And he said in al-Durar after quoting the speech of Sadr al-Shari'a: I say: Its verification is that jarh of a witness before ta'dil is a defense of testimony before its establishment, and it is from the category of beliefs, hence it accepts the report of a single person. After ta'dil, it is a removal of testimony after its establishment, so the judge must act on it if no valid jarh exists. From established principles, defense is easier than removal, and this is the secret of why jarh mujarrad is accepted before ta'dil even from one person, but not accepted after it; rather, it requires the full number of witnesses and proof of a right of God or of a person. With this verification, the objection of some affected persons who lack understanding of the speaker's intention, oblivious to principles and heedless, collapses – where he said: I say: There is consideration; the assumption is that such testimony is not considered, whether before or after ta'dil of witnesses, so there is no need for the restricted qualification mentioned. End. The restricted qualification is his statement: 'if evidence of uprightness is presented.' And in al-Azmjiyya: It may be said that evidence on jarh mujarrad is not accepted because it does not fall under the judge's authority, and evidence is only accepted on what falls under the judge's authority and is in his power to enforce; this does not differ whether it is before presenting evidence of uprightness or after. In summary, Sadr al-Shari'a should be asked about what he claims based on transmission; so ponder. End. And in Sharh al-Qahistani: In it, i.e., in the speech of Sadr al-Shari'a, that the intent of the jurists is that the judge does not pay attention to this testimony, but he asks about the witnesses of the plaintiff secretly and openly; if their uprightness is established, their testimony is accepted, as in al-Mudmarat. End. I say: When you investigate, you will see a contradiction among all their statements. The statement of al-Siraj is probably acceptance of jarh mujarrad before ta'dil; indeed, its apparent meaning is non-acceptance, and what is meant is that it does not establish a matter that removes them from the realm of acceptance. As for the establishment of challenge and the prevention of ruling based on the testimony of the discredited witnesses until they are declared upright, there is no debate. This is what Sadr al-Shari'a said in Sharh al-Wiqayah, and it is what is verified by Mulla Khusraw. Also, from... non-... between
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage contains important notes (tanbihat) on the timing of considering jarh (discrediting witnesses). The first note states that jarh, both mere and non-mere, is considered only after legal tazkiyah (attestation of uprightness), as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The judge first inquires about the witnesses' uprightness; if they are upright, then the opponent's discrediting is considered. If it is jarh mujarrad, it is not accepted; otherwise, it is accepted. However, the non-acceptance of jarh mujarrad applies both before and after ta'dil (modification). A question arises: does not a report of the witnesses' sin before evidence of their uprightness prevent the judge from accepting their testimony? The answer is yes, but that is for challenging their uprightness, not for establishing a matter that removes them from acceptance permanently. If they are later declared upright, their testimony is accepted again. Ibn al-Kamal explains that if testimony on sin were acceptable, they would be permanently disqualified. Then a statement from Sharh al-Wiqayah is cited: jarh mujarrad is not accepted if evidence of uprightness has been presented; but if not, a report of sin prevents judgment until tazkiyah, especially from two reporters. The second note discusses the imam's view, clarifying that the earlier expression 'but non-acceptance' is an exception because the previous context might imply acceptance of jarh mujarrad before ta'dil. The author of al-Durar provides a verification: jarh before ta'dil is a defense (daf') before testimony is established, so it is accepted from a single person; after ta'dil, it is a removal (raf') after testimony is established, so it requires a full number of witnesses and proof of a right. This is based on the principle that defense is easier than removal. This refutes an objection that jarh mujarrad is never considered. The passage concludes by noting that different scholars' statements should be harmonized; the intent is that before tazkiyah, jarh mujarrad is accepted as a defense, but after tazkiyah it is not accepted because it does not fall under the judge's authority.

Key Terms
التزكية الشرعية (al-tazkiyah al-shar'iyyah): The legal attestation of a witness's uprightness ('adalah) by the judge through inquiry and established evidence.
الجرح المجرد (al-jarh al-mujarrad): A discrediting statement that merely accuses a witness of sin without a specific legal claim that can be enforced.
الدفع والرفع (al-daf' wa al-raf'): Daf' (defense) prevents the establishment of testimony; raf' (removal) overturns already established testimony. The principle: daf' is easier than raf'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the resolved position in this passage, when is jarh mujarrad accepted from a single reporter?
A) Only after tazkiyah
B) Neither before nor after tazkiyah
C) Only before tazkiyah
D) It is accepted only from two reporters

Key Takeaway
Jarh mujarrad is accepted before tazkiyah as a defense (daf') from a single reporter, but after tazkiyah it is not accepted and requires full proof for removal.
